    1

    《冥祥记》[南朝齐]王琰
    　　
    　　　自序

    Explanation

    1

    Preface

    Records of the Supernatural [Southern Qi] Wang Yan

    This translation maintains the formal tone of the original text while providing clear context for the reader. The title "冥祥记" is rendered as "Records of the Supernatural" to convey the genre of the text, and the author and dynasty are transliterated as "Wang Yan" and "Southern Qi," respectively. The opening line "自序" is translated as "Preface" to indicate the introductory nature of the text.

    2

    琰稚年在交阯。彼土有贤法师者，道德僧也。见授五戒，以观世音金像一躯，见与供养；形制异今，又非甚古，类元嘉中作。镕镌殊工，似有真好。琰奉以还都。时年在龆龀，与二弟常尽勤至，专精不倦。后治改弊庐，无屋安设，寄京师南涧寺中。于时百姓竞铸钱，亦有盗毁金像以充铸者。时像在寺，已经数月。琰昼寝，梦见立于座隅；意甚异之。时日已?，即驰迎还。其夕，南涧十余躯像，悉遇盗亡。其后久之，像于曛?闲放光。显照，三尺许地，金辉秀起，焕然夺目。琰兄弟及仆役同睹者十余人。于时幼小，不即题记；比加撰录，忘其日月；是宋大明七年秋也。至泰始末，琰移居乌衣，周旋僧以此像权寓多宝寺。琰时暂游江都，此僧仍适荆楚；不知像处，垂将十载。常恐神宝，与因俱绝。宋升明末，游踬峡表，经过江陵，见此沙门，乃知像所。其年，琰还京师，即造多宝寺访焉。寺主爱公，云无此寄像。琰退虑此僧孟浪，将遂失此像，深以惆怅。

    Explanation

    2

    When Yan was young, he was in Jiaozhi. In that land, there was a virtuous monk, a man of morality. He was given the Five Precepts and a gold statue of Guanyin, which he was entrusted to worship. The statue's shape is different from today's, and it is not very ancient, likely made during the Yuanjia period. The casting and engraving are exceptionally fine, as if they are genuine and exquisite. Yan respectfully brought it back to the capital. At that time, he was in his childhood, and with his two younger brothers, they devoted themselves to worshiping the statue with unwavering dedication and tireless effort. Later, when he renovated his dilapidated house, there was no room to place the statue, so he temporarily placed it in the Nanjian Temple in the capital. At that time, the common people were competing to mint coins, and some even destroyed the gold statue to use the metal for casting. The statue had been in the temple for several months. Yan napped during the day and dreamed that the statue stood by his side. He found this very strange. When the sun had set, he immediately rushed to bring it back. That night, over ten statues in the Nanjian Temple were all stolen. After a long time, the statue began to emit light in the twilight. The light illuminated about three feet of ground, and the golden radiance was dazzling. Yan, his brothers, and over ten servants witnessed this together. At that time, being young, he did not immediately record it. When he later compiled a record, he forgot the date and month. This was in the autumn of the seventh year of the Daming era of the Liu Song dynasty (466 CE). By the end of the Taishi era, Yan moved to Wuyi, and the monk entrusted the statue to the Dabao Temple for temporary storage. When Yan briefly traveled to Jiangdu, the monk went to Jingchu. He did not know the location of the statue for nearly ten years. He often feared that the divine treasure would be lost along with the opportunity. At the end of the Shengming era of the Liu Song dynasty, when he traveled through the Xiang River area and passed through Jiangling, he saw this monk and learned the location of the statue. That year, Yan returned to the capital and immediately visited the Dabao Temple to inquire about it. The abbot, Aigong, said there was no such statue in the temple. Yan was worried that the monk had acted rashly and that he might lose the statue, deeply lamenting this.

    3

    其夜，梦人见语云，像在多宝，爱公忘耳，当为得之。见将至寺，与人手自开殿，见像在殿之东众小像中，的的分明。诘旦造寺，具以所梦请爱公。爱公乃为开殿，果见此像在殿之东，如梦所睹。遂得像还。时建元元年七月十三日也。像今常自供养，唐释道宣三宝感通录卷二引像今常自供养至末庶必永作津梁。循复其事，有感深怀；沿此征觌，缀成斯记。夫镜接近情，莫踰仪像；瑞验之发，多自此兴。

    Explanation

    3

    That night, I dreamed of someone who spoke to me, saying that the image was in the treasure, and you, Master Ai, have forgotten it, but you will obtain it. I saw [someone] leading me to the temple, and with the help of someone, I opened the hall myself. I found the image clearly among other smaller images in the east of the hall. The next morning, I visited the temple and reported my dream in full detail to Master Ai. Master Ai then opened the hall, and indeed, I found the image in the east of the hall, just as I had seen in my dream. Thus, I obtained the image and returned. It was on the thirteenth day of the seventh month of the first year of Jianyuan. The image is now always kept for my own veneration. In the second volume of the 'San Bao Gan Tong Lu' by Tang Dynasty monk Daoxuan, it is recorded that the image is now always kept for my own veneration, and it is hoped that it will forever serve as a bridge. Following up on this matter, I am deeply moved; following this line of inquiry, I have compiled this record. The mirror is close to emotion, but nothing surpasses the image; miraculous signs often arise from this.

    4

    经云，镕斲图缋类形相者，爰能行动，及放光明。今西域释迦弥勒二像，晖用若冥，一引作真盖得相乎。今华夏景楷，一引作东今夏景摸　感通彔冥作真楷作模神应亟着，亦或当年群生，因会所感，假冯木石，以见幽异，不必克由容好，而能然也。故沈石浮深，实阐闽吴之化；尘金泻液，用舒彭宋之祸。感通录作用绵彭宋之福其余铨示繁方，虽难曲辨；率其大抵，允归自从。感通录作允归日从若夫经塔显效，旨证亦同；事非殊贯，故继其末。法苑珠林十七又十四引像今常自供养已下

    Explanation

    4

    According to the scriptures, those who refine and shape metal, paint, and create images can move and emit light. The statues of Shakyamuni and Maitreya in the Western Regions have a light that is as if in darkness, and one interpretation makes them true. The images in China, also known as Eastern images, are different interpretations. The records of spiritual connections show true models, and divine responses are often recorded. They may also be moved by events, using wood and stone to reveal the mysterious, without necessarily relying on beauty. Therefore, the story of a stone sinking and floating reveals the transformation in the regions of Min and Wu; the story of dust and gold being mixed alleviates the suffering in the regions of Peng and Song. The records of spiritual connections show the blessings in the regions of Peng and Song, and other methods of illustration, though difficult to explain, generally follow their own nature. The effectiveness of Buddhist stupas is the same, and the events are not different in essence, so they are followed up. The Fa Yuan Zhu Lin (Treasury of the Buddhist Law) and the Gan Tong Lu (Record of Spiritual Connections) cite these images, which are now often self-supplied.

    5

    冥祥记
    　　汉明帝梦见神人：形垂二丈，身黄金色，项佩日光。以问群臣。或对曰：“西方有神，其号曰佛，形如陛下所梦，得无是乎？”于是发使天竺，写致经像，表之中夏。自天子王侯，咸敬事之。闻人死精神不灭，莫不惧然自失。初使者蔡愔，将西域沙门迦叶摩腾等赍优填王画释迦佛像；帝重之，如梦所见也。乃遣画工图之数本，于南宫清凉台及高阳门显节寿陵上供养。又于白马寺壁，画千乘万骑绕塔三?之像，如诸传备载。法苑珠林十三三宝感通录二

    Explanation

    5

    Mysterious Auspicious Records

    Emperor Ming of Han dreamed of a divine being: two zhang tall, with a golden body, and a sunbeam pendant around the neck. He asked his ministers about it. Some replied, "There is a deity from the West, known as Buddha, whose form matches what Your Majesty has seen in your dream. Could it be this?" Thus, he sent envoys to India to bring scriptures and images, spreading them in the Central Plains. From the emperor down to the nobles, all revered and served this deity. Hearing that the spirit does not perish after death, none remained calm. Initially, the envoy Cai Yin brought Indian monks Kasyapa Matanga and others with the statue of the Buddha created by King Udayana of Gandhara. The emperor valued it greatly, just as he had seen in his dream. He then sent painters to create several copies, placing them on the Qingliang Terrace in the Nan Gong, the Gaoyang Gate, and the Xianjie Shouling for veneration. Also on the walls of the White Horse Temple, they painted images of thousands of chariots and horses circling the stupa three times, as recorded in various biographies. Jewel Forest of the Dharma Garden, Volume 13; Record of the Three Treasures' Responsive Communication, Volume 2.

    6

    晋羊太傅祜，字叔子，泰山人也。西晋名臣，声冠区夏。年五岁时，尝令乳母取先所弄指环。乳母曰：“汝本无此，于何取耶？”祜曰：“昔于东垣边弄之，落桑树中。”乳母曰：“汝可自觅。”祜曰：“此非先宅，儿不知处。”后因出门游望，迳而东行。乳母随之。至李氏家，乃入至东垣树下，探得小环。李氏惊怅曰：“吾子昔有此环，常爱弄之。七岁暴亡。亡后不知环处。此亡儿之物也，云何持去？”祜持环走。李氏遂问之。乳母既说祜言。李氏悲喜；遂欲求祜，还为其儿。里中解喻，然后得止。祜年长，常患头风。医欲攻治。祜曰：“吾生三日时，头首北户，觉风吹顶，意其患之，但不能语耳。病源既久，不可治也。”祜后为荆州都督，镇襄阳，经给武当寺殊余精舍。或问其故，祜默然。后因忏悔，叙说因果。乃曰，前身承有诸罪，赖造此寺，故获申济，所以使供养之情偏殷勤重也。法苑珠林二十六

    Explanation

    6

    Yang Hu, a high-ranking official of the Western Jin Dynasty, was known by his courtesy name Shuzi and hailed from Mount Tai. Renowned as a distinguished minister, his fame spread throughout the land. When he was five years old, he once asked his wet nurse to fetch the finger ring he had played with before. The wet nurse said, "You never had this ring; where could it be?" Hu replied, "I played with it at the eastern wall in the past, and it fell into a mulberry tree." The wet nurse said, "You can find it yourself." Hu said, "This is not my ancestral home; I don't know where it is." Later, when he went out to sightsee, he headed east. The wet nurse followed him. He arrived at the home of a family named Li and went to the eastern wall, where he found the small ring under a mulberry tree. The Li family was surprised and saddened, saying, "Our son once had this ring and loved to play with it. He died at the age of seven. After his death, we did not know where the ring was. This is the ring of our deceased son; why are you taking it away?" Hu took the ring and ran. The Li family then asked him about it. The wet nurse explained what Hu had said. The Li family was both sad and happy; they wanted to adopt Hu as their son. The villagers explained the situation, and the Li family then stopped.

    As Hu grew older, he often suffered from headaches. A doctor wanted to treat him. Hu said, "When I was three days old, my head was at the northern door, and I felt the wind blowing on my head. I suspect that this is the cause of my illness, but I could not speak about it at the time. The disease has been long-standing; it cannot be cured."

    Later, Hu became the governor of Jing Province and stationed himself in Xiangyang. He visited the Wudang Temple and its other excellent hermitages. Someone asked him why. Hu remained silent. Later, during a confession, he explained the cause and effect. He said, "In my previous life, I committed various sins. Thanks to the construction of this temple, I was thus able to be saved. This is why my devotion to offerings is particularly diligent and sincere." (From Fayuan Zhulin)

    7

    晋沙门仕行慧皎高僧传作士行者，颍川人也。姓朱氏。气志方远，识宇沈正，循心直诣，荣辱不能动焉。时经典未备，唯有小品；而章句阙略，义致弗显。魏甘露五年，发迹雍州，西至于阗，寻求经藏。踰历诸国。西域僧徒，多小乘学，闻仕行求方等诸经，咸骇怪不与。曰，边人不识正法，将多惑乱。仕行曰，“经云，千载将末，法当东流。若疑非佛说，请以至诚验之。”乃焚柴灌油。烟炎方盛，仕行捧经涕泪，稽颡誓曰：“若果出金口，应宣布汉地。

    Explanation

    7

    A Jin dynasty monk named Shixing (also known as Shihang in the Gao Seng Zhuan), originally from Yingchuan, bore the surname Zhu. He possessed a lofty spirit and far-reaching aspirations, with a deep and upright understanding. Following his heart directly, he was not moved by honor or disgrace. At the time, the Buddhist scriptures were incomplete, with only the shorter versions available; the verses and sentences were incomplete, and the meaning was not clearly expressed. In the fifth year of the Ganlu era of the Wei dynasty, he set out from Yongzhou and traveled west to Yutian, seeking the Buddhist canon. He passed through various countries. The monks of the Western Regions mostly practiced Hinayana Buddhism. When they heard that Shixing was seeking the Mahayana sutras, they were all startled and refused to give them, saying, "People on the border do not know the true Dharma and will be easily confused." Shixing replied, "The scriptures say that in the latter days, the Dharma will spread to the East. If you doubt that it is the Buddha's teaching, please test it with utmost sincerity." He then burned wood and poured oil. As the smoke and flames were at their peak, Shixing held the scriptures and wept, kneeling and swearing, "If it truly came from the Buddha's mouth, it should be announced in Han territory."

    8

    诸佛菩萨，宜为证明。”于是投经火中，腾燎移景。既而一积煨尽，文字无毁，皮牒若故。举国欣敬。因留供养。遣弟子法饶，赍送梵本，还至陈留浚仪仓垣诗寺。高僧传云陈留仓垣水南寺出之，凡九十篇，二十万言。河南居士竺叔兰，练解方俗，深善法味，亲共传译，今放光首品是也。仕行八十乃亡，依阇维之火灭。经日尸形犹全。国人惊异，皆曰，若真得道法，当毁坏。应声碎散。乃敛骨起塔。慧志道人先师相传。释公亦具载其事也。法苑珠林二十八

    Explanation

    8

    The Buddhas and Bodhisattvas should serve as witnesses. Thus, the scripture was thrown into the fire, and the flames rose, casting moving shadows. Soon after, all the ashes had burned away, yet the characters remained undamaged, and the parchment seemed as if it were still new. The entire country rejoiced and respected this miracle. Therefore, they were kept for worship. A disciple named Fa Rao was sent to carry and deliver the Sanskrit version of the text, returning it to the Cangyuan Temple in Junyi, Chenliu. As recorded in the Biography of Eminent Monks, this text originated from the Cangyuan Temple in Chenliu, totaling ninety chapters and two hundred thousand words. The lay Buddhist scholar Zhubolan from Henan, well-versed in local customs and dialects, deeply appreciated the flavor of the Dharma, and personally involved in the translation, produced the first chapter of the Flower Adornment Sutra. He served for eighty years before passing away by the fire of cremation. After several days, his body remained intact. The people were surprised and amazed, and all said, "If truly attained the Dharma, it should break apart at the sound." It would break apart at the sound. They then collected his bones and built a stupa. As recorded by the monk Huizhi, who inherited the teachings from his predecessors, and Master Shi also recorded this event, Chapter 28 of the Jewels of the Dharma Garden documents this story.

    9

    晋赵泰，字文和，清河贝丘人也。祖父京兆广记引作清河太守。泰，郡举孝廉；公府辟，不就。精思典籍，有誉乡里。当晚乃膺仕，终于中散大夫。泰年三十五时，尝卒心痛，须臾而死。下尸于地，心暖不已，屈伸随人。留尸十日。平旦，喉中有声如雨。俄而稣活。说初死之时，梦有一人，来近心下。复有二人，乘黄马。从者二人，夹扶泰腋。径将东行，不知可几里。至一大城，崔嵬高峻。城色青黑，状锡。广记引作城邑青黑色将泰向城门入。经两重门。有瓦屋可数千间；男女大小，亦数千人，行列而立。吏着皂衣。有五六人条疏姓字，云当以科呈府君。泰名在三十。须臾，将泰与数千人男女，一时俱进。府君西向坐，简视名簿讫，复遣泰南入黑门。有人着绛衣坐大屋下，以次呼名，问生时所事：“作何孽罪，孽字依广记引补行何福善？谛汝等辞以实言也。此恒遣六部使者，常在人间，疏记善恶，具有条状。

    Explanation

    9

    Zhao Tai, courtesy name Wenhé, was from Beiqiu, Qinghe. His grandfather was the governor of Jingzhao, as noted in the Guangji (Record of Wonders). Zhao Tai was recommended by his county as a filial and clean official, but he declined the invitation from the imperial court to serve. He devoted himself to studying classical texts and earned a good reputation in his hometown. He began his official career later in life and eventually became a Zhongshangdaifu (Middle Scattering Doctor). At the age of thirty-five, Zhao Tai once suffered a sudden and severe heart attack, dying almost instantly. His body was laid on the ground, but his heart remained warm, and his limbs could still be bent and stretched by others. The body was left for ten days. At dawn, there was a sound in his throat like rain. Soon after, he revived. He recounted that when he first died, he dreamed of a person coming close to his heart. Two more people arrived, riding yellow horses, with two attendants supporting him under the armpits. They took him eastward, not knowing how far they traveled. They reached a large city, tall and steep, with blue-black walls like tin, as noted in the Guangji. They led Zhao Tai to the city gate and entered through two gates. There were thousands of tile-roofed houses, and men, women, and children, numbering in the thousands, stood in rows. Officials wore black clothes. Five or six people listed names and surnames, saying they would present the list to the governor. Zhao Tai's name was on the thirtieth list. Soon, Zhao Tai and thousands of others were led forward together. The governor, sitting facing west, reviewed the list of names. He then sent Zhao Tai south into a black gate. There was a person wearing red clothing sitting under a large house, calling out names in order and asking about their deeds in life: "What sins did you commit, and what good deeds did you perform? Speak the truth about your deeds." These six officials are always sent to record good and evil deeds, with detailed records.

    不可得虚。”泰答，“父兄仕宦皆二千石。我少在家修学而已，无所事也，亦不犯恶。”乃遣泰为水官监作使，将二千余人运沙裨岸。昼夜勤苦。后转泰水官都督，知诸狱事。给泰马兵，令案行地狱。所至诸狱，楚毒各殊。或针贯其舌，流血竟体。或被头露发，裸形徒跣，相牵而行。有持大杖，从后催促。铁床铜柱，烧之洞然；驱迫此人，抱卧其上。赴即焦烂，寻复还生。或炎炉巨镬，焚煮罪人。身首碎堕，随沸翻转。有鬼持叉，倚于其侧。有三四百人，立于一面，次当入镬，相抱悲泣。或剑树高广。广记引有此字不知限量。根茎枝叶，皆剑为之。人众相訾，自登自攀，若有欣意。广记引作欣竞而身首割截，尺寸离断。泰见祖父母及二弟，在此狱中。相见涕泣。泰出狱门，见有二人赍文书来，语狱吏，言有三人，其家为其于塔寺中县旛烧香，救解其罪，可出福舍。俄见三人，自狱而出；已有自然衣服，完整在身。
