    10

    It cannot be obtained." Tai replied, "My father and elder brothers all hold the rank of 2,000 stones. I have only studied at home since my youth, and have nothing to do, nor have I committed any evil." He was then sent to serve as the supervisor of water management, leading over two thousand people to transport sand and reinforce the embankment. They worked day and night with great effort. Later, he was promoted to the position of supervisor of water management, overseeing all matters related to the prisons. He was given horses and soldiers, and ordered to inspect the underworld. Everywhere he went, the tortures varied. Some had needles piercing their tongues, with blood flowing all over their bodies. Others had their heads uncovered and hair exposed, naked and barefoot, dragging each other along. There were those holding large sticks, pushing them from behind. Iron beds and copper pillars, burning fiercely; forcing these people to lie on them. They immediately burn and rot, but soon regenerate. Some were in blazing furnaces and huge cauldrons, burning and boiling criminals. Their bodies and heads were shattered and tossed about. There were demons holding spears, standing by their side. There were several hundred people standing on one side, next to enter the cauldron, holding each other and weeping. Some had tall and wide sword trees, the Guangji (Comprehensive Records) mentions this word but does not specify its limits. The roots, stems, leaves, and branches are all made of swords. People criticize each other, climbing and grasping each other, as if with joy. The Guangji records that they compete with joy, and their bodies and heads are cut apart, cut into pieces. Tai saw his grandparents and two younger brothers in this prison. They wept upon seeing each other. Tai left the prison gate, and saw two people bringing documents, speaking to the prison guards, saying there are three people, whose families have hung banners and burned incense for them in the pagoda temple, to save them from their sins and release them into a place of happiness. Soon he saw three people leaving the prison; they were already dressed in natural clothes, complete and whole.

    11

    南诣一门，云名开光大舍；有三重门，朱采照发。见此三人，即入舍中。泰亦随入。前有大殿珍宝周饰，精光耀目。金玉为床。见一神人，姿容伟异，殊好非常，坐此座上。边有沙门立侍，甚众。见府君来，恭敬作礼。泰问此是何人，府君致敬。吏曰，号名世尊度人之师，有愿令恶道中人皆出听经。时云有百万九千人，皆出地狱，入百里城。在此到者，奉法众生也。行虽亏殆，尚当得度，故开经法。七日之中，随本城作善恶多少，差次免脱。泰未出之顷，已见十人，升虚而去。出此舍，复见一城，方二百余里，名为受变形城。地狱考治已毕者，当于此城，更受变报。泰入其城，见有土瓦屋数千区，各有坊巷。广记引作房舍正中有瓦屋高壮，阑槛采饰。有数百局吏，对校文书云，杀生者当作蜉蝣，朝生?死；劫盗者当作猪羊，受人屠割；淫泆者作鹤鹜獐麋，两舌者作?枭鸺鹠，捍债者为驴骡牛马。泰案行毕，还水官处。

    Explanation

    11

    To the south, there is a gate, said to be named the "Hall of Enlightened Light." It has three tiers of doors, each adorned with vivid red pigments that glow brilliantly. Upon seeing these three individuals, they immediately entered the hall. Ta also followed them in. In front stood a grand hall, its walls and furnishings encrusted with precious jewels, their brilliance dazzling to the eye. The bed was made of gold and jade. There they saw a divine being, whose appearance was majestic and extraordinary, unlike anything ordinary, seated upon this throne. Beside him stood numerous monks in attendance. When the Lord saw them, he greeted them with deep respect. Ta asked, "Who is this person?" The Lord responded with reverence. The official replied, "He is known as the 'Worldly Respected One, the Teacher Who Guides People.' He has vowed to lead all beings from the lower realms to listen to the teachings." It is said that there were a million nine thousand people who emerged from hell and entered the city spanning a hundred miles. Those who have arrived here are all beings who follow the Dharma. Though their actions may be flawed, they should still be saved, which is why the teachings of the scriptures are opened. Within seven days, depending on the amount of good or bad deeds they have done in their previous life, they will be released in a graded manner. Before Ta had even left, he had already seen ten people ascend into the void and depart. Exiting this hall, Ta saw another city, measuring over two hundred miles in area, named the "City of Transformation." Those whose punishment in hell has been completed will undergo further transformations in this city. Ta entered the city and saw thousands of houses made of clay and tiles, each with its own neighborhoods and alleys. Records indicate that these are houses. In the center stood a tall and sturdy building, its railings and decorations splendid. There were hundreds of officials, comparing and verifying documents, saying that those who kill will become mayflies, living only for a short time; those who rob will become pigs or sheep, to be slaughtered by others; those who engage in promiscuity will become cranes, ducks, deer, and boars; those who spread rumors will become owls and screech owls; those who evade debts will become donkeys, mules, cows, or horses. After inspecting everything, Ta returned to the office of the water official.

    12

    主者语泰，“卿是长者子，以何罪过，而来在此？”泰答，“祖父兄弟，皆二千石。我举孝廉；公府辟，不行。修志念善，不染众恶。”主者曰：“卿无罪过，故相使为水官都督。不尔，与地狱中人无以异也。”泰问主者曰：“人有何行，死得乐报？”主者唯言：奉法弟子，精进持戒，得乐报，无有滴罚也。泰复问曰：“人未事法时，所行罪过，事法之后，得以除不？”答曰：“皆除也。”语毕，主者开縢箧，检泰年纪，尚有余算三十年在。

    Explanation

    12

    The overseer spoke to Tai, saying, "You are the son of a respected elder. For what crime or fault have you come here?" Tai replied, "My grandfather and uncles were all officials of the rank of 2,000 stones. I was recommended as a filial and upright official; I was summoned by the imperial court but did not go. I cultivate my aspirations and think of goodness, not tainted by many evils." The overseer said, "You have no crimes or faults, so I have appointed you as the water official supervisor. Otherwise, you would be no different from those in hell." Tai asked the overseer, "What actions does a person take that result in a happy afterlife?" The overseer replied, "Disciples who follow the law, diligently observe precepts, receive a happy reward, and there is no punishment at all." Tai asked again, "Before a person follows the law, the sins they commit, after following the law, can these sins be forgiven?" The overseer answered, "They can all be forgiven." When the conversation was over, the overseer opened a bamboo box, checked Tai's age, and found that he still had thirty years of life remaining.

    13

    乃遣泰还。临别，主者曰：“已见地狱罪报如是，当告世人，皆令作善。善恶随人，其犹影响，可不慎乎？”时亲表内外○视泰者，五六十人，同闻泰说。泰自书记，以示时人。时晋太始五年七月十三日也。乃为祖父母二弟延请僧众，大设福会。皆命子孙改意奉法，课劝精进。时人闻泰死而复生，多见罪福，互来访问。时有太中大夫武城孙丰，关内侯常山郝伯平等十人，同集泰舍，款曲寻问，莫不惧然，皆即奉法也。法苑珠林七太平广记三百七十七

    Explanation

    13

    Tai was then sent back. At parting, the host said, "Having seen the punishment in hell like this, you should inform the world, all should do good deeds. Good and evil follow people, just as shadows follow shapes; can one not be careful?" At that time, relatives inside and outside, those who visited Tai, numbered fifty or sixty. They heard Tai's words together. Tai himself wrote it down, to show the people of the time. It was July 13th of the fifth year of the Tai Shi era in the Jin dynasty. Then, Tai invited monks for his ancestors and two younger brothers, greatly set up a blessing assembly. All commanded their descendants to change their minds and follow the law, encouraging diligent progress. The people of the time heard that Tai died and came back to life, often seeing punishment and blessings, and came and went to visit. There were the Grand Middle Doctor Sun Feng from Wucheng, the Inner Pass Marquis Hao Boping and ten others, who gathered together at Tai's house, carefully asked, and no one did not be frightened. All immediately followed the law. Chapter Seven of the Jewel Forest of the Dharma Garden, Chapter 377 of the Comprehensive Records of Peace and Prosperity.

    14

    晋沙门支法衡，晋初人也。得病旬日亡。经三日而稣活。说死时，有人将去，见如官曹舍者数处，不肯受之。俄见有铁轮，轮上有铁爪，从西转来；无持引者，而转驶如风。有一吏呼罪人当轮立；轮转来轹之，翻还；如此，数人碎烂。吏呼衡道人来当轮立。衡恐怖自责，悔不精进，“今当此轮乎？”语毕，谓衡曰：“道人可去！”于是仰首，见天有孔，不觉倏尔上升。以头穿中，两手搏两边，四向顾视，见七宝宫殿，及诸天人。衡甚踊跃，不能得上。疲而复还下所。将衡去。人笑曰：“见何等物，不能上乎？”乃以衡付船官。船官行船，使为柂工。衡曰：“我不能持柂。”强之。有船数百，皆随衡后。衡不晓捉柂，跄沙洲上。吏司推衡，汝道而失，以法应斩。

    Explanation

    14

    A monk named Zhi Faheng from the Jin Dynasty fell ill for ten days and died. After three days, he revived. He recounted that upon his death, someone took him to several places resembling government offices, but they refused to accept him. Soon, he saw an iron wheel with iron claws on it, turning from the west. There was no one holding or pulling it, yet it turned swiftly like the wind. A clerk called out for a sinner to stand before the wheel. The wheel turned and crushed the person, then turned back. This happened to several people, who were crushed to pieces. The clerk then called out for Zhi Faheng to stand before the wheel. Terrified and blaming himself, Zhi Faheng regretted not having been diligent. "Will I be hit by this wheel now?" he asked. The clerk then told him, "Monk, you can go!" Zhi Faheng looked up and saw a hole in the sky, and suddenly he ascended. He put his head through the hole, held onto both sides with his hands, and looked around in all directions. He saw palaces made of seven treasures and various heavenly beings. Zhi Faheng was very excited but could not ascend. He grew tired and returned to the lower place. They took him away. People laughed and said, "What did you see that you couldn't ascend?" Then they handed Zhi Faheng over to the ship officials. The ship officials were operating the ship and made him the helmsman. Zhi Faheng said, "I cannot hold the tiller." They forced him. There were hundreds of ships following behind him. Zhi Faheng did not know how to hold the tiller and crashed onto a sandbar. The officials pushed Zhi Faheng and said, "You led the ship astray, and according to the law, you should be executed."

    15

    引衡上岸，雷鼓将斩。忽有五色二龙，推船还浮。吏乃原衡罪。载衡北行。三十许里，见好屯岸，有数万家，云是流人。衡窃上岸。屯中饶狗，牙欲啮之。衡大恐惧。望见西北有讲堂，上有沙门甚众，闻经呗之声。衡遽走趣之。堂有十二阶。衡始蹑一阶，见亡师法柱踞胡床坐。见衡曰：“我弟子也，何以而来？”因起临阶，以手巾打衡面，曰，“莫来！”衡甚欲上，复举步登阶。柱复推令下。至三乃止。见平地有井一口，深三四丈，塼无隙际。衡心念言，此井自然。井边有人谓曰：“不自然者，何得成井？”虽见法柱，故倚望之，谓衡“可复道还去，狗不啮汝！”衡还水边，亦不见向来船也。衡渴欲饮水，乃堕水中，因便得稣。于是出家，持戒菜食。昼夜精思为至行。沙门比丘法桥，衡弟子也。珠林七

    Explanation

    15

    Lead Heng onto the shore, and sound the drum as if for execution. Suddenly, two colorful dragons appeared and pushed the boat back to float. The official then pardoned Heng's crime. They took Heng northward. After about thirty miles, they reached a good harbor or landing place, where there were tens of thousands of displaced people. Heng stealthily went ashore. The camp was full of dogs that wanted to bite him. Heng was greatly afraid. He saw a lecture hall to the northwest, with many monks inside, and heard the sound of chanting scriptures. Heng rushed to go there. The hall had twelve steps. Heng started to climb the first step when he saw the deceased teacher Fa Zhu sitting on a trapeze-like chair. Fa Zhu saw Heng and said, "I am your teacher, why have you come?" He then stood up and approached the steps, using his handkerchief to hit Heng's face, saying, "Do not come!" Heng very much wanted to go up, so he took steps to ascend the stairs. Fa Zhu pushed him down again. This happened up to three times and then stopped. Heng saw a well on the ground, about 30 to 40 feet deep, with seamless bricks. Heng thought to himself, "This well is natural." Someone by the well said, "If it's not natural, how could it be a well?" Even though Heng saw Fa Zhu, he still hoped and told Heng, "You can go back, and the dogs won't bite you!" Heng returned to the water's edge, but he did not see the boat he had come in. Heng was thirsty and wanted to drink water, so he fell into the water and thus revived. He then became a monk, observed precepts, and ate vegetables. He thought deeply day and night, practicing the highest virtues. The monk Bhikshu Fa Qiao, who was Heng's disciple, is mentioned in the Zhu Lin (Seven).

    16

    晋安罗江县，有霍山，其高蔽日。上有石杵，高僧传石杵作石盂疑杵是杅字之讹面径数丈。杵中泉水，深五六尺，经常流溢。古老传云，列仙之所游饵也。有沙门释僧群，隐居其山，常饮此水，遂以不饥，因而绝粒。晋安太守陶夏，高僧传云陶夔闻而求之。群以水遗陶，出山辄臭。陶于是越海造山。于时天景澄朗。陶践山足，便风雨晦暝。如此者三，竟不得至。群所栖营，与泉隔一涧。旦夕往还，以一木为梁。后旦将渡，辄见一折翅鸭，舒翼当梁，头逆唼；僧群永不得过。欲举锡拨之，恐其坠死。于此绝水，俄而饥卒。时传云，年百四十。群之将死，为众说云：“年少时尝打折一鸭翅，将或此鸭因缘之报乎？”珠林六十三

    Explanation

    16

    Jin'an Luojiang County has a Huo Mountain, whose height blocks the sun. On the mountain, there is a stone basin (or possibly a stone pestle) with a diameter of several zhang. The water in the basin overflows and flows continuously. According to ancient legends, this place is where immortals would play or fish. There was a monk named Sengqun who lived in seclusion on this mountain and drank the water from the basin, which prevented him from feeling hungry, leading him to abstain from food. The governor of Jin'an, Tao Xia (or possibly Tao Kui), heard about Sengqun and sought him out. Sengqun gave Tao the water, but it turned foul as soon as it left the mountain. Tao then crossed the sea to find Sengqun. At the time, the sky was clear and bright. When Tao stepped onto the base of the mountain, it began to rain heavily and become dark. This happened three times, but Tao never reached Sengqun. Sengqun's dwelling was separated from the basin by a stream. He would cross back and forth using a wooden bridge. One morning, as he was about to cross, he saw a duck with a broken wing spreading its wings across the bridge, biting against the wood. Sengqun could never cross the stream after this. He wanted to use his staff to push the duck away but was afraid it would fall and die. Without water, he soon starved to death. It is said that he lived to be 140 years old. Before his death, Sengqun told the crowd, "When I was young, I broke a duck's wing. Could this be the retribution for that deed?" (From Zhu Lin 63)

    17

    晋沙门耆域者，天竺人也。自西域浮海而来，将游关洛，达旧襄阳，欲寄载船北渡。船人见梵沙门衣服弊陋，轻而不载。比船达北岸，耆域亦上。举船皆惊。域前行，有两虎迎之，弭耳掉尾，域手摩其头，虎便入草。于是南北岸奔往请问，域日无所应答。及去，有数百人追之；见域徐行，而众走犹不及。惠帝末，域至洛阳。洛阳道士悉往礼焉。域不为起。译语讥其服章曰，“汝曹分流佛法，不以真诚，但为浮华，求供养耳。”见洛阳宫，曰，“忉利天宫，仿彿似此。

    Explanation

    17

    The monk Qiyu from Jin was a person from Tianzhu (India). He traveled by sea from the Western Regions, intending to visit the regions of Guanzhong and Luoyang, reaching the ancient city of Xiangyang, where he sought to board a ship to cross the river northward. The ship owner, seeing the Buddhist monk in tattered and shabby clothes, dismissed him lightly and did not allow him to board. When the ship finally reached the northern bank, Qiyu also climbed aboard. Everyone on the ship was astonished. As Qiyu walked ahead, two tigers greeted him, lowering their ears and wagging their tails. Qiyu gently patted their heads, and the tigers retreated into the grass. People from both banks then rushed to ask questions, but Qiyu remained silent. When he left, hundreds of people chased after him; they saw Qiyu walking slowly, and despite their efforts, they could not catch up. By the end of Emperor Huai's reign, Qiyu arrived in Luoyang. Taoist practitioners from Luoyang all came to greet him, but Qiyu did not stand up. An interpreter criticized his attire, saying, "You all divide the teachings of the Buddha, not out of sincerity, but merely for show, seeking offerings." When he saw the palace in Luoyang, he said, "The Tushita Heaven is somewhat similar to this."

    18

    当以道力成就，而生死力为之，不亦勤苦乎！”沙门支法渊竺法兴。并年少，后至。域为起立。法渊作礼讫，域以手摩其头曰：“好菩萨，羊中来。”见法兴入门，域大欣笑，往迎作礼。捉法兴手，举着头上曰：“好菩萨，从天人中来？”尚方中有一人，废病数年，垂死。域往视之，谓曰：“何以堕落，生此忧苦？”下病人于地，卧单席上，以应器置腹上，纻布覆之。梵○三偈讫，为梵祝可数千语。寻有臭气满屋。病人曰，活矣。域令人举布，见应器中如污泥者。病人遂瘥。

    Explanation

    18

    "Should spiritual cultivation be achieved through the power of the Dao, yet it is the force of life and death that accomplishes it, is it not hard work?" The monks Zhi Fayuan and Zhu Faxing, both young and arriving later, stood up for them. Fayuan performed the bow, and Yu rubbed his head and said, "Good bodhisattva, come from the sheep." Seeing Faxing enter, Yu was greatly delighted and smiled, went to welcome him and performed the bow. Taking Faxing's hand, he raised it to his head and said, "Good bodhisattva, come from the heavenly beings?" In the palace, there was a person who had been ill for many years and was on the verge of death. Yu went to see him and said, "Why did you fall into this state, causing such sorrow and suffering?" He lay the patient on the ground, on a single mat, placed a bowl on his abdomen, and covered him with coarse cloth. After reciting three verses of a Buddhist chant, he recited a chant of several thousand words. Soon there was a foul smell filling the room. The patient said, "I am alive." Yu ordered someone to lift the cloth, and saw that the bowl contained something like mud. The patient then recovered.

    19

    长沙太守滕永文，先颇精进。时在洛阳，两脚风挛经年。域为祝，应时得申，数日起行。满水寺中有思惟树，先枯死，域向之祝，旬日，树还生茂。时寺中有竺法行善谈论，时以比乐令。见域，稽首曰：“已见得道证，愿当秉法。”域曰：“守口摄意，身莫犯如是行者，度世去。”法行曰：“得道者当授所未闻。斯言，人岁沙弥亦以之诵，非所望于得道者。”域笑曰：“如子之言，八岁而致诵，百岁不能行。人皆知敬得道者，不知行之即自得。以我观之易耳。妙当在君，岂愠未闻。

    Explanation

    19

    Teng Yongwen, the governor of Changsha, was previously quite diligent in his spiritual practice. At that time, while in Luoyang, his legs were paralyzed by wind evil for many years. Yu made a wish, and at the right time, he was able to move his legs, and after several days, he was able to walk again. There was a Tree of Contemplation in Man Shui Temple, which had previously died, but Yu made a wish to it, and after ten days, the tree grew lush again. At that time, there was a monk named Zhufa Xing who was good at discussion, and he was compared to the officer in charge of music. When he saw Yu, he bowed respectfully and said, "I have seen the evidence of your attainment of the Way. I wish to uphold the Dharma." Yu replied, "Guard your speech and control your mind, and do not violate such conduct with your body, and cross over to the other shore." Zhufa Xing said, "One who has attained the Way should teach what has not been heard before. Such words, even an eight-year-old novice can recite them, but they are not what one expects from one who has attained the Way." Yu smiled and said, "As you say, at eight years old, one can memorize, but in a hundred years, one cannot practice. Everyone knows to respect one who has attained the Way, but they do not know that by practicing, one attains it oneself. In my view, it is easy. The subtlety lies in you. Why be angry about not having heard it?"

    20

    ”京师贵贱，赠遗衣物，以数千亿万，悉受之。临去，封而留之，唯作旛八百枚，以骆驼负之先遣。随估客西归天竺。又持法兴一纳袈裟随身。谓法兴曰：“此地方大为造新之罪，可哀如何？”域发，送者数千人。于洛阳寺中中食讫，取道。人有其日发长安来，见域在长安寺中。又域所遣估客及骆驼奴达炖煌河上，逢估客弟于天竺来，云近炖煌寺中见域。弟子漯登者云，于流沙北逢域，言语款曲，计其旬日，又域发洛阳时也。而其所行盖已万里矣。珠林二十八高僧传载在耆域之○当迻正

    Explanation

    20

    京城中的富贵贫贱，赠送衣物作为礼物，数量达到数千亿，全部接受。临行前，将衣物封存并留下，只制作了八百面旗帜，用骆驼运送并先行出发。跟随商人西行返回印度。又携带法兴的一件袈裟随身。对法兴说：“这个地方因建造新事物而犯下了大罪，多么可悲啊！”域离开时，送别的人有数千人。在洛阳寺中吃完饭后，选择道路出发。有人在同一天从长安出发，见到域在长安寺中。域派遣的商人和骆驼奴到达了敦煌河上，遇到了从印度来的商人的弟弟，说最近在敦煌寺中见到了域。弟子漯登说，在流沙以北遇到了域，详细而诚恳地交谈，计算大约十天，正是域离开洛阳的时候。而他已经行走了大约一万里的路程。《珠林》第二十八卷的高僧传记载了关于耆域的条目，应当进行校正。

    21

    晋沙门佛调，不知何国人。往来常山，积年业，尚纯朴，不表辞饰；时咸以此重之。常山有奉法者兄弟二人，居去寺百里。兄妇病甚笃，载出寺侧，以近医药。兄既奉调为师，朝昼常在寺中，咨询行道。异日。调忽往其家，弟具问嫂所苦，并审兄安否。调曰：“病者粗可，卿兄如常。”调去后，弟亦策马继往，言及调旦来。兄惊曰：“和尚旦初不出寺，汝何容相见？”兄弟争问调，调笑而不答，咸共异焉。调或独入深山，一年半岁，赍干饭数升，还恒有余。有人尝随调山行数十里。天?大雪，调入石穴虎窟中宿。

    Explanation

    21

    During the Jin dynasty, there was a monk named Fódiào, whose country of origin is unknown. He traveled frequently to Chángshān, where he practiced the Dharma for many years. He remained simple and unadorned, not seeking elaborate speech or appearance; at that time, all respected him for this. In Chángshān, there were two devout practitioners who were brothers, living a hundred li away from the temple. The elder brother's wife was gravely ill, so she was taken to live near the temple for easier access to medical care. Since the elder brother had taken Fódiào as his teacher, he often remained at the temple during the day and early morning, consulting with him on spiritual practice. On another day, Fódiào suddenly visited their home. The younger brother asked him in detail about his sister-in-law's suffering and inquired about his brother’s well-being. Fódiào replied, “The patient is somewhat better, and your brother is as usual.” After Fódiào left, the younger brother also rode his horse to follow him, mentioning that Fódiào had come that morning. The elder brother was surprised and said, “The monk did not leave the temple at dawn, how could you have met him?” The brothers both questioned Fódiào about this, but he merely smiled and did not answer, and all were amazed by this. Sometimes Fódiào would go alone into the deep mountains, staying for a year or half a year, carrying only a few sheng of dry rice, and upon returning, there was always more than enough. Once, someone followed Fódiào on a mountain journey for dozens of miles. It was a day of severe cold and heavy snow, and Fódiào spent the night in a stone cave or a tiger’s den.

    22

    虎还横卧窟前。调语曰：“我夺汝居处，有愧如何！”虎弭耳下山。随者骇惧。调自克亡期，远近悉至。乃与诀曰：“天地长久，尚有崩坏；岂况人物，而欲永存？若能荡除三垢，专心真净；形数虽乖，而神会必同。”众咸涕流。调还房端坐，以衣蒙头，奄然而终。终后数年，调白衣弟子八人，入西山伐木，忽见调在高岩上，衣服鲜明，姿仪畅悦。皆惊喜作礼问，“和尚尚在此耶？”答曰，“吾常自在耳。”具问知故消息，良久乃去。八人便舍事还家，向同法者说，众无以验之。共发冢开棺，不见其尸。珠林二十八

    Explanation

    22

    The tiger returned and lay down in front of its den. The monk said, "I have taken your dwelling, how can I not feel ashamed!" The tiger lowered its ears and descended the mountain. Those who followed were filled with fear. The monk had predicted his own time of death, and people from far and wide came to bid him farewell. He said to them, "The heavens and earth endure for a long time, yet they still have their moments of collapse; how much more so for human beings, who desire eternal existence? If one can cleanse oneself of the three defilements and focus on true purity, even if physical forms differ, the spiritual essence will surely be the same." All present shed tears. The monk returned to his room, sat upright, covered his head with a cloth, and died suddenly. Several years later, eight of the monk's lay disciples entered the west mountain to cut wood. Suddenly, they saw the monk on a high cliff, dressed brightly and looking joyful. They were all surprised and joyful, bowing to ask, "Is the master still here?" He replied, "I have always been here." They asked about the news of the old friends, and after a long while, they departed. The eight disciples then gave up their work and returned home to tell their fellow practitioners. The others had no way to verify this. They opened the tomb and found no body. From the "Buddhist Treasury," Chapter Twenty-Eight.

    23

    晋犍陀勒，不知何国人也。尝游洛邑，周历数年。虽敬其风操，而莫能测焉。后语人曰，盘鸱高僧传鸱作?山中有古塔寺，若能修建，其福无量。众人许之。与俱入山。既至，唯草木深芜，莫知基朕。勒指示曰：“此是寺基也。”众试掘之，果得塔下石础。复示讲堂，僧房，井灶。开凿寻求，皆如其言。于是始疑其异。寺既修，勒为僧主。去洛百里。每朝至洛邑，赴会听讲竟，辄乞油一钵，擎之还寺。虽复去来早晚，未曾失中晡之期。有人日能行数百里者，欲随而验之，乃与俱。此人驰而不及；勒顾笑曰：“汝执吾袈裟，可以不倦。”既持衣后，不及移晷，便已至寺。其人休息数日乃还。方悟神人。后不知终。珠林八十二

    Explanation

    23

    Jin Dynasty's Kandala, whose nationality is unknown, once traveled to Luoyang and spent several years there. Although people respected his manner and conduct, no one could fully understand him. Later, he told others that in a mountain there was an ancient pagoda temple, and if it could be restored, the merit would be boundless. Everyone agreed to this proposal. He went with them into the mountains. Upon arrival, they found only deep and overgrown vegetation, and no one knew where the base of the temple was. Kandala pointed out and said, "This is the site of the temple." They tried digging and indeed found the stone base of the stupa. He then showed the lecture hall, monks' quarters, and wells and kitchens. When they excavated and searched, everything was as he had said. Thus, they began to suspect his extraordinary nature. After the temple was restored, Kandala became the abbot. It was a hundred miles away from Luoyang. Every morning he would go to Luoyang, after attending gatherings and listening to lectures, he would then ask for a bowl of oil and carry it back to the temple. Although he went and came at different times, he never missed the noon hour. There was someone who could travel hundreds of miles in a day, who wanted to follow and verify it, so he went with him. This person ran but could not catch up; Kandala looked back and smiled, saying, "You hold my robe, and you will not get tired." After holding the robe, before the shadow moved, he had already arrived at the temple. This person rested for several days and then returned. Only then did they realize he was a divine being. Later, it is unknown what became of him. Chapter 82 of Zhu Lin.

    24

    晋抵世常，中山人也。家道殷富。太康中，禁晋人作沙门。世常奉法精进，潜于宅中起立精舍，供养沙门；于法兰亦在焉。僧众来者，无所辞却。有一比丘，姿形顽陋，衣服尘敝，跋涉涂泞，来造世常。常出为作礼，命奴取水，为其洗足。比丘曰：“世常应自洗我足。”常曰：“年老疲瘵，以奴自代。”比丘不听。世常窃骂而去比丘。便见神足变身八尺，颜容瑰伟，飞行而去。世常抚膺悔叹，自扑泥中。时抵家僧尼及行路者五六十人，俱得望视，见在空中数十丈上，了了分明。奇芬异气，经月不歇。法兰即名理法师见宗者也。有记在后卷传。兰以语于弟子法阶，阶每说之，道俗多闻。珠林二十八

    Explanation

    24

    Shi Chang of Jin, a man from the state of Zhongshan, was a man of great wealth. During the reign of Emperor Tai Kang, it was forbidden for people of Jin to become monks. Shi Chang, however, was devoted to the Dharma and made diligent efforts. He secretly built a monastery in his home to support and provide for monks, and there was also the monk Falei among them. No matter who came, he did not refuse them. One day, a monk with an ugly and unattractive appearance, wearing dusty and worn-out clothes, traveled through muddy roads to visit Shi Chang. Shi Chang came out to greet him with respect and ordered his servant to fetch water to wash the monk's feet. The monk said, "Shi Chang should wash my feet himself." Shi Chang replied, "I am old and weak, so I have my servant do it." The monk would not listen. Shi Chang secretly cursed the monk and left. The monk then transformed into a figure eight feet tall, with a magnificent appearance, and flew away. Shi Chang beat his chest in regret and fell into the mud. At that time, about fifty or sixty monks, nuns, and passersby were all able to see the monk flying high in the sky, clearly visible. A strange fragrance and unusual aura lasted for months. Falei was a famous monk known as the Seer of the Dharma. There is a record of this in the subsequent volume. Falei told this to his disciple Fahjie, who often recounted it, and many people, both monastic and lay, heard it. This story is recorded in the Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest), volume twenty-eight.

    25

    晋沙门康法朗，学于中山。永嘉中，与四比丘西入天竺。行过流沙，千有余里。见道边败坏佛图，无复堂殿，蓬蒿没人。法朗等下拜瞻礼，见有二僧，各居其一：一人读经，一人患痢。秽污盈房。其读经者了不营视，朗等恻然兴念，留为煮粥，埽除浣濯。至六日，病者稍困，注痢如泉。朗等共料理之。其夜，朗等并谓病者必不移旦。至明晨往视，容色光悦，痛状休然。广记引作病状顿除屋中秽物，皆是华馨。朗等乃悟是得道冥士以试人也。病者曰：“隔房比丘，是我和尚。久得道慧，可往礼觐。”法朗等先嫌读经沙门无慈爱心，闻已乃作礼悔过。读经者曰：“诸君诚契并至，同当入道。朗公宿学业浅，此世未得愿也。”谓朗伴云：“慧此居植根深，当现世得愿。”因而留之。法朗后还中山为大法师，道俗宗之。珠林九十五广记八十九

    Explanation

    25

    During the Jin dynasty, a monk named Kang Falang studied in Zhongshan. In the Yongjia period, he traveled west with four other monks to India. They crossed the vast desert, covering more than a thousand miles. Along the way, they saw a ruined stupa by the roadside, with no remaining halls or pavilions, overgrown with weeds and grass. Kang Falang and his companions prostrated and paid homage, and they saw two monks, each in their own room: one was reading scriptures, and the other was suffering from dysentery. The room was filled with filth and excrement. The monk reading the scriptures showed no concern, but Kang Falang and his companions felt compassion and took action, staying to cook porridge and clean the room. After six days, the sick monk became increasingly weak, and his dysentery was as severe as a gushing spring. Kang Falang and his companions cared for him together. That night, they all believed the sick monk would not survive until morning. But the next morning, when they went to check on him, his face was radiant and joyful, and the pain had vanished. The house was now filled with the fragrance of flowers. Kang Falang and his companions realized that the sick monk was an enlightened being testing them. The sick monk said, "The monk in the adjacent room is my master. He has long attained wisdom and enlightenment. You should go and pay your respects." Kang Falang and his companions had previously disapproved of the monk reading scriptures for lacking compassion, but upon hearing this, they prostrated and repented. The monk reading the scriptures said, "All of you have come together with sincere faith, and you are all destined to enter the path. Master Lang's accumulated learning is shallow, and he will not attain his wish in this life." He then told Kang Falang's companion, "Master Hui has deeply rooted himself in this place and will attain his wish in this life." Therefore, he was left behind. After this, Kang Falang returned to Zhongshan and became a great master of Buddhism, revered by both monks and laypeople.

    26

    晋竺长舒者，其先西域人也。世有资货，为富人。竺居晋元康中内徙洛阳。长舒奉法精至；尤好诵观世音经。其后邻比失火。长舒家悉草屋，又正下风，自计火已逼近，政复出物，所全无几，乃敕家人不得辇物。亦无灌救者。唯至心诵经。有顷，火烧其邻屋，与长舒隔篱，而风忽自回，火亦际屋而止。于时咸以为灵。里中有轻险少年四五人，共毁笑之，云风偶自转，此复何神。伺时燥夕，当爇其屋：能令不然者，可也。其后天甚早燥。风起亦驶，少年辈密共束炬掷其屋上。三掷三灭，乃大惊惧，各走还家。明晨，相率诣长舒自说昨事，稽颡辞谢。长舒答曰：“我了无神，政诵念观世音，当是威灵所祐。诸君但当洗心信向耳。”自是邻里乡党咸敬异焉。珠林二十三

    Explanation

    26

    Zhang Shu of Jin was a descendant of people from the Western Regions. His family had long been wealthy. During the Yuan Kang period of the Jin Dynasty, he moved to Luoyang. Zhang Shu was devout and meticulous in his observance of the law, especially loving to recite the Guanyin Sutra. Later, a fire broke out in the neighborhood. Zhang Shu's house was made of thatch and was located downwind, so he thought the fire was already close. Even if he took out the goods, he could save very little, so he ordered his family not to move the goods. No one else was trying to extinguish the fire. He only recited the Guanyin Sutra with utmost sincerity. After a while, the fire burned the neighboring house, which was separated from Zhang Shu's by a fence, but the wind suddenly changed direction, and the fire stopped at the edge of the house. At that time, everyone believed it was a miraculous event. There were a few reckless young men in the neighborhood who mocked him, saying the wind just happened to turn, and what kind of divine power was this? They waited for a dry evening to burn his house: if they could prevent the fire from spreading, they would be satisfied. Later, the weather was very dry. The wind also blew strongly, and the young men secretly gathered torches and threw them onto Zhang Shu's roof. They threw three times, and each time the fire was extinguished, so they were greatly frightened and ran back to their homes. The next morning, they came together to Zhang Shu and told him about what happened last night, bowing and apologizing. Zhang Shu replied, "I have no divine power; I just recite the Guanyin Sutra, and it must be the protective power of the bodhisattva. You all should cleanse your hearts and have faith." From then on, neighbors and fellow villagers all respected and admired him. Zhu Lin 23.

    27

    晋浔阳庐山西有龙泉精舍，即慧远沙门之所立也。远始南渡，爱其区丘。欲创寺宇，未知定方。遣诸弟子访履林涧，疲息此地。群僧并渴。率同立誓曰：“若使此处，宜立精舍，当愿神力，即出佳泉。”乃以杖掘地，清泉涌出。遂畜为池。因构堂于其后。天尝亢旱，远率诸僧转海龙王经，为民祈雨。转读未毕，泉中有物，形如巨蛇，腾空而去。俄尔洪雨四澍，高下普沾。以有龙瑞，故名焉。珠林三十三

    Explanation

    27

    On the west of Mount Lu in Xunyang, Jin, there is the Longquan Hermitage, which was established by Master Huiyuan. When Master Huiyuan first moved south, he loved the terrain of this place. He wanted to build a temple but did not know the exact location. He sent his disciples to explore the woods and streams, and they became tired and rested here. All the monks were thirsty. Together they took an oath, saying, "If this place is suitable for building a hermitage, may the divine power bring forth a good spring." Then he dug with a staff, and a clear spring gushed forth. Thus they collected it into a pond and built a hall behind it. During a period of severe drought, Master Huiyuan led the monks to chant the Hai Long Wang Jing (Sea Dragon King Sutra) to pray for rain. Before the chanting was completed, there was something in the spring, shaped like a giant snake, which rose into the air and departed. Soon after, heavy rain fell from all directions, raining down on both high and low places. Because of the dragon's auspicious sign, it was named Longquan. This is recorded in Zhu Lin Thirty-Three.

    28

    晋沙门于法兰，高阳人也。十五而出家。器识沉秀，业操贞整。寺于深岩。尝夜坐禅，虎入其室；因蹲床前。兰以手摩其头。虎奋耳而伏。数日乃去。竺护，炖煌人也。风神情宇，亦兰之次。于时经典新译，梵语数多，辞句烦芜，章偈不整；乃领其旨要，刊其游文。亦养徒山中。山有清涧，汲漱所资。有采薪者，尝秽其水；水即竭涸，俄而绝流。护临涧徘徊，叹曰：“水若遂竭，吾将何资！”言终而清流洋溢，寻复盈涧。并武惠时人也。支道林为之像赞曰：“于氏超世，综体玄旨。嘉遁山泽；仁感虎兕。护公澄寂，道德渊美。微吟空涧，枯泉还水。”法苑珠林六十三

    Explanation

    28

    Yulan Fan, a monk from the Jin Dynasty, was from Gaoyang. At the age of fifteen, he left home to become a monk. He had deep insight and outstanding qualities, and his conduct was pure and upright. His temple was located in a deep cave. Once, he sat in meditation at night, and a tiger entered his room. The tiger then crouched in front of the bed. Yulan touched its head with his hand, and the tiger raised its ears and crouched down. After several days, it left.

    Zhu Hu, a native of Dunhuang, had a demeanor and appearance that were second only to Yulan. At the time, newly translated scriptures were abundant, with many Sanskrit terms. The phrases were complicated and messy, and the verses were not well-arranged. Zhu Hu edited out unnecessary words and cultivated disciples in the mountains. The mountain had a clear stream, which served as the source for drinking and washing. There was someone who cut wood and once polluted the water. The water immediately dried up, and soon after, the stream stopped flowing. Zhu Hu stood by the stream and wandered around, sighing and saying, "If the water really dries up, what will I use for drinking and washing?" After he finished speaking, the clear stream flowed abundantly, and soon the stream was full again. Both were contemporaries of Emperor Wu and Emperor Huizong. Zhi Daolin wrote an inscription for them: "Yulan transcended the world, summarizing the profound meanings. He retired to the mountains and lakes, and his kindness moved the tiger. Zhu Hu was calm and serene, with a profound and beautiful moral character. He softly sang in the empty valley, and the dried-up spring returned to flowing." From the Jewel Forest of the Dharma Garden, Chapter 63.

    29

    晋司空庐江何充，字次道，弱而信法，心业甚精。常于斋堂，置一空座，筵帐精华，络以珠宝；设之积年，庶降神异。后大会道俗，甚盛。坐次一僧，容服粗垢，神情低陋，出自众中，迳升其座，拱默而已，无所言说。一堂怪骇，谓其谬僻。充亦不平，嫌于颜色。及行中食，此僧饭于高座；饭毕，提钵出堂，顾谓充曰：“何侯徒劳精进！”因掷钵空中，陵空而去。充及道俗，驰遽观之：光仪伟丽，极目乃没。追共惋恨，稽忏累日。法苑珠林四十二

    Explanation

    29

    He Chong, the Sikan of Lujiang during the Jin Dynasty, was weak in physical strength but firm in faith, and his mind and industry were very refined. He often placed an empty seat in his study hall, adorned with fine fabrics and decorated with jewels. He had set it up for many years, hoping to attract divine or supernatural beings. Later, he held a grand assembly of both religious and secular people, which was very impressive. Suddenly, one monk came out of the crowd and directly ascended the seat, simply sitting there in silence, saying nothing. Everyone in the hall was startled, thinking he was strange or eccentric. He Chong disliked his appearance.

    When it came time for lunch, this monk ate at the high seat. After finishing his meal, he picked up his bowl and left the hall, turning to He Chong and saying, "Your Lordship has labored in vain!" Then he threw his bowl into the air and flew away. He Chong and the assembly rushed to look, and they saw a magnificent and splendid figure, which disappeared into the distance. They followed him with regret and performed penance for several days.

    30

    晋尼竺道容，不知何许人。居于乌江寺。戒行精峻，屡有征感。晋明帝时，甚见敬事。以华藉席，验其所得；果不萎焉。时简文帝事清水道；所奉之师，即京师所谓王濮阳也。弟内其道舍，容亟开化；帝未之从。其后帝每入道屋，辄见神人为沙门形，盈满室内，帝疑容所为，因事为师。遂奉正法。晋氏显尚佛道，此尼力也。当时崇异，号为圣人。新林寺即帝为容所造也。孝武初，忽而绝迹，不知所在。乃葬其衣钵。故寺边有冢在焉。珠林四十二

    Explanation

    30

    Nichiren, a nun of the Jin dynasty, was of unknown origin. She resided at the Wujiang Temple. Known for her strict and virtuous conduct, she often exhibited miraculous signs. During the reign of Emperor Ming of Jin, she was greatly respected. To test her supernatural abilities, a flower was placed on a seat; it indeed did not wither. At the time, Emperor Jianwen followed the teachings of the Clear Water School, and his teacher was known as Wang Puyang in the capital. Nichiren was invited into his hermitage and repeatedly tried to enlighten him, but the emperor did not follow her advice. Later, whenever the emperor entered the hermitage, he would always see divine beings appearing in the form of monks, filling the room. He suspected that Nichiren was responsible and thus took her as his teacher. Consequently, he followed the true Dharma. The Jin dynasty elevated Buddhism, largely due to Nichiren's efforts. She was highly revered and called a sage. Xinlin Temple was built by Emperor Xiaowu for Nichiren. At the beginning of Emperor Xiaowu's reign, Nichiren suddenly disappeared, and no one knew where she had gone. Her robes and begging bowl were buried, and a tomb can be found near the temple.

    31

    晋阙公则，赵人也。恬放萧然，唯勤法事。法事感通录引作法华。晋武之世，死于洛阳。道俗同志，为设会于白马寺中。其夕转经。宵分，闻空中有唱赞声。仰见一人，形器壮伟，仪服整丽乃言曰：“我是阙公则，今生西方安乐世界，与诸菩萨共来听经。”合堂惊跃，皆得睹见。时复有汲郡卫士度，亦苦行居士也。师于公则。其母又甚信尚，诵经长斋，家常饭僧。时日将中，母出斋堂，与诸尼僧，逍遥眺望。忽见空中有一物下，正落母前，乃则钵也；有饭盈焉，馨气充?。○堂肃然，一时礼敬。母自分行斋人食之，皆七日不饥。此钵犹云尚存此土。度善有文辞，作八关忏文。晋末斋者尚用之，晋永昌中死，亦见灵异。有浩像者作圣贤传，具载其事云。度亦生西方。吴兴王该日。烛曰：“阙夐登霄，卫度继轨。咸恬泊以无生，俱蜕骸以不死”者也。珠林四十二三宝感通录四

    Explanation

    31

    Quègōngzé of Jin, from Zhao, was a man of carefree and detached disposition, devoted only to religious practices. The Fashì Gǎntōng Lù (Records of the Marvelous Connections in Religious Practices) cites this as the Fǎhuá (Lotus Sutra). During the reign of Emperor Wu of Jin, he died in Luoyang. Both monks and laypeople who shared his faith held a gathering at the White Horse Temple. That night, they recited scriptures. At midnight, they heard a singing and praising sound in the air. Looking up, they saw a person with a majestic appearance and well-dressed attire, who then said, "I am Quègōngzé, and I have been reborn in the Western Blissful World, coming with the Bodhisattvas to listen to the sutras." Everyone in the hall was shocked and jumped up, all able to see him. There was also Wei Shìdù from Jǐ County, who was also a practicing layperson and learned from Quègōngzé. His mother was very devout, recited scriptures, observed long fasts, and regularly fed monks. One day, she went out of the斋堂, accompanied by nuns and monks, and strolled around. Suddenly, she saw something fall from the air, landing right in front of her, which was Quègōngzé's bowl; it was full of rice, and the fragrance filled the air. The hall was solemn, and everyone paid respects. She distributed the food among the monks, and all of them did not feel hungry for seven days. This bowl is said to still exist in this world. Wei Shìdù was skilled in writing and composed the Bāguān Chàn (Eight Gates Repentance) text. In the late Jin dynasty, people still used it. He died in Yongchang during the Jin dynasty and was also seen with supernatural phenomena. The Shèngxiánzhuàn (Biographies of the Saints) by Hào Xiàng records these events. Wei Shìdù also was reborn in the West. Wang Gāi of Wúxīng said on that day, "Quègōngzé ascended to heaven, and Wei Shìdù followed in his footsteps. Both were tranquil and detached, transcending life and death." Zhūlín (Jewel Forest) Vol. 42, Sānbǎo Gǎntōng Lù (Records of the Marvelous Connections of the Three Treasures) Vol. 4.

    32

    晋南阳滕普，累世敬信。妻吴郡全氏，尤能精苦。每设斋会，不逆招请；随有来者，因留供之。后会僧数阙少，使人衢路要寻。见一沙门，荫柳而坐，因请与归。净人行食，翻饭于地；倾箪都尽，罔然无计。此沙门云：“贫道钵中有饭，足供一众。”使普分行，既而道俗内外，皆得充饱。清净既毕，掷钵空中，翻然上升。极目乃灭。普即刻木作其形像，朝夕拜礼。普家将有凶祸，则此像必先倒踣云。普子含，以苏峻之功封东兴者也。珠林四十二

    Explanation

    32

    During the Jin Dynasty, there was a man named Teng Pu from Nanyang who had many generations of reverence and faith. His wife, Quan from Wu County, was especially devoted and could endure great hardships. They often set up vegetarian feasts without actively inviting guests; whenever someone came, they would invite them to stay and be served. One day, when they were hosting a gathering for monks and there were not enough of them, they sent someone to the road to look for more. They saw a monk sitting under a willow tree, so they invited him to return with them. When the servant was serving food, he accidentally spilled it on the ground, completely emptying the basket, leaving them helpless and without a plan. The monk said, "This humble monk has food in his bowl that is enough to feed everyone." They had the monk distribute the food, and afterward, both the monks and laypeople inside and outside the gathering were fully satisfied. After the meal, the monk threw his bowl into the air and ascended into the sky, disappearing from sight. Teng Pu then carved a wooden statue of the monk and worshipped it daily. Whenever Teng Pu's family was about to face misfortune, the statue would fall over first. Teng Pu's son, Han, was granted the title of Dongxing for his military achievements against Su Jun. This story is recorded in Zhu Lin Volume 42.

    33

    沙门竺法进者，开度浮图主也。聪达多知，能解殊俗之言。京洛将乱，欲处山泽。众人请留，进皆不听。大会烧香，与众告别。临当布香，忽有一僧来，处上座：衣服尘垢，面目黄肿。法进怪贱，牵就下次；辄复来上。牵之至三，乃不复见。众坐既定，方就下食，忽暴风扬沙，柈桉倾倒。法进忏悔自责；乃止不入山。时论以为：世将大乱，法进不宜入山。又道俗至意，苦相留慕，故见此神异，止其行意也。珠林四十二

    Explanation

    33

    The Monk Zhu Fa Jin, the head of the Kai Du Floating Pagoda, was intelligent, knowledgeable, and capable of understanding foreign languages. As the capital city was about to face turmoil, he wished to live in the mountains and wilderness. The people asked him to stay, but he refused to listen. He held a grand gathering where incense was burned, and he bid farewell to the crowd. Just as he was about to distribute the incense, a monk suddenly appeared and sat in the upper seat. His clothes were dusty and dirty, and his face was yellow and swollen. Zhu Fa Jin found him strange and lowly and pulled him to a lower seat. However, the monk repeatedly returned to the upper seat. Zhu Fa Jin pulled him three times before he disappeared. Once the crowd had settled down, Zhu Fa Jin only then ate at the lower seat. Suddenly, a strong wind blew sand, and the trays and tables tipped over. Zhu Fa Jin repented and blamed himself, and then stopped and did not enter the mountains. People at the time believed that the world was about to be in great turmoil, and Zhu Fa Jin should not enter the mountains. Both Buddhist monks and laypeople who were deeply concerned earnestly tried to persuade and admire him, and therefore, this supernatural event occurred to stop his intention to leave. (From Zhu Lin, Chapter 42)

    34

    晋周闵，汝南人也。晋护军将军。家世奉法。苏峻之乱，都邑人士，皆东西波迁。广记引作播迁闵家有大品一部，以半幅八丈素反覆书之。又有余经数台，大品亦杂在其中。既当避难，单行不能得尽持去；尤惜大品，不知在何台中。仓卒应去，不展寻搜，广记引无此句徘徊叹吒。不觉大品忽自出外。闵惊喜持去。周氏遂世宝之。今云尚在。一说云：周嵩妇胡母氏，有素书大品。素广五寸，而大品一部尽在焉。又并有舍利，银罂贮之。并缄于深箧。永嘉之乱，胡母将避兵南奔，经及舍利，自出箧外。因取怀之。以渡江东。又尝遇火，不暇取经。及屋尽火灭，得之于灰尽之下，俨然如故。会稽王道子就嵩，曾云求以供养。后尝蹔在新渚寺。刘敬叔云，曾亲见此经：字如麻大，巧密分明。新渚寺，今天安是也。此经盖得道僧释慧则所写也。或云，尝在简靖寺，靖首尼读。珠林十八广记一百十三

    Explanation

    34

    A Man Named Zhou Min from Ruyang

    Zhou Min was a man from Ruyang during the Jin dynasty, holding the title of Guardian Army General. His family had always adhered to the law. During the rebellion led by Su Jun, people from the capital cities all moved east and west. Zhou Min's family had a complete set of the Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra, written back and forth on a half-width eight-zhang piece of white silk. They also had several other scriptures, with the Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra mixed among them. When they had to flee, they could not take everything with them; they especially cherished the Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra and did not know which scroll it was in. In the hurry of departure, they could not thoroughly search, and Zhou Min wandered about, sighing and murmuring. Suddenly, the Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra appeared outside. Zhou Min was overjoyed and took it with him. The Zhou family thus treasured it for generations, and it is said to still be in existence. Another account says: Zhou Song's wife, Lady Humu, had a white silk-written Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra. The silk was five inches wide, and the entire Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra was written on it. It also contained relics, stored in a silver vessel, sealed in a deep chest. During the rebellion of the Western Jin dynasty, Lady Humu fled south to avoid the war. The scripture and relics spontaneously appeared outside the chest. She took them in her arms and crossed the river eastward. She once encountered a fire, and when the house was destroyed and the fire extinguished, she found them under the ashes, still as they were. The Prince of Kuaiji, Daozi, once sought to obtain them for worship. Later, the scripture was temporarily kept at New Zhu Temple. Liu Jingshu said he once saw this scripture personally: the characters were as large as hemp, intricately and clearly written. New Zhu Temple is now known as Tian'an Temple. This scripture was written by the monk Hui Ze. It is also said that it was once kept at Jianjing Temple, where it was read by the nun Jingshou.

    35

    晋史世光者，襄阳人也。咸和八年，于武昌死。七日，沙门支法山转小品，疲而微卧。闻灵座上，如有人声。史家有婢，字张信，见世光在灵上着衣帢，具如平生。语信云：“我本应堕龙中，广记引作狱中支和尚为我转经，昙护昙坚迎我上第七梵天快乐处矣。护坚并是山之沙弥，已亡者也。后支法山复往为转大品，又来在坐。世光生时，以二旛供养。时在寺中。乃呼张信持旛送我。信曰“诺，”便绝死。将信持旛，俱西北飞上一青山。上如?璃色。到山顶，望见天门，世光乃自提旛，遣信令还；与一青香，如巴豆，曰：“以上支和尚。”信未还，便遥见世光直入天门。信复道而还，倏忽醒活；亦不复见手中香也；旛亦故在寺中。

    Explanation

    35

    Jin Shi Shiguang, a man from Xiangyang, died in Wuchang in the eighth year of Xianhe (333 AD). Seven days later, the monk Zhi Fashan chanted the shorter sutra, growing tired and taking a slight nap. He heard what seemed like human voices coming from the spirit seat. A servant of the Shishi household, named Zhang Xin, saw Shiguang on the spirit seat, dressed and wearing a hat, just as he had been in life. Shiguang spoke to Zhang Xin, saying, "I was originally destined to fall into the dragon realm, but the monk Zhi Fashan chanted sutras for me, and the deceased monks Tan Hu and Tan Jian welcomed me to the seventh level of the heavenly realm, a place of great joy. Tan Hu and Tan Jian were both novices of Zhi Fashan and have since passed away. Later, Zhi Fashan returned to chant the longer sutra, and came back to sit with us. When I was alive, I offered two banners as a gift. At that time, they were in the temple. I called Zhang Xin to take the banners and send me off. Zhang Xin said, 'Yes,' and then died. I took Zhang Xin with me, holding the banners, and we flew northwest to a green mountain. The mountain was like lapis lazuli in color. When we reached the summit, I saw the gate to heaven. I took the banners and sent Zhang Xin back, giving him a green incense that looked like the fruit of the castor oil plant, and said, 'Offer this to the monk Zhi Fashan.' Before Zhang Xin returned, I saw Shiguang enter the gate to heaven directly. Zhang Xin returned by the same path and suddenly woke up alive; he no longer saw the incense in his hand, but the banners were still in the temple.

    36

    世光与信，于家去时，其六岁儿见之，指语祖母曰：“阿爷飞上天，婆为见不？”世光后复与天人十余，俱还其家，徘徊而去。每来必见簪帢，去必露髻。信问之。答曰：“天上有冠，不着此也。”后乃着天冠与群天神，鼓琴行歌，经上母堂。信问何用屡来。曰，“我来，欲使汝辈知罪福也；亦兼娱乐阿母。”琴音清妙，不类世声；家人大小，悉得闻之。然闻其声，如隔壁障，不得亲察也。唯信闻之，独分明焉。有顷去，信自送。广记引有送字见世光入一黑门，有顷来出，广记引作寻即出来谓信曰：“舅在此，日见榜挞，楚痛难胜。省视还也。舅生犯杀罪，故受此报。可告舅母：会僧转经，当稍免脱。”舅即轻车将军报终也。珠林五广记一百十二

    Explanation

    36

    Shi Guang and Xin were leaving home when their six-year-old son saw something and pointed to his grandmother, saying, "Grandfather is flying to heaven, can you see him?" Later, Shi Guang returned with more than ten celestial beings, all of whom went back to his home and lingered before leaving. Every time they came, they wore hairpins and hats, but when they left, their hair was uncovered. Xin asked them why. They replied, "In heaven, there are crowns, so we don't wear these." Afterward, they wore heavenly crowns and accompanied a group of divine beings, playing the lute and singing as they walked past the mother's room. Xin asked why they came so often. They said, "We come to make you all understand the consequences of good and evil deeds; we also come to entertain the grandmother." The sound of the lute was clear and exquisite, unlike the sounds of this world; all the family members could hear it. However, the sound was like hearing through a wall, and they could not see them clearly. Only Xin could hear it distinctly. After a while, they left, and Xin accompanied them. In the Extensive Records, it mentions the word "send" and describes Shi Guang entering a black gate. After a while, he came out and said to Xin, "Uncle is here, and he is beaten daily, suffering unbearable pain. I will visit and return. Uncle committed a murder, so he is receiving this punishment. Tell Aunt that gathering monks to recite sutras will gradually alleviate his suffering." The uncle was the General of Light Chariots, and this is the end of his story. This is recorded in Zhu Lin Volume Five and Extensive Records Chapter One Hundred and Twelve.

    37

    晋张应者，历阳人。本事俗神，鼓舞淫祀。咸和八年，移居芜湖。妻得病。应请祷备至，财产略尽。妻，法家弟子也，谓曰：“今病日困，求鬼无益，乞作佛事。”应许之。往精舍中，见竺昙铠。昙铠曰：“佛如愈病之药。见药不服，虽视无益。”应许当事佛。昙铠与期明日往斋。应归，夜梦见一人，长丈余，从南来。入门曰：“汝家狼藉，乃尔不净。”见昙铠随后，曰：“始欲发意，未可责之。”应先巧眠觉，便炳火作高座，及鬼子母座。昙铠明往，应具说梦。遂受五戒。斥除神影，大设福供。妻病即闲，寻都除愈。咸康二年，应至马沟籴盐。还泊芜湖浦宿。梦见三人，以○钩钩之。应曰：“我佛弟子。”牵终不置，曰：“奴叛走多时。

    Explanation

    37

    Zhang Ying of the Jin dynasty was from Lüyang. He used to serve the vulgar gods and engage in licentious rituals. In the eighth year of the Xianhe era (333 CE), he moved to Wuhu. His wife fell ill. Zhang Ying prayed fervently and spent all his wealth on offerings. His wife, a follower of the Legalist school, said to him, "Now my illness is worsening, praying to the gods is of no benefit. Please perform Buddhist rites." Zhang Ying agreed. He went to a temple and met Zhi Tan Kai. Zhi Tan Kai said, "The Buddha is like medicine that cures illness. Seeing medicine but not taking it, even though looking at it is of no benefit." Zhang Ying agreed to follow Buddhist practices. Zhi Tan Kai set a date for the next day to conduct the rites. That night, Zhang Ying had a dream where a man over ten feet tall came from the south and entered the house, saying, "Your home is in disarray and not clean enough." He saw Zhi Tan Kai following and said, "You have just started to have an intention, so you cannot be blamed." Zhang Ying woke up and immediately lit a fire and prepared a high seat and a seat for the Ghost Mother. The next day, Zhi Tan Kai arrived, and Zhang Ying told him about the dream. He then received the Five Precepts. He expelled the influence of the gods and made a great offering of merit. His wife's illness improved and soon she was completely cured. In the second year of the Xiankang era (336 CE), Zhang Ying went to Magou to buy salt. On his return, he stopped at the Wuhu harbor to spend the night. He dreamed of three people who hooked him with a hook. He said, "I am a disciple of the Buddha." They continued to pull him, saying, "A slave has run away for a long time."

    38

    ”应怖谓曰：“放我，当与君一升酒调。”乃放之。谓应，但畏后人复取汝耳。眠觉，腹痛泄痢；达家大困。应与昙铠，问绝已久。病甚，遣呼之。适值不在。应寻气绝。经日而稣活。说有数人以○钩钩将北去。下一阪岸。岸下见有镬汤刀剑，楚毒之具。应时悟是地狱。欲呼师名，忘昙铠字，但唤“和上救我！”亦时唤佛。有顷，一人从西面来，形长丈余，执金杵，欲撞此钩人，曰：“佛弟子也，何入此中？”钩人怖散。长人引应去，谓曰：“汝命已尽，不复久生。可蹔还家。颂呗三偈，并取和上名字，三日当复命过，即生天矣。”应既稣，即复怵然。既而三日，持斋颂呗，遣人疏取昙铠名。至日中，食毕，礼佛读呗，遍与家人辞别。澡洗着衣，如眠便尽。珠林六十二

    Explanation

    38

    Ying Bo said to him, "Let me go, and I will give you a measure of wine." The person released him. He told Ying Bo, "I am only afraid that someone else will take you." After sleeping, he felt abdominal pain and diarrhea; he was very weak when he returned home. Ying Bo and Tan Kai had been out of touch for a long time. He was very ill and sent for him, but he happened to be away. Ying Bo soon died. After a day, he revived. He said that several people were dragging him north with hooks. They descended to a slope by the bank. At the bottom of the bank, there were cauldrons of boiling water, swords, and instruments of torment. Ying Bo realized he was in hell. He wanted to call out his teacher's name but forgot Tan Kai's name. He only called out, "Save me, Venerable One!" and also called out to the Buddha. After a while, a man came from the west, over ten feet tall, holding a golden pestle. He was about to strike the people with hooks, saying, "You are a disciple of the Buddha, why are you here?" The people with hooks were terrified and scattered. The tall man led Ying Bo away and said, "Your life is over, you will not live long. You can return home temporarily. Recite three verses of chanting and mention your teacher's name. In three days, you will be reborn in heaven." After reviving, Ying Bo was once again terrified. After three days, he observed a fast, recited chants, and had someone write down Tan Kai's name. At noon, after eating, he paid respects to the Buddha, recited chants, and bid farewell to his family. He bathed, dressed, and then died as if falling asleep. Zhu Lin volume 62.

    39

    晋董吉者，于潜人也。奉法三世，至吉尤精进。恒斋戒诵首楞严经。屯中有病，辄请吉读经；所救多愈。同县何晃者，亦奉法士也。咸和中，卒得山毒之病，守困。晃兄惶遽，驰往请吉。董何两舍，相去六七十里。复隔大溪，五月中，大雨。晃兄初渡时，水尚未至。吉与期设中食后。此字广记引有比往而山水暴涨，不复可涉，吉不能泅；迟回叹息；坐岸良久；欲下不敢渡。吉既信直。必欲赴期。乃恻然发心，自誓曰：“吾救人苦急，不计躯命。克冀如来大士，当照乃诚。”便脱衣，以囊经戴置头上，迳入水中，量其深浅，乃应至颈。及吉渡，正着膝耳。既得上岸，失囊经，甚惋恨。进至晃家，三礼忏悔，流涕自责。俯仰之闲，便见经囊在高座上。吉悲喜取看，邑邑如有湿气。开囊视经，尚燥如故。

    Explanation

    39

    During the Jin Dynasty, there was a man named Dong Ji from Yuchen. He had been practicing the Dharma for three generations, and by the time of Ji, his devotion was especially deep. He constantly observed斋戒 and recited the Shou Leng Yan Jing (Surangama Sutra). When someone in the village was sick, they would always invite Ji to read the sutras, and most of those he helped recovered. There was also a man named He Huang from the same county who was also a practitioner of the Dharma. During the Xianhe period, He suddenly contracted a poisonous mountain illness and became severely ill and bedridden. His brother, in great distress, rushed to ask Ji for help. The distance between Dong and He's homes was about sixty to seventy li, separated by a large river. In the middle of May, heavy rain fell. When He's brother first crossed the river, the water had not yet risen. Ji agreed to meet after midday meal. However, as they were about to leave, the mountain torrent suddenly rose, and it was no longer possible to cross. Ji could not swim, so he hesitated and sighed, sitting by the riverbank for a long time, wanting to go down but daring not to cross. Ji, being honest and straightforward, determined to keep his appointment. Feeling compassion, he made a vow to himself, saying, "I will save people in their time of urgent suffering, regardless of my own life. I hope the Buddha or Bodhisattva will grant me this wish and illuminate my sincerity." He then took off his clothes, placed the bag containing the sutra on his head, and directly entered the water, measuring the depth, which should have reached up to his neck. When Ji crossed, it only reached his knees. After successfully crossing the river, he lost the bag containing the sutra and was very regretful. He went to He's house, performed three prostrations and repentance, shed tears, and blamed himself. In a moment, he suddenly saw the bag containing the sutra on the high seat. Ji took it with a mix of sadness and joy, noting that it seemed damp and discolored. When he opened the bag and saw the sutra, it was still dry as before.

    40

    于是屯人，一时奉法。吉所居西北，有一山，高峻，中多妖魅，犯害居民。吉以经戒之力，欲伐降之。于山际四五亩地，手伐林木，构造小屋，安设高座，转首楞严经。百余日中，寂然无闻。民害稍止。后有数人至吉所，语言良久。吉思惟此客言者，非于潜人；穹山幽绝，何因而来；疑是鬼神；乃谓之曰：“诸君得无是此中鬼耶？”答曰：“是也。闻君德行清肃，故来相观。并请一事，想必见听。吾世有此山，游居所托。君既来止，虑相逆冒，恒怀不安。今欲更作界分，当杀树为断。”吉曰：“仆贪此静寂。读诵经典，不相干犯。方为卿比，广记引作方喜为此愿见祐助。”鬼答：“亦复凭君，不见侵克也。”言毕而去。经一宿，前芟地，四际之外，树皆枯死，如火烧状。吉年八十七亡。珠林十八广记一百十二

    Explanation

    40

    At that time, the people gathered and obeyed the law. Ji lived in the northwest, where there was a high and steep mountain with many demons and spirits that harmed the residents. Ji used the power of the scriptures and precepts to subdue them. He cleared a small area of land, built a small house, set up a high seat, and recited the Shurangama Sutra. For over a hundred days, there was no sound or disturbance, and the harm to the people gradually ceased. Later, several people came to Ji's place and spoke with him for a long time. Ji thought that the guests were not from the local area, wondering how they came to this remote and secluded mountain. He suspected they were ghosts or spirits and said to them, "Are you perhaps ghosts from this mountain?" They replied, "Yes, we are. We have heard of your virtuous and pure conduct, so we came to observe you. We also request one thing, which we hope you will grant. We have lived in this mountain for generations, using it as our home. Since you have come to live here, we fear we might offend you and are always uneasy. Now we want to make a boundary, and we will cut down trees to mark it." Ji said, "I love this quiet place and read scriptures here; I do not interfere with anyone. I am glad to help you and wish to see your wishes fulfilled." The ghosts replied, "We also rely on you and will not invade or harm you." They finished speaking and left. After one night, the trees outside the cleared area withered and died, as if burned. Ji died at the age of 87. Zhu Lin volume 18, Guang Ji volume 112.

    41

    晋周珰者，会稽剡人也。家世奉法。珰年十六，便菜食持斋，讽诵成具。及顷转经。正月长斋，竟延僧设，受八关斋。至乡市寺，请其师竺僧密及支法阶竺佛密，令持小品，斋日转读。至日，三僧赴斋，忘持小品。至中食毕。欲读经，方忆。意甚惆怅。珰家在阪怡屯，去寺三十里，无人遣取。至人定烧香讫，举家恨不得经。密益踧踖。有顷，闻有叩门者，言送小品。珰愕然心喜。开门，见一年少，着单衣?，先所不识，又非人行。时疑其神异，便长跪受经，要使前坐。年少不进，期夜当来听经。比道人出，忽不复见。香气遍一宅中。既而视之，乃密经也。道俗惊喜。密经先在厨中，缄钥甚谨。还视其钥，俨然如故。于是屯中十余家，咸皆奉佛。益敬爱珰。珰遂出家，字昙嶷。讽诵众经，至二十万言。珠林十八广记一百十

    Explanation

    41

    Zhou Dang of the Jin dynasty was a native of Yandian, Kuaiji. His family had always adhered to the precepts. At the age of sixteen, he began to follow a vegetarian diet and fast, reciting scriptures thoroughly. As time passed, he also started to recite scriptures. During the first month, he observed a long fast and invited monks to set up a ceremony for the Eight Precepts. He invited his teachers Zhi Sengmi, Zhi Fahai, and Zhi Fomi to come and recite the Small Sutra on the day of the fast. On the day of the fast, the three monks arrived for the ceremony, but forgot to bring the Small Sutra. After the midday meal, when they were about to read the scriptures, they suddenly remembered. They felt very distressed. Zhou Dang's home was in Ban Yi Tun, thirty li away from the temple, and no one was sent to fetch the Small Sutra. By the time of evening incense burning, the whole family regretted not having the scriptures. The monks felt even more uneasy. After a while, they heard someone knocking on the door, saying they had brought the Small Sutra. Zhou Dang was surprised and delighted. He opened the door and saw a young man dressed in a simple robe, someone he had never seen before, and not someone who usually traveled. He suspected it might be a divine or supernatural being and knelt down to receive the scriptures, inviting him to sit. The young man did not move forward, promising to come back at night to listen to the scriptures. By the time the monks left, the young man had disappeared. The fragrance filled the entire house. When they looked at the scriptures, it was indeed the Small Sutra. The monks and laypeople were amazed. The Small Sutra had been kept in the kitchen, sealed and locked very carefully. When they checked the lock, it was still intact. Thus, more than ten families in the village began to follow Buddhism and respected and loved Zhou Dang. Zhou Dang eventually left home to become a monk, taking the name Tan Yi. He recited and memorized many scriptures, totaling over 200,000 words. This story is recorded in Chapter 18 of the Zhu Lin and Chapter 110 of the Guang Ji.

    42

    晋孙稚，字法晖，齐国般阳县人也。父祚，晋太中大夫。稚幼而奉法。年十八，以咸康元年八月病亡。祚后移居武昌。至三年四月八日，沙门于法阶行尊像，经家门。夫妻大小出观，见稚亦在人众之中，随侍像行。见父母，拜跪问讯。随共还家。祚先病，稚云：“无他祸祟，不自将护所致耳。五月当差。”言毕辞去。其年七月十五日，复归，跪拜问讯，悉如生时。说其外祖父为太山府君，见稚，说稚母字曰，“汝是某甲儿耶。”“未应便来，那得至此。”稚答：“伯父将来。欲以代谴。”有教推问。欲鞭罚之；稚救解得原。稚兄容，字思渊，时在其侧。稚谓曰：“虽离故形在优乐处，但读书无他作，愿兄勿复忧也。

    Explanation

    42

    Translation:

    Jin Sun Zhi, courtesy name Fa Hui, was from Bangyang County in Qi State. His father, Zuò, held the position of Taizhong Dafu in the Jin court. Sun Zhi was obedient to the law from a young age. At eighteen, he died in August of the first year of Xiankang (335 AD). After his death, Zuò moved to Wuchang. In the third year, on the eighth day of the fourth month, a Buddhist monk performed a ritual involving a revered statue and passed by their home. Sun Zhi appeared among the crowd, following the statue. He saw his parents, bowed and greeted them. They returned home together. Zuò had fallen ill, and Sun Zhi said, "There are no other calamities; it's just that I did not take proper care of myself. I will be better by May." After speaking, he left. On the fifteenth day of the seventh month of that year, he returned, bowed and greeted, behaving as he did when alive. He said that his maternal grandfather was the Lord of Tai Shan, who saw Sun Zhi and asked, "Are you the son of someone named so-and-so?" "You shouldn't be here yet; how did you get here?" Sun Zhi replied, "My uncle will come; he wants to take my place." There was an order to investigate and punish him, but Sun Zhi was saved from punishment. His brother, Róng, courtesy name Siyuan, was present at the time. Sun Zhi said to him, "Although I have left my old form and am in a place of joy, I only read and do nothing else. I hope you will not worry further."

    43

    但勤精进，系念修善，福自随人矣。我二年学成，当生国王家。同辈有五百人，今在福堂，学成皆当上生第六天上。我本亦应上生，但以解救先人，因缘缠缚，故独生王家耳！”到五年七月七日，复归。说邾城当有寇难。事例甚多，悉皆如言。家人秘之，故无传者。又云：“先人多有罪?，宜为作福。我今受身人中，不须复营，但救先人也。愿父兄勤为功德。作福食时，务使鲜洁。一一如法者，受上福；次者，次福；若不能然，然后费设耳。当使平等，心无彼我，其福乃多。”祚时有婢，稚未还时，忽病殆死，周身皆痛。稚云：“此婢欲叛我，前与鞭，不复得去耳。推问婢，”云：“前实欲叛，与人为期日垂至而便住，”云云。珠林九十一

    Explanation

    43

    But if one diligently progresses and keeps the mind focused on cultivating virtue, good fortune will naturally follow the person. I will complete my studies in two years and be born into the king's family. My peers, numbering five hundred, are now in the Hall of Bliss, and upon completing their studies, they will all ascend to the Sixth Heaven. I should have also ascended, but because I was bound by karmic ties to save my ancestors, I was reborn alone in the king's family! On the fifth year, the seventh day of the seventh month, I returned. I said that the city of Zhuzhou would face a threat of invasion. There were many examples of this, and all came true. The family kept it secret, so it was not widely known. It was also said: "My ancestors have many sins; it is appropriate to make merit for them. I am now born into the human world, and there is no need to make further efforts, but to save my ancestors. I hope my father and elder brothers diligently make merit and virtue. When making offerings, ensure that the food is fresh and clean. Those who strictly follow the rules will receive the highest blessings; those who do so moderately will receive lesser blessings; if they cannot do so, then it is acceptable to make offerings as they can. It should be done with equality, without distinguishing between self and others, and the blessings will be abundant." When Zuo had a maid, who was ill and nearly died before returning, her whole body was in pain. Zuo said: "This maid wanted to rebel against me, and before she could, I lashed her, and she could not leave. When I questioned the maid, she said: 'Before, I really wanted to rebel, and I had made an agreement with someone, but I stopped just as the day was about to arrive.' So on and so forth. Zhu Lin 91

    44

    晋李恒，字元文，谯国人。少时，有一沙门造恒，谓曰：“君福报将至，而复对来随之。君能守贫修道，不仕宦者，福增对灭。君其勉之！”恒性躁，又寒门，但问仕当何所至，了不寻究修道意也。与一卷经，恒不肯取。又固问，荣途贵贱何如？沙门曰：“当带金紫，极于三郡。若能于一郡止者，亦为善也。”恒曰：“且当富贵，何顾后患？”因留宿。恒夜起，见沙门身满一床，入呼家人，大小窥视，复变为大鸟，跱屋梁上。天晓，复形而去。恒送出门，忽不复见。知是神人。因此事佛，而亦不能精至。后为西阳、江夏、庐江太守，加龙骧将军。大兴中，预钱凤之乱，被诛。珠林五十六

    Explanation

    44

    Li Heng of the Jin dynasty, courtesy name Yuanwen, was from Qiao. In his youth, a Buddhist monk visited him and said, "Your good fortune is about to come, but negative consequences will follow. If you can live in poverty and cultivate the Dao, and avoid holding an official position, your good fortune will increase and negative consequences will diminish. Strive for this!" Li Heng was impetuous and came from a poor family. He only asked about his prospects in government service and did not delve into the meaning of cultivating the Dao. The monk gave him a scroll of scripture, but Li Heng refused to take it. The monk persisted and asked, "What will be your status in the ranks of nobility?" The monk replied, "You will hold high office, reaching the level of a governor in three prefectures. If you can limit yourself to one prefecture, that would be good." Li Heng said, "Let's pursue wealth and status first; why worry about future troubles?" He then stayed overnight. That night, Li Heng woke up and saw the monk's body filling the bed. He called his family, and they all peeked in, only to see the monk transform into a large bird perched on the roof beam. At dawn, the monk returned to his original form and left. Li Heng saw him off at the door, and suddenly, the monk disappeared. Li Heng realized he was a divine being. Thereafter, he devoted himself to Buddhism, but did not achieve great depth or purity. Later, he became the governor of Xiyang, Jiangxia, and Lujiang, and was promoted to the rank of Longxiang General. During the Daxing era, he participated in the rebellion led by Qian Feng and was executed. (Chapter 56 of the Zhu Jin)

    晋窦传者，河内人也。永和中，并州刺史高昌，冀州刺史吕护，各权部曲，相与不和。传为昌所用，作官长。护遣骑抄击，为所俘执。同伴六七人，共系入一狱。锁械甚严。克日当煞之。沙门支道山，时在护营中。先与传相识。闻其执厄，出至狱所候视之。隔户共语。传谓山曰：“今日困厄，命在漏刻，何方相救？”山曰：“若能至心归请，必有感应。”传先亦颇闻观世音，及得山语，○专心属念。昼夜三日，至诚自归。观其锁械如觉缓，解有异于常。

    Explanation

    45

    Duan Chuan, a man from Hebei, was during the Yonghe period. Gao Chang, the governor of Bingzhou, and Lü Hu, the governor of Jizhou, each controlled their own troops and were not in harmony with each other. Duan Chuan was appointed as an official by Gao Chang. Lü Hu sent riders to attack, and Duan Chuan was captured. He was imprisoned with six or seven companions in a single jail. The chains and shackles were very tight, and he was scheduled to be executed on a fixed day. The Buddhist monk Zhi Daoshan, who was at that time in Lü Hu's camp, had previously known Duan Chuan. Hearing of his predicament, he went to the prison to visit him. They spoke through the door. Duan Chuan told Zhi Daoshan, "Today I am in dire straits, my life is in the balance, what can you do to save me?" Zhi Daoshan said, "If you can sincerely pray for help, there will surely be a response." Duan Chuan had previously heard of Guanyin and, upon hearing Zhi Daoshan's words, focused his mind on this. For three days and nights, he sincerely returned to himself. It seemed as though his chains felt looser, and there was something unusual about the release.

    46

    聊试推荡，忽然离体。传乃复至心曰：“今蒙哀祐，已令桎梏自解。而同伴尚多，无心独去。观世音神力普济，当令俱免。”言毕，复牵挽余人，皆以次解落，若有割剔之者。遂开门走出，于警徼之闲，莫有觉者。便踰城迳去。时夜向晓，行四五里。天明不复进。共逃隐一榛中。须臾，觉失囚，人马络绎，四出寻捕。焚草践林，无不至遍。唯传所隐一亩许地，终无至者。遂得免还。乡里敬信异常，咸皆奉法。道山后过江，为谢居士敷具说其事。珠林十七
    　　晋大司马桓温，末年颇奉佛法，饭馔僧尼。有一比丘尼，失其名，来自远方，投温为檀越尼。才行不恒，温甚敬待，居之门内。尼每浴，必至移时。温疑而窥之：见尼裸身挥刀，破腹出脏，断截身首，支分脔切。温怪骇而还。及至尼出浴室，身形如常。温以实问。尼答云：“若遂淩君上，刑当如之。”时温方谋问鼎，闻之怅然。故以戒惧，终守臣节。尼后解去，不知所在。珠林三十三

    Explanation

    46

    A tentative push was made, and suddenly the body was separated. The transmission then returned to the heart and said, "Now we are favored by mercy and protection, and the shackles have naturally loosened. There are still many companions, and there is no desire to leave alone. The power of Guanyin to universally save all beings will surely make all of us escape." After speaking, they again pulled and led others, all gradually being released, as if someone were cutting or removing them. They then opened the door and walked out, in the midst of the watchmen, and no one noticed. They leaped over the wall and went straight away. It was late at night, nearing dawn, and they walked four or five miles. At dawn, they stopped moving forward. Together, they fled and hid in a thicket. Soon, they realized the prisoners were missing, and people and horses came in a continuous stream, searching and capturing everywhere, burning grass and trampling through forests, no place was left unsearched. Only the place where they were hidden, about an acre in size, was not reached. Thus they were able to escape and return. The village respected and believed in them exceptionally, all followed the law. After crossing the river, they went to the mountain, and for the layman named Xie, they prepared and recounted the story. Jewel Forest Seventeen

    In the late years, the Grand Marshal of Jin, Huán Wēn, was quite devoted to Buddhism, providing food and drink to monks and nuns. There was a nun, whose name is unknown, who came from afar and sought Huán Wēn as a benefactor. Her behavior was not constant, but Huán Wēn held her in high regard and allowed her to reside within his household. The nun would bathe, and it would take a long time. Huán Wēn, suspicious, peered at her: he saw the nun naked, wielding a knife, cutting open her abdomen, removing her organs, severing her head and body, and slicing them into pieces. Huán Wēn was startled and returned. When the nun emerged from the bath, her body was as usual. Huán Wēn asked her about it. The nun replied, "If I were to defy the ruler, the punishment would be the same." At the time, Huán Wēn was plotting to usurp the throne, and upon hearing this, he was filled with regret. Thus, he was warned and ultimately maintained his loyalty to his duties. The nun later left, and her whereabouts are unknown. Jewel Forest Thirty-Three

    宋案当作晋广记引无李清者，吴兴于潜人也。仕桓温大司马府参军督护。于府得病，还家而死。经久稣活。说云：初见传教，持信旛唤之，云公欲相见。清谓是温召，即起束带而去。出门，见一竹舆，便令入中。二人推之，疾速如驰。至一朱门，见阮敬；时敬死已三十年矣。敬问清曰：“卿何时来？知我家何似？”清云：“卿家异恶。”敬便雨泪，言，“知吾子孙如何？”答云：“具可。”敬云：二字广记引有“我今令卿得脱。汝能料理吾家否？”清云：“若能如此，不负大恩。”敬言，“僧达道人，是官师，甚被礼，敬当苦告之。”还内良久，遣人出云：“门前四层寺，官所起也。僧达常以平旦入寺礼拜，宜就求哀。”清往其寺，见一沙门，语曰：“汝是我前七生时弟子。已经七世受福，迷着世乐，忘失本业。背正就邪，当受大罪，今可改悔。

    Explanation

    47

    The Song case is recorded in the Jin Guang Ji but does not mention Li Qing. Li Qing was from Wuxing, Yuqian. He served as a military officer in the Grand Marshal's office under the Eastern Jin dynasty. While in the office, he fell ill, returned home, and died. After a long time, he was revived. He recounted: "I first encountered a missionary, who held a flag of faith and called to me, saying that the Grand Marshal wished to see me. I thought it was a summons from Grand Marshal Wen, so I immediately put on my belt and went. Outside the door, I saw a bamboo sedan chair and was told to get in. Two people pushed it, and it moved as swiftly as a galloping horse. We arrived at a red gate, where I saw Ruan Jing; at that time, Ruan Jing had been dead for thirty years. Ruan Jing asked Li Qing, 'When did you come? How is my family?' Li Qing replied, 'Your family is strange and unpleasant.' Ruan Jing then wept, saying, 'Do you know how my descendants are?' Li Qing answered, 'All is well.' Ruan Jing said, 'I will now allow you to escape. Can you manage my family?' Li Qing said, 'If you can do this, I will not betray your great kindness.' Ruan Jing said, 'Monk Da is an official teacher, highly respected. I will plead with him on your behalf.' After a long time inside, someone sent out a message saying, 'There is a four-story temple at the gate, built by the government. Monk Da often enters the temple to worship at dawn. You should go there to seek his pity.' Li Qing went to the temple and saw a monk, who said to him, 'You were my disciple in my previous seven lives. You have already received blessings in seven lives, but you are attached to worldly pleasures and have forgotten your true purpose. Turning away from righteousness and towards evil, you will suffer great sin. Now you can repent.'
