    和尚明出，当相佐助。”清还先舆中。夜寒噤冻。至晓门开，僧达果出至寺。清便随逐稽颡。僧达云：“汝当革心为善，归命佛法，归命比丘僧：受此三归，可得不横死。受持勤者，亦不，经苦难。”清便奉受。又见昨所遇沙门，长跪请曰：“此人僧乎宿世弟子。案乎字有讹广记引作达亦非忘正失法。方将○苦。先缘所追。今得归命，愿垂慈愍。”答曰：“先是福人，当易拔济耳。”便还向朱门。俄遣人出云：“李参军可去。”敬时亦出，与清一青竹枝，广记引作杖令闭眼骑之。清如其语，忽然至家。家中啼哭，及乡亲塞堂，欲入不得。会买材还，家人及客赴监视之。唯尸在地。清入至尸前，闻其尸臭。自念悔还。但外人逼突，不觉入尸时，于是而活。即营理敬家，分宅以居。于是归心三宝，勤信佛教，遂作佳流弟子。珠林九十五广记三百七十九

    Explanation

    48

    The Enlightened Monk Appeared

    The enlightened monk came out and said, "I will assist you." Qing returned to the carriage. It was a cold night, and he shivered from the cold. Until dawn when the gate opened, Monk Da indeed came to the temple. Qing then followed and knelt down. Monk Da said, "You should change your heart and do good, take refuge in the Buddha and the Dharma, and take refuge in the Sangha: by receiving these three refuges, you can avoid a premature death. Those who diligently receive and uphold will also not go through great suffering." Qing then accepted the refuges. He also saw the monk he had met the previous day, who knelt down and asked, "This person is a disciple of the monk from past lives. According to the Guangji (Comprehensive Records), the character '乎' is incorrect, as it reads '达' instead, and this is not a mistake but a deviation from the correct practice. He is about to suffer, pursued by past karma. Now able to take refuge, I hope for your compassion." The monk replied, "He was a fortunate person, so it will be easier to save him." Then he returned to the red gate. Soon, someone was sent out saying, "Lieutenant General Li can go." Jing also came out and gave Qing a green bamboo branch, instructing him to close his eyes and ride it. Qing followed the instructions, and suddenly arrived home. Cries filled the house, and relatives crowded the hall, unable to enter. When the coffin was bought and returned, family and guests came to watch over it. Only the body lay on the ground. Qing entered and stood before the body, smelling the stench of the body. He thought and regretted returning. But forced by outsiders, unaware of entering the body, he revived. He then arranged for Jing's family and divided the house to live in. Thus, he devoted himself to the Three Jewels, diligently believed in Buddhism, and became a good disciple. Zhu Lin 95, Guangji 379.

    49

    晋吕竦，字茂高，兖州人也。寓居始丰。其县南溪，流急岸峭，回曲如萦。又多大石，白日行者，犹怀危惧。竦自说，其父尝行溪中，去家十许里。日向?，天忽风雨，晦冥如漆，不复知东西。自分覆溺。唯归心观世音，且诵且念。须臾，有火光来岸，如人捉炬者，照见溪中了了。遥得归家，火常在前导，去船十余步。竦复与郗嘉宾周旋，郗所传说。珠林六十五

    Explanation

    49

    Lu Song, courtesy name Maogao, was from Yan State. He lived temporarily in Shifeng County. The southern stream of this county flows swiftly with steep banks, winding and twisting like a path. It is also filled with large rocks, and even during the day, those who travel there still feel a sense of danger. Lu Song recounted that his father once traveled in the stream, about ten or so miles from home. As the sun began to set, a sudden storm erupted, and the sky became as dark as ink, making it impossible to discern directions. His father felt he was about to drown. He focused his mind on the Bodhisattva Guanyin, continuously reciting and chanting. Soon, a firelight appeared on the shore, like someone holding a torch, illuminating the stream clearly. Guided by the firelight, he was able to return home, with the fire always leading the way ahead of the boat by about ten or so steps. Lu Song later spoke of this experience to Xie Jiajun, who also recounted it. This story is found in Volume 65 of the "Jade Forest."

    50

    晋徐荣者，琅琊人。尝至东阳，还经定山，舟人不惯，误堕洄澓中。游舞涛波，垂欲沈没。荣无复计。唯至心呼观世音。斯须闲，如有数十人齐力引船者，踊出澓中，还得平流。?江还下。日已向?，天大阴闇，风雨甚驶，不知所向。而涛波转盛。荣诵经不辍口。有顷，望见山头有火光赫然，回柁趣之，迳得还浦。举船安隐。既至，亦不复见光。同旅异之，疑非人火。明旦问浦中人，昨夜山上是何火光。众皆愕然曰：“昨风雨如此，岂如有火理，吾等并不见。”然后了其为神光矣。荣后为会稽府督护，谢敷闻其自说如此。时与荣同船者，有沙门支道蕴，谨笃士也，具见其事。后为傅亮言之，与荣所说同。珠林六十五

    Explanation

    50

    During the Jin dynasty, there was a man named Xu Rong from Langya. Once, he traveled to Dongyang and returned via Ding Mountain. The boatman was not accustomed to the waters and mistakenly fell into a whirlpool. Xu Rong danced in the waves, about to be submerged. With no other plan, he sincerely called upon the bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara. Shortly afterward, it seemed as if dozens of people were pulling the boat together, and it jumped out of the whirlpool, returning to smooth waters. He returned down the river. The day had turned dark, the sky became very dark, and the wind and rain were very strong. He did not know which way to go, and the waves became even stronger. Xu Rong recited scriptures without stopping. After a while, he saw a bright flame appear at the top of a mountain. He turned the rudder and headed towards it, immediately returning to the harbor. The whole boat was safe. After arriving, the light was no longer visible. His companions found it strange and suspected it was not a human-made fire. The next morning, he asked the people in the harbor what kind of firelight was on the mountain last night. Everyone was surprised and said, "The wind and rain were like this yesterday; how could there be fire? We did not see it." Then they realized it was divine light. Later, Xu Rong became the supervisor of the Kuaiji Prefecture, and Xie Fu heard him say this himself. At that time, there was a monk named Zhi Daoyun on the same boat with Xu Rong, who was a serious and devout person and witnessed the whole event. Later, he told Fu Liang about it, and it was the same as what Xu Rong had said. This is recorded in the Zhulin (Jade Forest) chapter 65.

    51

    晋兴宁中，沙门竺法义，山居好学。住在始宁保山，游刃众典，尤善法华。受业弟子，常有百余。至咸安二年，忽感心气疾病，已上六句依珠林十七引补积时攻治备至。而了不损。日就绵笃。遂不复自治。唯归诚观世音。如此数日。昼眠，梦见一道人，来○其病，因为治之：刳出肠胃，湔洗腑脏；见有结聚不净物甚多。洗濯毕，还内之。语义曰：“汝病已除。”眠觉，众患豁然。寻得复常。案其经云，或现沙门梵志之像；意者义公所梦其是乎。义以太元七年亡。自竺长舒至义六事，并宋尚书令傅亮所撰。二句广记引作宋尚书令傅亮撰其事迹亮自云，其先君与义游处。义每说其事，辄懔然增肃焉。珠林九十五又十七广记一百十　案傅亮所撰六事竺长舒已见前卷余不可考

    Explanation

    51

    During the Xingning period of the Jin dynasty, there was a monk named Zhu Fayi who lived in the mountains and loved learning. He resided in Shining Baoshan, skilled in many classics, especially the Lotus Sutra. He had over a hundred disciples who received instruction from him. By the second year of the Xian'an period, he suddenly felt a heart and qi illness. After a long time of treatment and care, his condition did not improve. Gradually, it became more severe, and he stopped treating himself. Instead, he sought refuge in the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara. For several days, he continued to rely on this practice. One day, while napping during the day, he dreamed of a hermit who came to cure his illness. The hermit treated him by cutting out his intestines and stomach, washing his internal organs, and finding many accumulated impurities. After washing, the hermit put them back. The hermit told Yi, "Your illness is gone." When Yi woke up, all his ailments were gone, and he soon returned to normal. According to the scriptures, sometimes Avalokiteshvara appears as a monk or a Brahmin. Perhaps what Master Yi dreamed was true. Yi passed away in the seventh year of the Taie period. From Zhu Changshu to Yi, six stories, all compiled by Fu Liang, the Prime Minister of the Song dynasty. Two entries in the Widely Recorded collection are attributed to Fu Liang, who compiled the stories. Fu Liang mentioned that his father had been friends with Yi. Whenever Yi talked about these things, he would become more solemn and respectful. Entries 95 and 17 in the Jade Forest and 110 in the Widely Recorded collection. According to Fu Liang's compilation, Zhu Changshu has been mentioned in previous volumes, but the rest are not verifiable.

    52

    晋杜愿，字永平，梓潼涪人也。家巨富。有一男，名天保，愿爱念。年十岁，泰元三年，暴病而死。经数月日，家所养猪，生五子；一子最肥。后官长新到，愿将以作礼，捉就杀之。有一比丘，忽至愿前，谓曰：“此豚是君儿也。如前百余日中，而相忘乎？”言竟，忽然不见。四顾寻视，见西天腾空而去。香气充布，弥日乃歇。珠林五十二

    Explanation

    52

    Du Yuan, courtesy name Yongping, was from Fuchong, Zitong. His family was very wealthy. He had a son named Tianbao, whom he deeply loved. At the age of ten, Tianbao died suddenly of an illness in the third year of Taiyuan (378 AD). Several months later, a pig in the family gave birth to five piglets, one of which was particularly fat. After the new official arrived, Du Yuan planned to use this pig as a gift. Just as he was about to catch and kill it, a Buddhist monk suddenly appeared before him and said, "This pig is your son. Do you not remember him after more than a hundred days?" After speaking, the monk suddenly disappeared. Looking around, Du Yuan saw the monk soar into the sky and depart to the West. The fragrance spread and lasted for a whole day before dissipating. This story is recorded in the "Pearl Forest" (珠林) series, chapter fifty-two.

    53

    晋唐遵，字○道，上虞人也。晋太元八年，暴病而死。经夕得稣。云有人呼将去，至一城府，未进。顷见其从叔，自城中出，惊问遵：“汝何故来？”遵答：“违离姑姊，并历年载，欲往问讯，本明当发，夜见数人，急呼来此。即时可得归去，而不知还路。”从叔云：“汝姑丧已二年。汝大姊儿道文，近被录来。既蒙恩放，仍留看戏，不即还去，积日方归，家已殡殓。乃入棺中，又摇动棺器，冀望其家觉悟开棺。棺遂至路，落檀车下。其家或欲开之。乃向卜者。卜云不吉，遂不敢开。不得复生。今为把沙之役，辛勤极苦。汝宜速去，勿复住此。且汝小姊，又已丧亡。今与汝姑，共在地狱，日夕忧苦。不知何时，可得免脱。汝今还去，可语其儿：勤修功德，庶得免之。”于此示遵归路。

    Explanation

    53

    During the reign of Emperor Taiyuan in the Eastern Jin Dynasty, Tang Zun of Shangyu had a sudden and severe illness and died. After a night, he regained consciousness and said that someone called him away, leading him to a city or administrative center, but he did not enter. Soon, he saw his maternal uncle or cousin coming out of the city and asked him in surprise, "Why are you here?" Tang Zun replied, "I have been away from my aunt and sister for many years and wanted to visit them. I originally planned to depart, but I saw several people at night who urgently called me here. I could return immediately but did not know the way back." The maternal uncle or cousin said, "Your aunt has been dead for two years. Your eldest sister's son, Dao Wen, was recently taken away. He was released as a favor but stayed to watch a performance. He did not immediately return home and returned after many days. The family had already performed the burial rites. He entered the coffin and shook the coffin lid, hoping his family would realize and open the coffin. The coffin reached the road and fell under a wooden cart. The family considered opening the coffin but consulted a diviner who said it was inauspicious, so they did not dare to open it. Dao Wen could not be revived. He is now engaged in hard labor in hell, working extremely hard. You should leave quickly and not stay here. Your younger sister has also died. You and your aunt are now in hell, suffering daily. I do not know when you can be freed from hell. You should return and tell Dao Wen to diligently perform good deeds, perhaps he can escape from hell." At this point, the way back was shown to Tang Zun.

    54

    将别，又属遵曰：“汝得还生，良为殊庆。在世无几，儵如风尘。天堂地狱，苦乐报应；吾昔闻其语，今睹其实。汝宜深勤善业，务为孝敬。受法持戒，慎不可犯。一去人身，入此罪地。幽穷苦酷，自悔何及。勤以在心，不可忽也。我家亲属，生时不信罪福，今并遭涂炭，长受楚毒，焦烂伤痛，无时暂休。欲求一日改恶为善，当何得耶？悉我所具，故以嘱汝。劝化家内，共加勉励。”言已，涕泣，因此而别。遵随路而归，俄而至家。家治棺将竟，方营殡殓。遵既附尸，尸寻气通。移日稍差。劝示亲识，并奉大法。初遵姑○南郡徐汉，长姊○江夏乐瑜于，小姊○吴兴严晚。途路县远，久断音息。遵既差，遂至三郡，寻访姑及小姊。姊子果并丧亡。长姊亦说儿道文殓后，棺动堕车，皆如叔言。既闻遵说道文横死之意，姊追加痛恨，重为制服。珠林九十七

    Explanation

    54

    As they were about to part, he entrusted Zun with these words: "You are able to return to life, which is indeed a great cause for celebration. Life in the world is short, fleeting like dust in the wind. Heaven and hell, the consequences of good and bad actions; I heard about it before, and now I see it in reality. You should diligently cultivate good deeds and be filial and respectful. Receive the teachings and keep the precepts, be cautious not to violate them. Once you leave the human body, you will enter this realm of sin. Endless suffering and cruelty, regretting it afterward will be too late. Diligence should be in your heart, do not neglect it. My family members, who did not believe in karma in life, are now suffering greatly, enduring long-lasting pain, burning and hurting, with no moment of respite. If they want to change from evil to good for even a day, what can they do? Knowing all this, I entrust you with this. Persuade and guide your family, encourage each other." After speaking, he wept, and they parted ways. Zun returned home along the road, soon reaching his house. The family was preparing the coffin, just about to perform the funeral rites. Zun touched the body, and soon the body regained breath. After a few days, he gradually recovered. He persuaded and showed his relatives and acquaintances, all following the great teachings. Initially, Zun's aunt in Nanjun was Xu Han, his elder sister in Jiangxia was Le Yu Yu, and his younger sister in Wuxing was Yan Wan. The distance was far, and communication had been cut off for a long time. After Zun recovered, he went to the three prefectures to find his aunt and younger sister. His sister's children had indeed died. His elder sister also said that after her son's burial, the coffin moved and fell from the cart, just as his uncle had said. After hearing Zun's explanation of his brother's sudden death, his sister felt even more grief and anger, and wore mourning clothes again. Zhu Jin (Pearl Forest), volume 97.

    55

    晋谢敷，字庆绪，会稽山阴人也，镇军将军輶之兄子也。少有高操，隐于东山，笃信大法，精勤不倦。手写首楞严经。当在都白马寺中，寺为灾火所延，什物余经，并成煨尽，而此经止烧纸头界外而已。文字悉存，无所毁失。敷死时，友人疑其得道。及闻此经，弥复惊异。至元嘉八年，河东蒲阪城中大灾火。火自隔河飞至，不可救灭；处戍民居，无不荡尽。唯精舍塔寺，并得不焚。里中小屋，有经像者，亦多不烧。或屋虽焚毁，而于煨尽之中，时得全经，纸素如故。一城叹异，相率敬信。珠林十八

    Explanation

    55

    Xie Fu, courtesy name Qing Xu, was from Shan Yin, Kuaiji, and was the nephew of General of the Army You. From a young age, he possessed noble character and retired to the East Mountain, firmly believing in the Great Law and diligently practicing without tiring. He personally wrote the Shurangama Sutra. While staying at the White Horse Temple in the capital, the temple was engulfed by a fire disaster, and all the belongings and other scriptures were reduced to ashes. However, this scripture was only burned at the edges of the paper, leaving the text completely preserved with no damage or loss. When he died, his friends suspected that he had attained enlightenment. Upon hearing of this scripture, they were even more amazed.

    In the eighth year of the Yungang era (431 AD), a great fire disaster struck the city of Pu'an in Hedong (modern-day Yongji, Shanxi). The fire crossed the river as if flying, and could not be extinguished. All the military outposts, civilian houses, and everything else were completely destroyed. Only the monasteries and pagodas were spared from the fire. Small houses in the neighborhood, if they contained scriptures or images, were also largely spared. Sometimes even if a house was burned down, the scriptures within were still found intact, with the paper looking as good as new. The entire city was amazed, and people began to revere and believe in Buddhism. This is recorded in the 18th chapter of the Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest).

    56

    晋济阴丁承，字德慎。建安中，案晋纪元无建安疑当作建元也为凝阴令。时北界居民妇，诣外井汲水。有胡人长鼻深目，左过井上，从妇人乞饮。饮讫，忽然不见。妇则腹痛，遂加转剧。啼呼有顷，卒然起坐，胡语指麾。邑中有数十家，悉共观视。妇呼索纸笔来，欲作书。得笔，便作胡书：横行，或如乙，或如己。满五纸，投着地，教人读此书。邑中无能读者。有一小儿，十余岁，妇即指此小儿能读。小儿得书，便胡语读之，观者惊愕，不知何谓。妇叫小儿起。小儿既起，翘足，以手弄相和。须臾各休。即以白德慎。德慎召见妇及儿，问之，云：当时忽忽不自觉，知德慎欲验其事，即遣吏赍书诣许下寺，以示旧胡。胡大惊，言佛经中闲，亡失道远，忧不能得。虽口诵，不具足。此乃本书，遂留写之。珠林十八

    Explanation

    56

    Ding Cheng of Jinyin, styled De Shen, was the magistrate of Jinyin during the Jian'an period (196–220 AD). According to the Jin dynasty chronology, there is doubt whether it should be Jian'an or Jianyuan. At that time, a woman from the northern border of the county went to an outer well to draw water. A man with a long nose and deep-set eyes passed by the well and asked the woman for a drink. After drinking, he suddenly disappeared. The woman then felt abdominal pain, which intensified. She cried out for a while, and then suddenly sat up, speaking in a foreign language and gesturing. Several dozen households in the village gathered to watch. The woman called for paper and ink, wanting to write something. When she got the pen, she wrote in a foreign script: horizontal lines, sometimes resembling the character "乙," sometimes resembling "己." She filled five sheets of paper, threw them on the ground, and instructed people to read the text. No one in the village could read it. There was a boy, about ten years old, whom the woman pointed out as being able to read it. The boy took the paper and read it in the foreign language. The onlookers were amazed and did not understand what it meant. The woman called the boy to stand up and perform a ritual. The boy stood up, raised his foot, and used his hands to make some gestures. After a short while, they all stopped. The woman immediately reported this to Ding Cheng. Ding Cheng summoned the woman and the boy and asked them about it. They said that they had been unaware at the time but knew that Ding Cheng wanted to verify the incident. Ding Cheng then sent an official with the text to a temple in Xu (许), to show it to an old man from the foreign land. The old man was greatly surprised and said that the text resembled a lost Buddhist scripture, which had been lost due to the long distance and was feared to be unobtainable. Although he could recite it, it was not complete. This was indeed the original text, and he decided to copy it down. This story is recorded in Chapter Eighteen of Zhu Lin (珠林).

    57

    晋琅琊王凝之，妻晋左将军夫人谢氏奕之女也。尝频亡，二男悼惜过甚，哭泣累年，若居至艰。后忽见二儿俱还，皆着锁械，慰勉其母，宜自宽割。儿并有罪，若垂哀怜。可为作福。于是哀痛稍止，而勤功德。珠林三十三
    　　晋沙门支遁，字道林，陈留人也。神宇隽发，为老释风流之宗。常与其师，辨论物类。谓鸡卵生用未足，杀之，与诸蜎动，不得同罚。师寻亡。忽见形来，至遁前，手执鸡卵投地，破之，见有鸡雏，出壳而行。遁即惟悟，悔其本言。俄而师及鸡雏，并灭不见。珠林七十二

    Explanation

    57

    Wang Ningzhi, Prince of Langya, was married to the daughter of General Xie Yi, a left general of the Jin dynasty. He often experienced the loss of family members, and his two sons mourned excessively, crying for many years as if facing the greatest hardship. Later, he suddenly saw his two sons return together, both wearing shackles and chains. They comforted and encouraged their mother, advising her to be self-reliant and cut ties. They said that they both had sins, and if she showed compassion, she could perform good deeds for them. As a result, his grief gradually subsided, and he became diligent in performing good deeds and cultivating virtue. (From the Jade Forest, Volume 33)

    Zhi Dun, a Buddhist monk of the Jin dynasty, was from Chenliu and was known by the name Dao Lin. He had a divine presence and sharp intellect, making him a leading figure in the fusion of Taoist and Buddhist thought. He often debated with his teacher about the moral status of various creatures. Zhi Dun argued that eggs were not yet fully developed and thus should not be killed, unlike small insects, which deserved different treatment. Soon after, his teacher passed away. One day, Zhi Dun suddenly saw his teacher appear before him, holding an egg and throwing it to the ground. The egg broke, and a chick emerged, walking out of its shell. Zhi Dun immediately realized his mistake and regretted his earlier words. Soon after, both his teacher and the chick disappeared. (From the Jade Forest, Volume 72)

    58

    晋庐山七岭，同会于东，共成峰崿。其崖穷绝，莫有升者。晋太元中，豫章太守范宁，将起学馆，遣人伐材其山。见人着沙门服，淩虚直上。既至，则回身踞其峰；良久，乃兴云气，俱灭。时有采药数人，皆共瞻睹。能文之士，咸为之兴。沙门释昙谛庐山赋曰：“应真淩云以踞峰，眇翳景而入冥者也。”珠林十九
    　　晋沙门释僧朗者，戒行明严，华戎敬异。尝与数人，俱受法请；行至中途。忽告同辈曰：“君等留寺衣物，似有窃者。”同旅即返，果及盗焉。晋太元中，于奉高县金舆山谷，起立塔寺，造制形像。符坚之末，降斥道人，惟敬朗一众，不敢毁焉。于时道俗信奉，每有来者。人数多少，未至一日，辄已逆知。使弟子为具，必如言果到。其谷旧多虎，常为暴害。立寺之后，皆如家畜。鲜卑慕容德，以二县祖课，充其朝中。至今号其谷为朗公谷也。珠林十九

    Explanation

    58

    During the Jin Dynasty, the seven ridges of Mount Lu converged to the east, forming a series of peaks. The cliffs were so steep and rugged that no one could climb them. In the Taiyuan period, Fan Ning, the governor of Yuzhang, planned to build a school and sent people to gather materials from the mountain. They saw a man dressed in a monk's robe ascending into the void straight up. Upon reaching the peak, he turned his body and sat upon it. After a while, he raised clouds and mist, and then disappeared. At that time, several people who were gathering herbs all witnessed this. Those skilled in writing were all inspired by it. The Buddhist monk Tan Di wrote in his Lu Mountain Assignment: "The Bodhisattva ascended into the clouds and sat on the peak, disappearing into the void."

    In the Jin Dynasty, the Buddhist monk Sang Lang was known for his strict discipline and was respected by both Han and foreign people. Once, while traveling with a few companions, he suddenly told his fellow travelers, "You left your belongings in the temple, and it seems someone has stolen them." They immediately returned and indeed caught the thief. During the Taiyuan period, he built a pagoda and temple in the Jinju Valley of Fenggao County, creating statues and images. In the late period of Former Qin, when the emperor Fu Jian suppressed Buddhism, he alone respected the group led by Sang Lang and did not dare to destroy their temple. At that time, both monks and laypeople revered him, and he could predict the number of visitors before they arrived, always preparing accordingly. Before the temple was built, the valley was often plagued by tigers that caused harm. After the temple was established, the tigers became like domesticated animals. The Xianbei ruler Murong De used the taxes from two counties to support his court. To this day, the valley is known as Lang Gong Valley.

    59

    晋沙门释法相，河东人也。常独山居，精苦为业。鸟兽集其左右，驯若家兽。太山祠大石函，以盛财宝。相时山行，宿于其庙。见一人玄衣武冠，令相开函，言终不见。其函石盖重过千钧，相试提之飘然而开。于是取其财宝，以施贫民。后渡江南，住越城寺，忽敖游放荡，优俳滑稽，或时裸袒，干冒朝贵。镇北将军司马恬恶其不节，招而酖之。频倾三钟，神气清怡，恬然自若。年八十九，元兴末卒。珠林十九

    Explanation

    59

    The Buddhist monk named Fashang (释法相) was from Hedong (河东). He often lived alone in the mountains, devoted to rigorous practice. Birds and animals gathered around him, tame like domestic animals. There was a large stone box at the Temple of Mount Tai, used to hold treasures. Fashang was traveling in the mountains and stayed in the temple. He saw a person dressed in a black robe and wearing a military hat, who ordered Fashang to open the box. When the person spoke, he disappeared. The stone lid of the box was extremely heavy, but Fashang managed to open it effortlessly. He then took the treasures and distributed them to the poor. Later, he crossed the river to the south and lived in Yuecheng Temple. Suddenly, he became carefree and unrestrained, skilled in jest and humor. Sometimes he went naked, offending the nobility. The Northern General Military Commander Sima Tian disliked his lack of restraint and invited him, then poisoned him. Fashang drank three cups repeatedly, but his spirit remained clear and calm, as if nothing had happened. He was aged 89 and died at the end of the Yuanxing era. This story is recorded in the "Jewel Forest" (珠林十九).

    60

    晋张崇，京兆杜陵人也。少奉法。晋太元中，符坚既败，长安百姓有千余家，南走归晋。为镇戍所拘。谓为游寇。杀其男丁，虏其子女。崇与同等五人，手脚共械，衔身掘坑，埋筑至腰。各相去二十步。明日将驰马射之，以为娱乐。崇虑望穷尽，唯洁心专念观世音。夜中，械忽自破，上得离身！因是便走，遂得免脱。崇既脚痛，同寻路，经一寺，乃复称观世音名，至心礼拜。以一石置前，发誓愿，言今欲过江东，诉乱晋帝，理此冤魂，救其妻息。若心愿获果，此石当分为二。崇礼拜已，石即破焉。崇遂至京师，发白虎撙，具列冤氏。帝乃悉加宥己。为人所略卖者，皆为编户。智生道人，目所亲见。法苑珠林六十五

    Explanation

    60

    Zhang Chong of Jin, a native of Duling, Jingzhao. When he was young, he was devoted to the law. During the Taiyuan period of the Eastern Jin, after Fu Jian was defeated, thousands of families from Chang'an fled south to return to the Jin dynasty. They were detained by the local garrison and considered as bandits. The men were killed, and the women and children were captured. Zhang Chong and four others were chained together by hands and feet, neck and body dug into pits, and buried up to the waist, each separated by twenty steps. The next day, they were to be chased and shot with arrows for entertainment. Zhang Chong, feeling desperate, focused solely on the Bodhisattva Guanyin. At night, the chains suddenly broke, allowing them to free themselves. They then escaped and managed to escape. Zhang Chong, now in pain from his feet, continued on the road with his companions, passing by a temple. There, he again called out the name of the Bodhisattva Guanyin, prostrated himself with sincere devotion, placed a stone in front of him, and made a vow, saying that he now intended to cross to the east of the river, to appeal to the Jin emperor about the chaos, to seek justice for these wronged spirits, and to save his wife and children. If his wish was granted, the stone would split into two. After Zhang Chong finished his prostration, the stone indeed split. Zhang Chong then arrived in the capital, reported to the White Tiger Hall, and detailed the list of wronged individuals. The emperor then pardoned them all. Those who had been sold as slaves were registered as commoners. The monk Zhi Sheng, who witnessed this with his own eyes, recorded it in the 65th volume of the "Flower Garden of the Dharma Treasury."

    61

    晋王懿，字仲德，太原人也。守车骑将军。世信奉法。父苗，符坚时为中山太守，为丁零所害。仲德与兄元德，携母南归。登陟峭崄，饥疲绝粮。无复余计，惟归心三宝。忽见一童子，牵青牛，见懿等饥，各乞一饭。因忽不见。时积雨大水，懿前望浩然，不知何处为浅，可得揭蹑。俄有一白狼，旋绕其前，过水而反，似若引导。如此者三。于是逐狼而渡，水才至膝。俄得陆路，南归晋帝。后自五兵尚书，为徐州刺史。尝欲设斋：宿昔洒扫，敷陈香华，盛列经像。忽闻法堂有经呗声，清婉流畅。懿遽往观：见有五沙门在佛坐前，威容伟异，神仪秀出。懿知非凡僧，心甚欢敬。沙门回相瞻?，意若依然。音旨未交，忽而竦身飞空而去。亲表宾僚，见者甚众。咸悉欣跃，倍增信悟。珠林六十五

    Explanation

    61

    晋王懿，字仲德，太原人也。守车骑将军。世信奉法。父苗，符坚时为中山太守，为丁零所害。仲德与兄元德，携母南归。登陟峭崄，饥疲绝粮。无复余计，惟归心三宝。忽见一童子，牵青牛，见懿等饥，各乞一饭。因忽不见。时积雨大水，懿前望浩然，不知何处为浅，可得揭蹑。俄有一白狼，旋绕其前，过水而反，似若引导。如此者三。于是逐狼而渡，水才至膝。俄得陆路，南归晋帝。后自五兵尚书，为徐州刺史。尝欲设斋：宿昔洒扫，敷陈香华，盛列经像。忽闻法堂有经呗声，清婉流畅。懿遽往观：见有五沙门在佛坐前，威容伟异，神仪秀出。懿知非凡僧，心甚欢敬。沙门回相瞻?，意若依然。音旨未交，忽而竦身飞空而去。亲表宾僚，见者甚众。咸悉欣跃，倍增信悟。珠林六十五

    Final Translation:

    Jin Wang Yi, courtesy name Zhongde, was from Taiyuan. He served as the Guardian of the Cavalry General. His family had always believed in and followed the law. His father, Miao, was the governor of Zhongshan during the reign of Fu Jian, but was killed by the Tiele. Zhongde and his elder brother Yuande took their mother southward. They ascended steep and dangerous terrain, starving, exhausted, and without food. With no other options, they dedicated themselves to the Three Jewels of Buddhism. Suddenly, they saw a boy leading a green ox, who saw their hunger and asked for a single meal for each of them. The boy then vanished. At that time, there was heavy rain and flooding. Yi looked ahead and saw the vast waters, unsure where the shallow part was where one could wade across. Soon, a white wolf circled in front of him, crossed the water, and returned, as if guiding them. This happened three times. Following the wolf, they crossed the water, which only reached their knees. Soon, they found a land route and returned south to the Jin Emperor. Later, he served as a military official and became the governor of Xuzhou. Once, he intended to set up a vegetarian meal: he cleaned and prepared the space, arranged incense and flowers, and displayed scriptures and images. Suddenly, he heard chanting in the lecture hall, clear, graceful, and flowing. Yi hurried to see and found five monks before the Buddha's seat, with majestic and extraordinary appearance and demeanor. Yi knew they were not ordinary monks and was very happy and respectful. The monks looked back at each other, as if they recognized something. Before they could exchange words, they suddenly rose up and flew away into the sky. Relatives, friends, and guests, many of whom witnessed this, were all delighted and greatly increased their faith and understanding. Chapter 65 of the "Jeweled Forest."

    62

    晋程道惠，字文和，武昌人也。世奉五升米道，不信有佛。常云：“古来正道，莫踰李老。何乃信惑胡言，以为胜教。”太元十五年，病死。心下尚暖，家不殡殓。数日得稣。说初死时，见十许人缚录将去。逢一比丘，云此人宿福，未可缚也。乃解其缚，散驱而去。道路修平，而两边棘刺森然，略不容足。驱诸罪人，驰走其中。肉随着刺，号呻聒耳。见惠行在平路，皆叹羡曰：“佛弟子行路，复胜人也？”惠曰：“我不奉法。”其人笑曰：“君忘之耳。

    Explanation

    62

    Jin Cheng Daohui, courtesy name Wenhua, was from Wuchang. His family had long practiced the Five Sheng Daoist sect and did not believe in Buddhism. He often said, "Since ancient times, the true path has never surpassed that of Laozi. Why believe in and be misled by foreign words, thinking they are superior teachings?" In the 15th year of Taiyuan (390 AD), he fell ill and died. His heart was still warm, and his family did not perform the burial rites immediately. After several days, he revived and recounted his experience. He said that when he first died, he saw about ten people binding and leading him away. He encountered a monk who said that this person had accumulated good karma and should not be bound. The monk then released him and sent him away. The road was smooth, but on both sides were dense thorns, barely allowing passage. The sinners were forced to run through this thorny path, their flesh sticking to the thorns, and their cries and groans filled the air. Seeing Daohui walking on a peaceful road, they all admired and said, "The path of the Buddhist disciple is indeed better than ours!" Daohui replied, "I do not follow the Dharma." The monk smiled and said, "You have just forgotten."

    63

    ”惠因自忆先身奉佛，已经五生五死。忘失本志。今生在世，幼遇恶人，未达邪正，乃惑邪道。既至大城，迳进听事。见一人，年可四五十，南面而坐。见惠，惊问曰：“君不应来。”有一人，着单衣帻，持簿书对曰：“此人伐社，杀人罪，应来此。”向所逢比丘亦随惠入，申理甚至。云伐社非罪也。此人宿福甚多，杀人虽重，报未至也。南面坐者曰，可罚所录人，命惠就坐，谢曰：“小鬼谬滥，枉相录来。亦由君忘失宿命，不知奉大正法教也。”将遣惠还，乃使暂兼覆校将军。

    Explanation

    63

    Hui recalled his past life serving the Buddha, having undergone five cycles of rebirth and death. He had forgotten his original aspiration. In this life, at a young age, he encountered evil people, failed to distinguish between right and wrong, and was misled by false teachings. Upon arriving in a large city, he proceeded directly to the hearing chamber. There, he saw a man, around forty or fifty years old, sitting facing south. The man was surprised and asked, “You should not be here.” Another person, wearing a plain robe and headband, holding records, replied, “This person cut down a sacred tree and committed murder, so he should be here.” The monk whom Hui had encountered earlier also followed him inside and argued persuasively. He claimed that cutting down the tree was not a crime. This person had accumulated much merit in past lives, and though the act of murder was grave, the retribution had not yet arrived. The man sitting facing south said, “It is possible to punish the person who recorded this,” and ordered Hui to sit. He then apologized, saying, “The minor demon made a mistake, wrongfully bringing you here. It is also because you forgot your past life, not knowing to follow the great orthodox teachings.” He was about to send Hui back, and was then appointed temporarily as a deputy inspector general.

    64

    历观地狱。惠欣然辞出。导从而行。行至诸城，城城皆是地狱。人众巨亿，悉受罪报。见有掣狗，啮人百节，肌肉散落，流血蔽地。又有群鸟，其喙如锋，飞来甚速，鸩然血至，入人口中，表里贯洞；其人宛转呼叫，筋骨碎落。其余经见，与赵泰屑荷，大抵粗同，不复具载。唯此二条为异，故详记之。观历既遍，乃遣惠还。复见向所逢比丘，与惠一铜物，形如小铃，曰：“君还至家，可弃此门外，勿以入室。某年月日，君当有厄。诫慎过此，寿延九十。

    Explanation

    64

    After observing the hells, Hui happily declined and left, guided and followed. They traveled through various cities, each of which was a hell. There were countless people, all suffering punishments. They saw tugging dogs, biting people's joints, causing muscles to scatter and blood to cover the ground. There were also flocks of birds with beaks like blades, flying swiftly, their blood flowing into people's mouths, from inside out, through and through. The people twisted and called out, their bones and tendons broken and falling. Other things seen were generally similar to Zhao Tai's experiences, not fully recorded. Only these two scenes were different, so they are recorded in detail. After observing all the hells, Hui was then sent back. Again, he saw the monk he had met before, who gave him a copper object shaped like a small bell. The monk said, "When you return home, you can throw this outside the door, do not bring it into the house. On a certain day in the year, you will face danger. Be cautious beyond this point, your life will extend to ninety years."

    65

    ”时道惠家于京师大街南，自见来还。达皂荚桥，见亲表三人，住车共语，悼惠之亡。至门，见婢行哭而市。彼人及婢，咸弗见也。惠将入门，置向铜物门外树上，光明舒散，流飞属天。良久还小，奄尔而灭。至户，闻尸臭惆怅恶之。时宾亲奔吊，突惠者多，不得徘徊。因进入尸，忽然而稣。说所逢车人及市婢，咸皆符同。惠后为廷尉，预西堂听讼，未及就列，欻然烦闷，不识人，半日乃愈。计其时日，即道人所戒之期。顷之，迁为广州刺史。元嘉六年卒，六十九矣。珠林五十五

    Explanation

    65

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    Dao Hui once lived in the southern part of the capital city's main street. One day, he returned home and reached the soapberry tree bridge. There, he encountered three relatives who stopped their carriage to talk and mourn his death. When he arrived at the door, he saw a maid walking and crying while going to market. Neither the people nor the maid were seen by anyone else. As Dao Hui was about to enter, he placed copper objects outside the door on a tree. The light spread and rose into the sky, gradually becoming smaller and suddenly disappearing. When he reached the door, he smelled the stench of the corpse and felt sad and disgusted. At that time, guests and relatives came to mourn, and many people rushed to Dao Hui, preventing him from lingering. Because he entered the room with the body, he suddenly revived. He described the people he met in the carriage and the maid at the market, and they all matched what he had seen. Later, Dao Hui became a prosecutor and participated in hearing cases in the west hall. Before he could take his place, he suddenly felt dizzy and disoriented, not recognizing anyone, and recovered after half a day. Calculating the time, it was the period Dao Hui had been warned about. Shortly afterward, he was promoted to the position of Governor of Guangzhou. He died in the sixth year of the Yüan Jia era, at the age of sixty-nine. This story is recorded in Zhu Lin Volume 55.

    66

    晋沙门慧达，姓刘名萨荷，西河离石人也。未出家时：长于军旅；不闻佛法；尚气武；好畋猎。年三十一，暴病而死。体尚温柔。家未殓。至七日而稣。说云将尽之时，见有两人执缚将去。向西北行。行路转高，稍得平衢。两边列树。见有一人，执弓带剑，当衢而立。指语两人，将荷西行。见屋舍甚多。白壁赤柱。荷入一家，有女子美容服。荷就乞食。空中声言，勿与之也。有人从地踊出，执铁杵，将欲击之。荷遽走，历入十许家皆然，遂无所得。复西北行，见一妪乘车，与荷一卷书。荷受之。西至一家，馆宇华整。有妪坐于户外，口中虎牙。屋内床帐光丽，竹席青几。复有女子处之。问荷，“得书来不？”荷以书卷与之。女取余书比之。俄见两沙门，谓荷，“汝识我不？”荷答：“不识。”沙门曰：“今宜归命释迦文佛。”荷如言发念，因随沙门俱行。遥见一城，类长安城，而色甚黑，盖铁城也。见人身甚长大肤黑如漆，头发曳地。

    Explanation

    66

    During the Jin Dynasty, there was a Buddhist monk named Huìdá, whose surname was Liu and given name was Sàhé. He was from Líshí, Xīhé. Before he became a monk, he was experienced in military service; he had not yet heard of Buddhist teachings; he valued martial virtues; and he loved hunting. At the age of thirty-one, he suddenly died from an illness. His body was still warm, and his family had not yet performed the burial rites. Seven days later, he revived. He recounted that as he was nearing death, he saw two people binding and taking him away. They headed northwest. The path became higher, gradually reaching a flat road. Trees lined both sides. He saw a person holding a bow and wearing a sword, standing in the middle of the road. The person pointed to two others and took Huìdá to the west. He saw many houses with white walls and red columns. He entered one house where a beautifully dressed woman was. He asked for food. A voice from the air said, "Do not give it to him." Someone emerged from the ground, holding an iron pestle, and was about to strike him. Huìdá ran quickly, entering ten or so houses, but finally got nothing. He then saw an old woman riding in a carriage, who gave him a scroll. He accepted it. He reached a house to the west, with elegant and well-ordered buildings. An old woman was sitting outside the house, with tiger teeth in her mouth. The interior had beautifully decorated beds and curtains, a bamboo mat, and a green table. There was another woman there. She asked Huìdá, "Did you receive the book?" He gave the scroll to her. The woman took the remaining books and compared them. Soon, he saw two monks, who said to Huìdá, "Do you recognize us?" He replied, "I do not recognize you." The monks said, "Now it is appropriate to devote oneself to the Buddha Śākyamuni." Huìdá followed the words and made a vow, and then followed the monks together. He saw a city in the distance, similar to the city of Chang'an, but the color was very dark, and it was a city of iron. He saw people with very tall and large bodies, their skin black like lacquer, and their hair dragging on the ground.

    67

    沙门曰：“此狱中鬼也。”其处甚寒。有冰如席，飞散着人。着头，头断；着脚，脚断。二沙门云：“此寒冰狱也。”荷便识宿命，知两沙门往维卫佛时，并其师也。作沙弥时，以犯俗罪，不得受戒。世虽有佛，竟不得见从。再得人身：一生羌中，今生晋中。又见从伯，在此狱里。谓荷曰：“昔在邺时，不知事佛。见人灌像，聊试学之；而不肯还直。今故受罪。犹有灌福，幸得生天。”次见刀山地狱。次第经历，观见甚多。狱狱异城，不相杂厕。人数如沙，不可称计。楚毒科法，略与经说相符。自荷履践地狱，示有光景。俄而忽见金色，晖明皎然。见人长二丈许，相好严华，体黄金色。左右并曰：观世大士也。皆起迎礼。有二沙门，形质相类，并行而东。荷作礼毕。菩萨具为说法，可千余言，末云：“凡为亡人设福，若父母兄弟，爰至七世，姻媾亲戚，朋友路人，或在精舍，或在家中，亡者受苦，即得免脱。七月望日，沙门受腊；此时设供，弥为胜也。

    Explanation

    67

    The monk said, "This is a ghost from the underworld." The place was extremely cold. There were ice shards as large as mats, flying and scattering onto people. When they hit someone's head, the head would break off; when they hit someone's feet, the feet would break off. The two monks said, "This is the Cold Ice Hell." The monk immediately recognized his past life, knowing that the two monks were disciples of the same teacher during the time of the Buddha Vipasyin. As a novice, he had committed a lay sin and thus could not receive ordination. Despite the presence of the Buddha, he never had the opportunity to follow him. He has been reborn twice: once in Qiang and now in Jin. He also saw his uncle in this hell. The uncle said to the monk, "In the past, when I was in Ye, I did not know about Buddhism. I saw someone pouring water over a statue and tried it myself; but I did not return the water. Now I am suffering punishment. I still have the merit from pouring water and will be reborn in heaven." Next, the monk saw the Blade Mountain Hell. He experienced various hells in sequence, seeing many things. Each hell was in a different city and did not mix with others. The number of people in the hells was as numerous as sand and could not be counted. The punishments and rules in the hells were roughly consistent with what is said in the scriptures. As the monk experienced the hells firsthand, there was a glimmer of light. Suddenly, he saw a golden light that was bright and clear. He saw a person who was about two zhang tall, with a beautiful appearance and a golden body. Those around him said, "This is the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara." Everyone rose to greet and pay respects. There were two monks who looked similar and walked east together. After the monk paid his respects, the Bodhisattva gave a detailed explanation, speaking for more than a thousand words, concluding, "In setting up merit for the deceased, whether they are parents, siblings, or even friends and passersby, it is beneficial. Whether in a temple or at home, the deceased can be freed from suffering. On the 15th day of the seventh month, when monks receive their year-end offerings, setting up offerings at this time is especially meritorious."

    68

    若制器物，以充供养，器器摽题，言为某人亲奉上三宝，福施弥多，其庆逾速。沙门白衣，见身为过，及宿世之罪，种种恶业，能于众中尽自发露，不失事条，勤诚忏悔者，罪即消灭。如其弱颜羞惭，耻于大众露其过者，可在屏处，默自记说，不失事者，罪亦除灭。若有所遗漏，非故隐蔽，虽不获免，受报稍轻。若不能悔，无惭愧心，此名执过不反，命终之后，克坠地狱。又他造塔及与堂殿，虽复一土一木，若染若碧，率诚供助，获福甚多。

    Explanation

    68

    If one makes objects to serve as offerings, each object should be clearly marked, stating that it is personally presented by a certain individual to the Three Jewels. The more extensive the offering, the swifter the reward. Monks and laypeople who recognize their present faults and past-life transgressions, as well as various evil deeds, and are able to fully confess them before the assembly without omitting any details, and who sincerely repent, will have their sins eradicated. If someone, out of shame, is unwilling to confess their faults before the assembly, they may do so in private, silently recalling and confessing their transgressions to themselves, without omitting any matters; in such a case, their sins will also be erased. If something is inadvertently omitted and not intentionally concealed, though they cannot escape the karmic consequences, the retribution will be somewhat lighter. But if one is unable to repent and lacks a sense of shame and remorse, this is called clinging to one’s faults without turning back. After death, such a person will inevitably fall into hell. Moreover, if someone builds a stupa or a hall, even using just one piece of earth or wood, whether dyed or green, and offers it with sincerity, they will gain great merit.

    69

    若见塔殿，或有草秽，不加耘除，蹈之而行，礼拜功德，功随即尽矣。”又曰：“经者尊典，化导之津。波罗密经，功德最胜。首楞严亦其次也。若有善人，读诵经处，其地皆为金刚，但肉眼众生，不能见耳。能勤讽持，不坠地狱。般若定本，及如来钵，后当东至汉地。能立一善，于此经钵，受报生天，倍得功德。”所说甚广，略要载之。荷临辞去，谓曰：“汝应历劫，备受罪报。以尝闻经法，生欢喜心，今当见受轻报。一过便免。汝得济活，可作沙门。

    Explanation

    69

    If you see a pagoda or temple hall, and there is grass or weeds, and it is not weeded or cleared, and you step on it and walk, and perform acts of worship or merit, the merit will immediately be exhausted." He then said, "The scriptures are revered classics, the means of transformation and guidance. The Perfection of Wisdom Sutra has the supreme merit. The Sutra of the Lion's Roar is second-best. If there is a good person, where they read and recite the scriptures, the ground becomes diamond-like, but ordinary beings with physical eyes cannot see it. If they can diligently recite and uphold, they will not fall into hell. The definitive edition of the Prajnaparamita Sutra, and the Buddha's alms bowl, will later come to the Han region (China). If one performs a good deed in connection with this scripture and alms bowl, they will receive a reward and be reborn in heaven, gaining double the merit." What was said is extensive, but a brief summary is provided. The speaker leaves and says, "You should endure many lifetimes, suffering severe karmic consequences. Because you have heard the teachings of the scriptures and developed a joyful heart, now you will experience a lighter karmic consequence. After one cycle, you will be free. You will be saved and live, and can become a monk.

    70

    洛阳、临淄、建业、鄮阴、成都五处并有阿育王塔。又吴中两石像，育王所使鬼神造也。颇得真相。能往礼拜者，不堕地狱。”语已东行。荷作礼而别。出南大道，广百余步。道上行者，不可称计。道边有高座高数十丈，有沙门坐之。左右僧众，列倚甚多。有人执笔，北面而立，谓荷曰：“在襄阳时，何故杀鹿？”跪答曰：“他人射鹿，我加创耳。又不啖肉，何缘受报？”时即见襄阳杀鹿之地，草树山涧，忽然满目。所乘黑马，并皆能言。悉证荷杀鹿年月时日。

    Explanation

    70

    There are five places that all have the Ashoka Stupa: Luoyang, Linzi, Jianye, Maoyin, and Chengdu. Additionally, there are two stone statues in Wu, created by the ghosts and spirits commanded by Emperor Ashoka. These statues are quite true to life. Those who go to worship them will not fall into hell.

    He then traveled eastward. He made a bow and left. The southern main road was wide over a hundred steps. The number of people walking on the road was incalculable. On both sides of the road, many monks were lined up. A person holding a brush stood facing north and said to He, "When you were in Xiangyang, why did you kill the deer?" He knelt and answered, "Someone else shot the deer, and I just added a wound. I didn't eat the meat, so why should I be punished?" At that moment, He saw the place in Xiangyang where the deer was killed, with grass, trees, mountains, and ravines suddenly filling his vision. The black horse he was riding could also speak, and all confirmed the year, month, day, and hour when He killed the deer.

    71

    荷惧然无对。须臾，有人以??之，投镬汤中。自视四体，溃然烂碎。有风吹身，聚小岸边，忽然不觉还复全形。执笔者复问：“汝又射雉，亦尝杀雁。”言已，?投镬汤，如前烂法。受此报已，乃遣荷去。入一大城，有人居焉。谓荷曰：“汝受轻罪，又得还生，是福力所扶。而今以后，复作罪不？”乃遣人送荷。遥见故身，意不欲还。送人推引，久久乃附形，而得稣活。奉法精勤，遂即出家。字曰慧达。太元末，尚在京师。后往许昌，不知所终。珠林八十六

    Explanation

    71

    The man was greatly frightened and had no response. After a moment, someone brought something (unclear) to him and threw him into a cauldron of boiling water. He looked at his body, which was rotten and shattered. There was a wind that blew him, gathering him at a small shore. Suddenly, without realizing it, he returned to his complete form. The recorder asked again: "You also shot a pheasant, and also killed a goose." After he finished speaking, he was thrown into the cauldron of boiling water again, as before, in the same way of rotting. After receiving this retribution, they sent him away. He entered a large city where people lived. They told him: "You have received a light punishment, and have been reborn, this is due to the power of good fortune. From now on, will you commit more sins?" They then sent someone to send him. He saw his old body from afar and did not want to return. The person who was sending him pushed and pulled, and after a long time, he attached to his form and revived. He diligently followed the law and then immediately left home to become a monk. His name was Huidat. At the end of the Taoyuan period, he was still in the capital. Later, he went to Xuchang, and no one knows what happened to him. Zhu Lin 86.

    72

    晋沙门竺法纯，山阴显义寺主也。晋元兴中，起寺行墙，至兰上买材。路经湖道。材主是妇人，而应共至材所，准许价直。遂与同船俱行。既入大湖，日?暴风，波浪如山。纯船小水入，命在瞬息。念值行无福，忽遇斯灾。又与妇人俱行，其以罔惧。乃一心诵观世音经。俄有大舟，泛流趣纯。适时既入夜，行旅已绝。纯自惟念，不应有此流船，疑是神力。既而共渡乘之。而此小船，应时即没。大舟随波鼓荡，俄得达其岸耳。珠林十七

    Explanation

    72

    During the Yuanxing period of the Jin dynasty, there was a monk named Zhi Fachuang, who served as the abbot of Xianyi Temple in Shanyin. While constructing a temple wall, he went to buy wood on the shore of Lan. On the way, they passed through a lake area, and the owner of the wood was a woman. They agreed to meet at the wood site and set the price. So, they went together on the same boat. Once they entered the large lake, a violent storm struck at dusk, with waves like mountains. The monk's small boat was flooded, and his life was in danger at any moment. He thought that he had no good fortune and suddenly encountered this disaster. Additionally, he was traveling with the woman, which greatly increased his fear. He then recited the Sutra of the Bodhisattva Guanyin with all his heart. Soon, a large boat appeared, floating toward him. At that time, it was already night, and there were no other travelers. Reflecting to himself, the monk wondered why there should have been such a flowing boat, suspecting it was a divine power. They then crossed together and boarded it. But the small boat immediately sank. The large boat followed the waves and moved, and soon reached the shore. This story is recorded in the Jade Forest, volume seventeen.

    73

    晋沙门释开达，隆安二年，登垄采甘草，为羌所执。时年大饥，羌胡相啖。乃至达栅中，将食之。先在栅者，有十余人；羌日夕亨俎，唯达尚存。自达被执，便潜诵观世音经，不懈乎心。及明日当见啖，其晨始曙，忽有大虎，遥逼群羌。奋怒号吼。羌各骇怖迸走。虎乃前啮栅木，得成小阕，可容人过。已而徐去。达初见虎啮栅，必谓见害。既栅穿而不入，心疑其异。将是观音力。计度诸羌，未应便反，即穿栅逃走；夜行昼伏，遂得免脱。珠林十七

    Explanation

    73

    A Buddhist monk named Sishikaikai from the Eastern Jin Dynasty, during the second year of the Long'an era, climbed a ridge to gather licorice when he was captured by the Qiang people. That year was marked by a severe famine, and the Qiang and Hu people were so desperate that they resorted to eating each other. He was taken into a stockade, where he was to be eaten along with ten or so others who were already confined there. The Qiang people prepared meals daily, but only Sishikaikai survived. From the moment he was captured, he secretly recited the Guanyin Sutra without ceasing in his heart. On the day he was scheduled to be eaten, just as dawn began to break, a large tiger suddenly appeared, roaring angrily at the Qiang people. Terrified, they scattered and fled. The tiger then approached the wooden fence, biting it until a small opening was created, large enough for a person to pass through. Afterward, the tiger slowly left. Initially, Sishikaikai thought the tiger would attack him, but when the fence was breached and the tiger did not enter, he began to suspect that something unusual was happening. He believed it was the power of Guanyin. Calculating that the Qiang people would not return immediately, he broke through the fence and fled, traveling at night and hiding during the day, and ultimately escaped. This account is recorded in the Zhu Lin (Jewel Grove), chapter seventeen.

    74

    晋潘道秀，吴郡人。年二十余，为军纠主北为征固。案此句有讹广记引作尝随军北征既而军小失利。秀窜逸被掠。经数处作奴。俘虏异域，欲归无因。少信佛法，恒志心念观世音。每梦寐，辄见像。广记引有像字后既南奔，迷不知道；于穷山中，忽睹真形，如今行像。因作礼。礼竟，豁然不觉失之。二句广记引作恰然不觉安行乃得还路，遂归本土。后精进弥笃。年垂六十而亡。珠林十七广记一百十
    　　晋栾苟，广记引并作荀不知何许人也，少奉法，尝作福富平令，先从征庐循，值小失利，船舫遭火垂尽，贼亦交逼：正在中江，风浪骇目，苟恐怖分尽，犹诵念观世音。俄见江中有一人挺然孤立，腰与水齐，苟心知祈念有感，火贼己切，广记引无此句便投水就之。身既浮涌，脚以履地寻而大军遣船迎接败者，遂得免济。珠林十七广记一百十

    Explanation

    74

    Pan Daoxiu of Wu County, during the Jin dynasty, was in his twenties when he served as a military officer and was dispatched to the north. According to the Guangji (Miscellaneous Records), the original text may have an error, and the correct version is: "He once followed the army north and the army suffered a small defeat." Pan Daoxiu fled and was captured, and he was enslaved in several places. Captured in a foreign land, he had no way to return home. He had faith in Buddhism and constantly prayed to Guanyin. In his dreams, he often saw images of Guanyin. Later, he fled south and became lost. In a remote mountain, he suddenly encountered a true image of Guanyin, as if it were a moving statue. He performed a ritual of worship. After the ritual was completed, he suddenly realized that the image had disappeared. According to the Guangji, an alternative reading is: "He suddenly realized that he was safe and found his way home, thus returning to his native land." After this, he became even more devout. He died at nearly sixty years old. Recorded in Zhulin 17 and Guangji 110.

    Luang Gou, according to the Guangji, whose name is also written as Luan Gou, was an unknown person who, in his youth, practiced the Dharma. He once served as the magistrate of Fuping and was dispatched to the south to suppress Lu Xun. He suffered a small defeat, and his ships were nearly destroyed by fire, while the enemy was also closing in. In the middle of the river, the wind and waves were terrifying, and Luang Gou was filled with fear. He continued to recite the name of Guanyin. Suddenly, he saw a person standing alone in the middle of the river, waist-deep in water. Luang Gou knew that his prayers had been answered. The fire and the enemy were now at bay. He jumped into the water to join the person. His body floated and rose, and his feet touched the ground. Soon after, the main army sent ships to rescue the defeated soldiers, and he was saved. Recorded in Zhulin 17 and Guangji 110.

    75

    晋沙门释法智为白衣时，常独行，至大泽中，忽遇猛火，四方俱起，走路已绝，便至心礼诵观世音；俄然火过，一泽之草，无有遗茎者，唯智所处容身不烧。于是始乃敬奉大法。后为姚兴将，从征索虏，军退，失马，落在围里；乃隐沟边荆棘丛中，得蔽头，复念观世音，心甚勤至。隔沟人遥唤后军，指令煞之，而军过搜觅辄无见者，遥得免济。后遂出家。珠林十七广记一百十
    　　晋南宫子敖，始平人也，戍新平城，为佛佛虏儿长乐公所破，合城数千人皆被诛害。子敖虽分必死，而犹至心念观世音。既而次至子敖，群刃交下，或高或僻，持刀之人，或疲懈四支不随。尔时长乐公亲自临刑，惊问之，子敖聊尔答云：“能作马鞍。”乃令原释。子敖亦不知所作此言。时后遂得遁逸。造小形像，广记引作乃造一观音小像贮以香函，行则顶戴也。珠林十七广记一百十

    Explanation

    75

    During the Jin dynasty, there was a monk named Fa Zhi, who was once a layperson. He often traveled alone and one day found himself in a marsh, where he suddenly encountered a fierce fire that erupted from all directions, blocking all escape routes. In his desperate situation, he sincerely recited and chanted the name of Guanyin. Suddenly, the fire passed, and all the grass in the marsh was completely burned, except for the spot where Fa Zhi stood, which remained unscathed. Thus, he began to revere and follow the great law (Dharma). Later, he became a general under Emperor Yao Xing and followed him to fight against the Xianbei. When the army retreated, he lost his horse and was captured. He hid in a thorny bush by a ditch, managed to cover his head, and continued to recite the name of Guanyin with a very sincere and earnest heart. People on the other side of the ditch called out to the rear army to execute him, but when the army passed and searched, they could not find him. He was saved from afar. Later, he became a monk. According to the Zhulin (Jade Forest) and Guangji (Extensive Records), volume 17, page 110.

    In the Jin dynasty, there was a layperson named Nan Gong Ziao from Shiping. He was garrisoning at Xiping City and was defeated by the Longle Prince of the Fofo (Xianbei) tribe. Thousands of people in the city were all killed. Although Nan Gong Ziao knew he would surely die, he still sincerely recited the name of Guanyin. Later, it was his turn, and multiple swords came down, some high, some low, or some off-target. The person holding the knife was tired and his limbs did not follow his commands. At that time, the Longle Prince personally oversaw the execution and asked him in surprise. Nan Gong Ziao casually replied, "Can make a saddle." Then he was spared. Nan Gong Ziao did not know why he said this. Later, he managed to escape. He made a small statue of Guanyin and kept it in a fragrant box, carrying it on his head when traveling. According to the Guangji (Extensive Records), volume 17, page 110.

    76

    晋刘度，平原辽城人也乡里有一千余家，并奉大法，造立形像，供养僧尼。值虏主木未时此县尝有逋逃，未大怒，欲尽灭一城。众并凶惧，分必殄尽。度乃洁诚率众归命观世音。顷之，未见物从空中下，绕其所住屋柱；惊视，乃观世音经。使人读之，广记引无此句未大欢喜，用省刑戮。于是此城即得免害。珠林十一广记一百十
    　　晋郭宣之，太原人也，义熙四年，为杨思平梁州府司马。杨以辄害范元之等被法，宣亦同执在狱，唯一心归向观世音菩萨。后夕将眠之际，忽亲睹菩萨光明照狱，宣瞻觌礼拜，祈请誓愿，久之乃没。俄而宣之独被恩赦。既释，依所见形，制造图像，又立精舍焉。后历零陵衡阳，卒官。珠林十七

    Explanation

    76

    Jin Dynasty Liu Du, from Liaocheng in the Plain (a region in modern-day Shandong), lived in a village with over a thousand households, all of whom followed the great law, created images, and provided support for monks and nuns. During the time of the foreign ruler "Mumu," this county had some fugitives, and the ruler "未" became extremely angry, wanting to completely destroy the city. The people were all terrified and believed they would inevitably be destroyed. Liu Du then sincerely led the people to dedicate themselves to the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara. Soon, something descended from the sky and circled around the pillar of the house where they resided. They were surprised and saw it was the Sutra of Avalokiteshvara. They had someone read it, and it was found that the widely recorded text did not contain this sentence. The ruler "未" was greatly pleased and thus spared the punishment. Thus, this city was spared from harm. (From the "Jewel Treasury" Volume 11, "Broad Record" Volume 110)

    Jin Dynasty Guo Xuanzhi, from Taiyuan, served as the Military Governor of Liangzhou in the fourth year of the Yixi era (408 AD). Yang Siping was accused of harming Fan Yuanzhi and others and thus subjected to the law, and Guo Xuanzhi was also imprisoned with him. He dedicated himself solely to the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara. One night, as he was about to sleep, he suddenly witnessed the light of the Bodhisattva illuminating the prison. He gazed upon, worshipped, and prayed, vowing for a long time until the light disappeared. Soon, Guo Xuanzhi was uniquely granted amnesty. After being released, he created images based on what he had seen and established a meditation hall. Later, he served in various places such as Lingling and Hengyang, and died in office. (From the "Jewel Treasury" Volume 17)

    77

    晋新野庾绍之，小字道覆，晋湘东太守，与南阳宋协中表昆弟，情好绸缪。绍元兴卒，病卒，义熙中，忽见形诣协，形貌衣服，具如平生，而两脚着械。既至，脱械置地而坐。协问：“何由得顾？”答云：“蹔蒙假归，与卿亲好，故相过也。”协问：鬼神之事，绍辄漫略，不甚谐对。唯云：“宜勤精进，不可杀生；若不能都断，可勿宰牛，食肉之时，无啖物心。”协云：“五脏与肉，乃复异耶？”答曰：“心者，善神之宅也，其罪尤重。”具问亲戚，因谈世事，末复求酒。协时时饵茱萸酒，因为设之。酒至，对杯不饮，云有茱萸气。协曰：“为恶之耶？”答云：“下官皆畏之，非独我也。”绍为人语声高壮，此言论时不异恒日。有顷，协儿邃之来，绍闻屐声，极有惧色，谓协曰：“生气见陵，不复得住；与卿三年别耳！”因贯械而起，出户便灭。协后为正员郎，果三年而卒珠林九十四广记三百二十四

    Explanation

    77

    Jin Xinjiang's Yu Shaozhi, with the nickname Dao Fu, was the governor of Xiangdong during the Eastern Jin Dynasty. He had a close relationship with NanYang's Song Xie, who was his cousin and brother-in-law, and their affection was deep and enduring. Yu Shaozhi died in the first year of Yuanxing due to illness. In the first year of Yixi, he suddenly appeared in the form of a spirit to visit Song Xie. His appearance and attire were exactly as they had been in life, but his feet were bound with shackles. Upon arrival, he removed the shackles and placed them on the ground before sitting down. Song Xie asked, "Why have you come to see me?" Yu Shaozhi replied, "I have been temporarily allowed to return, and because of our close relationship, I have come to visit you." Song Xie asked about matters related to spirits and the supernatural, but Yu Shaozhi spoke vaguely and did not provide detailed answers. He only said, "You should strive for spiritual advancement, not kill living beings; if you cannot completely abstain, do not slaughter cows, and when eating meat, do not consume the heart." Song Xie asked, "Is the heart different from other parts of the body?" Yu Shaozhi replied, "The heart is the dwelling place of the benevolent spirit, and its sin is particularly heavy." He then inquired about Song Xie's relatives and discussed worldly affairs. At the end, he requested wine. Song Xie often drank wine with wormwood, so he prepared it for Yu Shaozhi. When the wine was served, Yu Shaozhi did not drink, saying there was a scent of wormwood. Song Xie said, "Is it because it is bad?" Yu Shaozhi replied, "All of us fear it, not just me." Yu Shaozhi had a loud and strong voice, and during this conversation, it was no different from his usual self. After a while, Song Xie's son Shuo Zhi came, and Yu Shaozhi heard the sound of his footsteps and became extremely frightened. He told Song Xie, "I am being oppressed by living energy and cannot stay here anymore; I will be separated from you for three years!" He then put on the shackles and stood up, and upon exiting the door, he disappeared. Song Xie later became a regular official, and indeed, he died three years later. (From Jade Forest 94 and Record of the Marvelous 324)

    78

    晋沙门释法安者，庐山之僧远法师弟子也，义熙末，阳新县虎暴甚盛，县有大社树，下有筑神庙，左右民居以百数。遭虎死者夕必一两，法安尝游其县，?投此屯，民以惧虎，早闭门闾，且不识法安，不肯受之。法安遥之树下，坐禅通夜，向晓，有虎负人而至，投树之北，见安，如喜如跳，伏安前，安为说法授戒，虎据地不动，有顷而去。至旦，屯人追死者至树下，见安大惊，谓其神人，故虎不害。自兹以后，而虎患遂息。众益敬异，一县士庶，略皆奉法。后欲画像山壁，不能得空青，欲用铜青，而又无铜。夜梦人迳其床前云：“此中有两铜钟，便可取之。”安明即掘得，遂以成像。后远法师铸像，安送一劝助；余一，武昌太守熊无患借观之，遂留不改。法苑珠林十九

    Explanation

    78

    A Buddhist monk named Fa'an, a disciple of Master Yuan of Mount Lu, was traveling to Yangxin County during the end of the Yìxī era. At the time, tigers were rampant in the area, and there was a large sacred tree in the county with a temple built beneath it. The surrounding settlements housed hundreds of families. Every evening, a few people were killed by tigers. One day, Fa'an arrived in the county and stayed in a settlement. The people were afraid of the tigers and closed their doors early, and not knowing Fa'an, they did not accept him. Fa'an sat in meditation under the tree through the night. Early in the morning, a tiger carrying a person arrived and approached the tree. Seeing Fa'an, the tiger jumped around excitedly, lay down in front of him, and Fa'an taught it precepts. The tiger stood still and then left. By dawn, the people of the settlement followed the dead to the tree and saw Fa'an, greatly surprised. They thought he was a divine being, so the tiger did not harm them. From then on, the tiger problem ceased. The people became more respectful and amazed, and almost all of them followed the law (or religious precepts). Later, Fa'an wanted to paint an image on the mountain wall but could not find blue stone, so he wanted to use green stone, but there was no copper. He dreamed of someone passing by his bed and saying, "There are two bronze bells here, you can take them." In the morning, Fa'an dug them up and used them to complete the image. Later, when Master Yuan cast an image, Fa'an contributed one. The other one was borrowed by the governor of Wuchang, Xiong Wuhuan, to view and remained with him.

    79

    汉案当作晋珠林误题沙门竺昙盖秦郡人也，真确有苦行，持钵振锡，取给四辈。居于蒋山。常行般舟，尤善神祝，多有应验。司马元显甚敬奉之，卫将军刘毅闻其精苦，招来姑孰，深相爱遇。义兴案当作义熙五年，大旱，陂湖竭涸，苗稼焦枯，祈祭山川，累旬无应；毅乃请僧设斋，盖亦在焉。斋毕，躬乘露桁，浮泛川溪，文武士庶，倾州悉行。盖于中流，焚香礼拜，至诚慷慨，乃读海龙王经；造卷发音，云气便起，转读将半，沛泽四合，才及释轴，洪雨滂注，畦湖毕满，其年以登。刘敬叔时为毅国郎中令，亲豫此集，自所睹见。珠林六十三

    Explanation

    79

    A Monk Named Zhi Tan

    During the Jin Dynasty, a monk named Zhi Tan, from the Qin Prefecture, was known for his true virtue and ascetic practices. He carried a begging bowl and a staff, providing for the four classes of people (monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen). He resided on Jiangshan Mountain. He often practiced the "Banzhou" meditation and was particularly skilled in divination and exorcism, with many of his predictions and rituals proving accurate. Emperor Yuanxian of the Jin Dynasty held him in high respect and venerated him. General Liu Yi, upon hearing of his rigorous practices, invited him to Gusu, where he was deeply loved and cherished. In the fifth year of the Yixi era (405 AD), a severe drought struck, causing ponds and lakes to dry up and crops to wither and die. Despite repeated prayers and sacrifices to mountains and rivers, there was no response for many days. General Yi then invited monks to perform a ritual meal, and Zhi Tan was among them. After the meal, he personally rode in a carriage, floating on rivers and streams. Literati, soldiers, and commoners from the entire state participated in the ritual. Zhi Tan, in the middle of the river, burned incense and performed worship with sincerity and enthusiasm. He then read aloud from the Sutra of the Dragon King of the Sea. As he began to read, clouds formed. Halfway through, rain fell in all directions. Just as he finished reading the scroll, heavy rain poured down, filling all ponds and fields. That year, there was a bountiful harvest. Liu Jingshu, who was serving as a Langzhongling under General Yi, personally attended this gathering and witnessed these events. This account is recorded in Chapter 63 of the Jade Forest.

    80

    晋向靖，字奉仁，河内人也，在吴兴郡丧数岁女。四字广记引作有一女数岁而亡女始病时，弄小刀子，母夺取不与，伤母手。丧后一年，母又产一女，女年四岁，谓母曰：“前时刀子何在？”母曰：“无也。”女曰：“昔争刀子，故伤母手，云何无耶？”母甚惊怪，具以告靖，靖曰：“先刀子犹在不？”母曰：“痛念前女，故不录之。”靖曰：“可更觅数个刀子，合置一处，令女自择。”女见大喜，即取先者曰：“此是儿许。”父母大小乃知前女审其先身。珠林二十六广记三百八十七引至即取先者

    Explanation

    80

    During the Jin dynasty, Xiang Jing, courtesy name Fengren, was a man from Hedong. He had a daughter in Wuxing who died at a young age. The Four-Character Notes cite a story about a girl who died at a young age. When she first fell ill, she played with a small knife, and her mother took it away from her, causing the child to injure her mother's hand. A year after her death, the mother gave birth to another daughter, who was four years old. The girl asked her mother, "Where is the knife from before?" The mother replied, "It is not here." The girl said, "We argued over the knife before, so I hurt your hand. How can it not be here?" Her mother was greatly surprised and informed Xiang Jing about this. Xiang Jing asked, "Is the previous knife still around?" The mother replied, "I am too heartbroken to remember the past, so I did not keep it." Xiang Jing suggested, "Find several knives, put them together in one place, and let the girl choose." The girl saw them and was very happy, immediately picking up the original one and saying, "This is mine." The parents and others then realized that the deceased daughter had a clear memory of her past life. This story is cited in Zhu Lin volume 26 and Guang Ji volume 387, specifically up to the point where the girl takes the knife.

    81

    赵石长和者，赵国高邑人也，年十九时，病一月余日亡。家贫，未能及时得殡敛，经四日而稣。说：初死时，东南行，见二人治道，在和前五十步，和行有迟疾，二人治道亦随缓速，常五十步。而道之两边，棘刺森然，皆如鹰爪，见人甚众，群走棘中，身体伤裂，地皆流血。见和独行平道，俱叹息曰：“佛子独行大道中。”前至，见瓦屋采楼，可数千闲，有屋甚高，上有一人，形面壮大，着皂袍四缝，临窗而坐。和拜之，广记引作升之阁上人曰：“石君来耶？一别二千余年。”长和尔时意中便若忆此别时也，和相识有马牧孟丞夫妻，先死已积年岁，阁上人曰：“君识孟丞不？”长和曰：“识。”阁上人曰：“孟丞生时不能精进，今恒为我司埽除之役；孟丞妻精进，居处甚乐。

    Explanation

    81

    Zhaoshi Changhe was a man from Gaoyi in Zhao. At the age of nineteen, he fell ill for more than a month and died. Due to poverty, he could not be buried in time, and after four days, he revived. He recounted: "At the time of my initial death, I traveled southeast and saw two people repairing the road, fifty steps ahead of me. As I walked at varying speeds, the two people also adjusted their pace to match, always maintaining a distance of fifty steps. The path on either side was lined with dense thorns, all like eagle claws. Many people rushed into the thorns, suffering severe injuries, and blood flowed everywhere. Seeing me walking alone on a flat path, they all sighed and said, 'The Buddha's child walks alone on the great road.' As I continued, I came to a place with tile-roofed houses and colorful towers, numbering in the thousands. There was a particularly tall house, and on top of it, a man with a large and imposing appearance was sitting by the window, wearing a black robe with four seams. I bowed to him, and the man on the upper floor said, 'Is it you, Stone? We have been separated for more than two thousand years.' At that moment, I felt as if I remembered this separation. I knew a couple named Ma Mu Shengcheng and his wife, who had died many years ago. The man on the upper floor asked, 'Do you recognize Shengcheng?' I replied, 'I do.' He said, 'Shengcheng did not strive diligently in life and now serves as a cleaner for me; his wife, however, was diligent and lives very happily.'

    82

    ”举手指西南一房曰：“孟妻在此也。”孟妻开窗见和，厚相慰问，遍访其家中大小安不消息，曰：“石君还时，可更见过，当因附书也。”俄见孟丞执?提箕，自阁西来，亦问家消息。阁上人曰：“闻鱼龙超精进为信，尔何所修行？”长和曰：“不食鱼肉，酒不经口，恒转尊经，救诸疾痛。”阁上人曰？“所传不妄也。”语久之闲，阁上人问都录主者：“审案石君名录，勿谬滥也。”主者案录云：“余三十年命在。”阁上人曰：“君欲归不？”和对曰：“愿归。”乃敕主者，以车骑两吏送之。长和拜辞，上车而归。前所行道，更有传馆吏民饮食储跱之具。倏忽至家，恶其尸臭，不欲附之，于尸头立；见其家亡妹于后推之，踣尸面上，因得稣活。道人支法山时未出家，闻和所说，遂定入道之志。法山者，咸和时人也。珠林七广记三百八十三

    82

    He pointed to a room in the southwest and said, "Meng's wife is here." Meng's wife opened the window and saw Chang He, and gave heartfelt condolences, inquiring about the well-being of all members of his family. She said, "When Master Shi returns, you can visit again, and I will send a letter." Soon, she saw Meng the Chancellor carrying a basket, coming from the west of the hall, and also asked about the family news. The person on the veranda said, "Have you heard that Fish and Dragon have advanced spiritually? What have you practiced?" Chang He replied, "I do not eat fish or meat, do not drink alcohol, always recite the scriptures, and help those in pain." The person on the veranda said, "What has been said is not false." After talking for a while, the person on the veranda asked the chief recorder, "Check the list of Master Shi, do not make mistakes." The chief recorder checked the list and said, "I have thirty years of life left." The person on the veranda said, "Do you want to return?" Chang He replied, "I wish to return." Then, he ordered the chief recorder to send two officials by carriage to escort him. Chang He bowed and took leave, then got on the carriage and returned. On the way, there were more relay stations with officials and civilians storing food and supplies. Suddenly, he arrived home, disliked the smell of the corpse, did not want to touch it, and stood at the head of the corpse. He saw his deceased sister-in-law push him from behind, causing him to fall on the face of the corpse, and thus he revived. Monk Zhi Fashan, who had not yet entered the monastic life, heard what He said and thus decided to enter the path of the Dharma. Fashan was a person of the Xianhe period. Jewel Forest, Volume Seven, General Records, Chapter Three Hundred and Eighty-Three.

    赵沙门单，或作善，字道开，不知何许人也。别传高僧传在佛调之止舟云，炖煌人，本姓孟，少出家，欲穷栖岩谷，故先断谷食。初进?，三年后服练松脂，三十年后唯时吞小石子，石子下，辄复断酒脯杂果。体畏风寒，唯啖椒姜，气力微弱，而肤色润泽，行步如飞。山神数试，未曾倾动，仙人恒来，意亦不耐，每啮蒜以却之。端坐静念，昼夜不眠。久住抱罕，石虎建武二年，自西平迎来，至邺下，不乘舟车，日行七百余里。

    Explanation

    83

    A Buddhist monk named Shan, sometimes written as Shan, with the courtesy name Dao Kai, whose origin is unknown. In a separate biography in the High Monks' Transmission and the story of Buddha adjusting his boat, it is said that he was from Dunhuang and originally surnamed Meng. He became a monk at a young age and wanted to live in remote mountains and valleys, so he first stopped eating grains. Initially, he took some unspecified substance, and three years later, he began to take pine resin. Thirty years later, he only occasionally swallowed small stones. After the stones passed, he stopped drinking alcohol and eating meat and fruits. His body fears cold and wind, and he only eats pepper and ginger. His strength is weak, but his skin is smooth and lustrous, and he walks like a flying bird. Mountain gods frequently tested him, but he never wavered. Immortals often came to him, but he also did not tolerate them. He would chew garlic to repel them. He sat quietly and meditated, never sleeping day or night. He stayed for a long time in Bao Han. In the second year of Jianwu reign of Shi Hu, he was brought from Xiping and arrived at Ye. He did not ride in boats or carriages and traveled over seven hundred miles a day.

    84

    A Man of Asceticism and Benevolence

    Passing through Nan'an, he initiated a young boy, aged thirteen or fourteen, as a novice monk. The boy's behavior was also mature. Upon arrival, he resided in the Zhaode Pagoda, wearing coarse and tattered robes, often exposing his back. Inside the house, he built a small pavilion, about eight or nine feet high, and wove reeds into a canopy, meditating within it. He abstained from food for seven years, regularly taking various medicines, which had the scent of pine resin and poria. Skilled in treating eye diseases, he frequently traveled through the countryside, healing the common people. Both local and distant nobles offered gifts, which he accepted and distributed, leaving nothing for himself. At the end of Shi Hu's reign, foreseeing the chaos, he moved south to Xuchang with his disciples. In the third year of Shengping, he came to Jianye, then traveled to Panyu, residing on Luofu Mountain, resting in the shade of the forest, finding joy in solitude. He died in July of that year, leaving a final instruction to be buried in the woods, which his disciples followed. In the first year of Xingning, Chen Jun's Yuan Yanbo, as the governor of Nanhai, climbed this mountain with his brother Ying Shu to pay respects to his remains, burning incense and performing rituals. Jewel Forest, Chapter 27.

    秦徐义者，高陆人也，少奉法，为苻坚尚书。坚末，兵革蜂起，贼获义，将加戮害，乃埋其两足，编发于树。夜中专念观世音，有顷得眠，梦人谓之曰：“今事亟矣，何暇眠乎？”义便惊起，见守防之士，并疲而寝；乃试自奋动，手发既解，足亦得脱，因而遁去。百余步，隐小丛草，便闻追者交驰，火炬星陈，互绕此丛，而竟无见者。天明，贼散，归投邺寺，遂得免之。珠林十七广记一百十
    　　秦毕览，东平人也，少奉法，随慕容垂北征，没虏，单马逃窜。虏追骑将及，览至心诵念观世音；既得免脱，因入深山，迷惑失道，又专心归念，中夜，见一道人，法服持锡，示以途径，遂得还路，安隐至家。珠林十七广记一百十

    Explanation

    85

    In the Qin state, there was a man named Xu Yi from Gaolü. When he was young, he served the law and became a high official under Fu Jian. During the later years of Fu Jian's reign, widespread military uprisings broke out, and Xu Yi was captured by the rebels, who intended to kill him. They buried his feet and tied his hair to a tree. At night, Xu Yi devoted himself to chanting the name of Guanyin (Avalokiteshvara). After a while, he fell asleep and had a dream where a person told him, "The situation is urgent, why should you sleep?" Xu Yi woke up suddenly and saw that the guards were all tired and asleep. He then tried to move himself, and his hands were freed, and his feet also escaped. Thus, he fled. After a hundred steps, he hid in a small patch of grass and heard the pursuers passing by, their torches arranged in a star-like formation, circling around the patch of grass, but they never saw him. When dawn came, the rebels dispersed, and Xu Yi returned to the temple in Ye, thus escaping. This story is recorded in Zhulin (Jade Forest) Volume 17, Chapter 110.

    In the Qin state, there was another man named Bi Luan from Dongping. When he was young, he served the law and followed Murong Chui on a northern campaign, where he was captured by the enemy and fled alone on horseback. The enemy's cavalry was about to catch up, so Bi Luan devoted himself to chanting the name of Guanyin. After escaping, he entered a deep mountain and lost his way. He then focused his mind on returning, and in the middle of the night, he saw a monk in monastic robes holding a staff, who showed him the way. Thus, he found his way back and arrived safely home. This story is also recorded in Zhulin (Jade Forest) Volume 17, Chapter 110.

    In the Song dynasty, there was a monk named Fa Chen. On his deathbed, he said, "A man from Songshan told me, 'The General Liu in Jiangdong should receive the mandate of heaven.' He also gave me thirty-two jade disks and a piece of gold as proof." Emperor Song heard this and ordered the monk Hu Yi to go to Songshan, where he practiced for seven days and seven nights. Hu Yi dreamed of an old man with a long beard who pointed the way. When he woke up, he clearly remembered the location and dug it up. This story is recorded in Guangji (Extensive Records) Volume 276.

    宋仇那跋摩者，此言功德，高僧传云此言功德铠案拔摩是铠记误也种罽宾王子也，幼而出家，号三藏法师。宋初，来游中国，宣译至典甚众。律行精高，莫与为比。惠高僧传惠作慧观沙门钦其风德，要来京师，居于只洹寺。当时来诣者，疑非凡人，而神味深密，莫能测焉。尝赴请于钟山定林寺，时诸道俗多采众华，布僧席下，验求真人；诸僧所坐，华同萎悴，而跋摩席华，鲜荣若初，于是京师歙然增加敬意。至元嘉八年九月十八日卒，都无痾患，但结跏趺坐，敛衽?手，乃经信宿，容色不变。于时或谓深禅，既而得遗书于筵下，云获沙门二果，乃知其终。弟子侍侧，普闻馨烟。京师赴会二百余人，其夕转经，户外集听盈阶。将晓，而西南上有云气勃然，俄有一物，长将一?，绕尸而去，同集咸睹云。跋未亡时，作三十偈，以付弟子曰：“可送示天竺僧也。”法苑珠林四十二

    Explanation

    86

    The Translator of Merit: Master Kao Na

    This is called the Translator of Merit. According to the Biographies of Eminent Monks, it means "merit armor," but the record is in error. He was a prince of Kāpiśa (Kāśmīra) who, at a young age, entered the monastic life and was known as a Tripiṭaka Master. In the early Song dynasty, he came to China, where he translated many important Buddhist scriptures. His observance of precepts was extremely high, unmatched by others. Master Huiguan, a monk, admired his virtue and invited him to the capital, where he lived at the Jetavana Monastery.

    At that time, those who came to see him suspected that he was not an ordinary person, but his spiritual essence was profound and mysterious, beyond comprehension. He once attended a gathering at Dinglin Temple on Zhongshan Mountain. At that time, many laypeople and monks picked various flowers and placed them under the monk's seat to test for a true sage. The flowers under the other monks' seats withered, but the flowers under Master Kao's seat remained fresh and vibrant. Thus, the capital city's respect for him increased.

    He passed away on the 18th day of the 9th month in the 8th year of the Yuanjia era (431 AD). He died without any illness, just sitting in the full lotus position, with his sleeves folded and hands together, for two nights, with his appearance unchanged. At that time, some thought he was in deep meditation, but later a note was found under the seat saying he had attained the second level of arhatship, thus it was known that he had passed away. His disciples who were by his side smelled a fragrant smoke. Over 200 people from the capital came to the gathering, and that evening, as they chanted scriptures, people gathered outside the door, filling the steps.

    As dawn approached, a dense cloud appeared in the southwest, and soon a creature, about a foot long, circled his body and then disappeared. All present saw this. Before he passed away, he composed thirty verses and said to his disciples, "You can show these to monks from India." This account is found in Chapter 42 of The Jewel Forest of the Dharma Realm.

    宋陈安居者，襄阳县人也，伯父少事巫俗，鼓舞祭祀，神影庙宇，充满其宅；父独敬信释法，旦夕斋戒。后伯父亡，无子，父以安居绍焉。安居虽即伯舍，而理行精求，淫飨之事，废不复设。于是遂得笃病，而发则为歌神之曲，迷闷惛僻，如此者弥岁，而执心愈固。常誓曰：“若我不杀之志，遂当亏夺者，必先自脔截四体，乃就其事。”家人并谏之，安居不听。经积二年，永初元年，病发，遂绝，但心下微暖，家人不敛；至七日夜，守视之者，觉尸足闲如有风来飘衣动衾，于是而稣有声，家人初惧尸蹶，并走避之，既而稍能转动，末求饮浆，家人喜之，问从何来？安居乃具说所经见云：初有人若使者；将刀数十，呼将去。从者欲缚之，使者曰：“此人有福，未可缚也。

    Explanation

    87

    A Man Named Chen Anju from Xiangyang County

    Chen Anju was a native of Xiangyang County in the state of Song. His elder uncle was involved in shamanistic customs, performing dances and sacrifices, with temple images and structures filling his house. His father, on the other hand, alone revered and trusted Buddhist law, practicing daily fasting and purification. After the elder uncle died without an heir, the father designated Anju as his successor. Although Anju inherited the elder uncle's house, he pursued a more refined and disciplined life, abandoning excessive feasting and sacrificial rituals. As a result, he fell ill severely, and during his episodes, he would sing songs to the gods, becoming confused and dazed. This persisted for a year, and his resolve grew stronger. He often vowed, "If my determination to kill (possibly referring to himself) were to be thwarted, I would first cut off my limbs before proceeding." His family tried to dissuade him, but Anju refused to listen. After two years, in the first year of Yongchu, his illness flared up, and he seemingly died, but with warmth still in his chest, so the family did not bury him. On the seventh night, those watching noticed the corpse's feet moving as if wind was blowing, clothes and bedding fluttering, and then Anju made a sound of revival. Initially, the family feared the corpse was coming back to life and fled, but later, he began to move slightly and eventually asked for water. The family was delighted and asked where he had come from. Anju then detailed what he had experienced: initially, there was someone resembling a messenger; carrying many knives, he called for Anju to follow. The followers wanted to bind him, but the messenger said, "This person has good fortune, do not bind him."

    ”行三百许里，至一城府，楼宇甚整，使者将至数处，如局司所居，末有人授纸笔与安居曰：“可疏二十四通死名。”安居即如言疏名成数通，有一侍从内出，扬声大呼曰：“安居可入。”既入，称有教付刺奸狱，吏两人，一云：“与大械。”一云：“此人颇有福，可止三尺械。”疑论不判，乃共视文书，久之，遂与三尺械。有顷，见有贵人，翼从数十，形貌都雅，谓安居曰：“汝那得来？”安居具陈所由，贵人曰：“汝伯有罪，但宜录治，以先植小福，故蹔得游散，乃敢告诉？吾与汝父，幼少有旧，见汝依然可随我共游观也。”狱吏不肯释械，曰：“府君无教，不敢专辄。”贵人曰：“但付我，不使走逸也。”乃释之。贵人将安居遍至诸地狱，备观众苦，略与经文相符。游历未竟有传教来云：“府君唤安居。”安居茫惧然求救于贵人，贵人曰：“汝自无罪，但以实对，必无忧也。
