    88

    Traveled about three hundred li, Anju arrived at a city or administrative center where the buildings were very well-organized. The messenger went to several places, including the residence of the bureau director. Finally, someone gave paper and ink to Anju and said, "You can write down twenty-four names of the dead." Anju wrote down the names as instructed. A servant then came out and shouted loudly, "Anju, you may enter." Upon entering, it was said there was an order to hand over to the prison for investigating crimes. Two officials debated, one saying, "Use the large chain," and the other, "This person has quite a bit of fortune; a three-foot chain will suffice." Unable to reach a decision, they all looked at the documents for a long time and eventually decided to give him a three-foot chain. After a while, a noble person appeared with several attendants, his appearance very elegant. He asked Anju, "How did you come here?" Anju explained his situation. The noble person said, "Your uncle has a crime, but he should be recorded and punished. Because of a small amount of previous good fortune, you temporarily got to wander around, so you dared to report. I and your father had old acquaintances when young. Seeing you still, I can take you on a tour." The prison guard did not release the chain, saying, "The lord has no instruction; I dare not act on my own." The noble person replied, "Just give it to me; I will not let him escape." So they released him. The noble person took Anju to all the hells, showing him all the sufferings, which roughly matched the scriptures. While touring, a messenger came and said, "The lord calls Anju." Feeling confused and fearful, Anju sought help from the noble person. The noble person reassured him, "You yourself have no crime; just answer truthfully, and there will be no worry."

    89

    ”安居至合，见有钳梏者数百，一时俱进，安居在第三，既至阶下，一人服冠冕，立于囚前，读诸罪簿：其第一者云，昔娶妻之始，夫妇为誓，有子无子，终不相弃，而其人本是祭酒，妻亦奉道，共化导徒众，得士女弟子，因而奸之，遂弃本妻，妻常冤诉。府君曰：“汝夫妇违誓大义，不罪二，终罪一也；师资义着在三，而奸之，是父子相淫，无以异也。付法局详刑！”次读第二女人辞牒，忘其姓名，云家在南阳冠军县黄水里，家安爨器于福灶口，而此妇眠重，婴儿于灶上匍匐走行，粪污爨器中，此妇寤，已即请谢神，祗盥洗精熟，而其舅乃骂詈此妇，言无有天道鬼神，置此女人，得行污秽，司令闻知此，录送之。府君曰：“眠重非过，小儿无知，又已请谢神明，是无罪也；舅骂詈言无道，诬谤幽灵，可录之来。”须臾而到，赤索捉至。

    Explanation

    89

    Translation:

    At the assembly, there were hundreds of shackled prisoners who were brought forward all at once, and "Anju" was in the third position. Once they reached the steps below, a man wearing a crown stood before the prisoners and read the records of their crimes. The first entry stated that when the man married, he and his wife took an oath: whether they had children or not, they would never abandon each other. However, the man was originally a high-ranking official in a religious or scholarly organization, and his wife also followed the same path. Together, they led and educated many disciples, but he committed adultery and abandoned his original wife. The wife frequently complained of her injustice. The judge said, "You both violated the great principle of your vow, and you are not guilty of two crimes, but one; the relationship between teacher and disciple is sacred, and committing adultery is akin to incest, which is a grave sin. Hand this case over to the legal department for sentencing!"

    Next, the judge read the petition of the second woman. Her name is forgotten, but she said her home was in Huangshui Village, Junxian County, Nanyang. She had placed cooking utensils at the mouth of a special stove. One day, the woman slept heavily, and her baby crawled on the stove, defecating in the cooking utensils. Upon waking, the woman immediately apologized to the gods and washed the utensils thoroughly. However, her brother-in-law scolded her, saying there were no gods or spirits, and that she allowed such filth to occur. The officials heard about this and took her to be punished. The judge said, "Sleeping heavily is not a fault, and the baby was innocent. The woman had already apologized to the gods, so she is not guilty; your brother-in-law's scolding is unrighteous, and he is spreading false accusations against the spirits. He can be brought in for punishment." Shortly after, he was brought in with a red rope around his neck.

    90

    安居阶下人具读名牒，为伯所诉云云，府君曰：“此人事佛，大德人也！其伯杀害无辜，訾诳百姓，罪宜穷治；以昔有小福，故未加罪，伯今复谤诉无辜？”教催录取，未及至，而府君遣安居还，云：“若可还去，善成胜业，可寿九十三，努力勉之！勿复更来也。”安居出至合，局司云：“君可拔郤死名。”于是安居以次抽名既毕，而欲向游贵人所贵人亦至，云：“知汝无他，得还甚善，努力修功德；吾身福微，不办生天受报，于此辅佐府君，亦优游富乐神道之美。吾家在宛，姓某名某，还为吾致意：深尽奉法，勿犯佛禁，可具以所见示语之也。

    90

    Anju, the person at the lower level, read the list of names, and was complained about by his elder brother. The lord said, "This person worships the Buddha, a great virtuous person! His elder brother killed the innocent and slandered the people, and should be thoroughly investigated; because he had a little good fortune in the past, he was not punished. The elder brother now again defames the innocent?" The instruction was given to take him in, but before they could arrive, the lord sent Anju back, saying, "If you can return, good deeds will be accomplished, you can live to be ninety-three years old, strive hard! Do not come again." Anju left and went to the hall, the official said, "You can withdraw your name from the list of the dead." Thus, Anju removed his name one by one, and then decided to visit the noble person. The noble person also arrived, saying, "Knowing you have no other intentions, it is very good that you can return, strive hard to cultivate virtue; my own virtue is slight, I cannot ascend to heaven to receive reward, here to assist the lord, also enjoy the beauty of leisurely and wealthy spiritual life. My home is in Wan, my surname is [surname] and my name is [name], when you return, convey my greetings: deeply adhere to the law, do not violate the Buddhist precepts, you can fully tell them what you have seen."

    ”乃以三人送安居出门，数步，有专使送符与安居，谓曰：“君可持此符，经过戍逻以示之，勿辄偷过，偷过有徒?也。若有水碍，可以此符投水中，即得过也。”安居受符而归行久之，阻大江，不得渡，安居依言投符，蒙然如眩，乃是其家屋前中方地也。正闻家中号恸哭泣，所送之人，劝还就身，安居云：“身已臭秽吾不复能归。”此人乃强排之，踣于尸脚上。安居既愈，欲验黄水妇人，故往冠军县寻问；果有此妇，相见依然，如有曩旧，云：己死得生，舅即以某日而亡，说所闻见，与安居悉同。受五戒师字僧昊，襄阳人也，末居长沙，本与安居同里，闻其口说。安居之终，亦亲睹，果九十三焉。珠林六十二

    Explanation

    91

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    Example 3

    Source: 凡為文章，猶乘騏驥，雖有逸氣，當以銜勒制之，勿使流亂軌躅，放意填坑岸也。

    Translation: In all writing, it is like riding a swift steed — though it may possess a wild and unrestrained spirit, one must control it with bit and bridle, and must not let it run wild, straying from the proper path or indulging in aimless wanderings.

    Example 4

    Source: 自古明王聖帝，猶須勤學，況凡庶乎！此事遍於經史，吾亦不能鄭重，聊舉近世切要，以啟寤汝耳。

    Translation: From ancient times, wise kings and sage emperors still required diligent study; how much more so, then, for common people! This matter is found throughout the classics and histories. I cannot elaborate further, but I will briefly mention a few essential points of recent times in order to enlighten you.

    Example 5

    Source: 夫文章者，原出五經：詔命策檄，生於書者也；序述論議，生於易者也；歌詠賦頌，生於詩者也；祭祀哀誄，生於禮者也；書奏箴銘，生於春秋者也。朝廷憲章，軍旅誓誥，敷顯仁義，發明功德，牧民建國，不可暫無。至於陶冶性靈，從容諷諫，入其滋味，亦樂事也。行有餘力，則可習之。

    Translation: As for writings, their origin lies in the Five Classics: edicts, memorials, and military proclamations arise from the Shujing (Book of Documents); expository and argumentative writings arise from the Yijing (Book of Changes); songs, odes, and praises arise from the Shijing (Book of Poetry); ritual sacrifices, mourning, and elegies arise from the Liji (Book of Rites); memorials, admonitions, and inscriptions arise from the Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn Annals). Court regulations, military oaths and decrees, the proclamation of benevolence and righteousness, the elucidation of virtue and merit, governing the people and establishing the state—all are indispensable. As for cultivating the mind and spirit, offering gentle admonition in a relaxed manner, and savoring the flavor of such writings, these too are pleasant pursuits. When one has spare energy, then one may study them.

    Source text:
    ”乃以三人送安居出门，数步，有专使送符与安居，谓曰：“君可持此符，经过戍逻以示之，勿辄偷过，偷过有徒?也。若有水碍，可以此符投水中，即得过也。”安居受符而归行久之，阻大江，不得渡，安居依言投符，蒙然如眩，乃是其家屋前中方地也。正闻家中号恸哭泣，所送之人，劝还就身，安居云：“身已臭秽吾不复能归。”此人乃强排之，踣于尸脚上。安居既愈，欲验黄水妇人，故往冠军县寻问；果有此妇，相见依然，如有曩旧，云：己死得生，舅即以某日而亡，说所闻见，与安居悉同。受五戒师字僧昊，襄阳人也，末居长沙，本与安居同里，闻其口说。安居之终，亦亲睹，果九十三焉。珠林六十二

    92

    宋沙门僧规者，武当寺僧也，时京兆张瑜于此县，常请僧规在家供养。永初元年十二月五日，无痾忽暴死，二日而稣愈。自说云：五日夜五更中，闻门巷闲哓哓有声，须臾，见有五人，炳炬火，执信旛，迳来入屋，叱咀僧规因顿卧恍然，五人便以赤绳缚将去。行至一山，都无草木，土色坚黑，有类石铁；山侧左右，白骨填积，山数十里，至三岐路有一人，甚长壮，被铠执仗，问五人：“有几人来？”答曰：“政一人耳！”五人又将规入一道中，俄至一城外，有屋数十，筑壤为之，屋前有立木，长十余丈，上有铁梁，形如桔槔，左右有匮，贮土，土有品数，或有十斛形，亦如五升大者。

    Explanation

    92

    During the Southern Song Dynasty, there was a monk named Senggui from Wudang Temple. At that time, Zhang Yu from Jingzhao often invited Senggui to his home for support. In the first year of Yongchou, on the fifth day of the twelfth month, Senggui died suddenly without any illness, but he revived after two days. He recounted what happened: On the fifth night of the fifth watch, he heard a clamor in the street. Soon after, he saw five people carrying torches and holding banners, coming straight into the house. They shouted at Senggui, causing him to fall into a trance-like state, and the five people then bound him with a red rope and took him away. They led him to a mountain with no grass or trees, the soil was hard and black, like stone or iron. On both sides of the mountain, there were piles of white bones, stretching for dozens of miles. They reached a three-way fork where there was a very tall and strong man, wearing armor and holding weapons. He asked the five people, "How many of you have come?" They replied, "Only one person!" The five then took Senggui into one of the paths, and soon they arrived at the outskirts of a city. There were dozens of houses, built from earth, with a standing tree in front of the house, over ten zhang tall. On top of the tree was an iron beam shaped like a seesaw, with bins on either side, storing earth. The earth had different sizes, some as large as ten dou, others as small as five dou.

    93

    有一人，衣帻并赤，语规曰：“汝生世时，有何罪福？依实说之，勿妄言也。”规惶怖未答，赤衣人如局吏云：“可开簿检其罪福也。”有顷，吏至长木下，提一匮土，县铁梁上称之，如觉低昂，吏谓规曰：“此种量罪福之秤也。汝福少罪多，应先受罚。”俄有一人，衣冠长者，谓规曰：“汝沙门也，何不念佛？我闻悔过可度八难。
    ”规于是一心称佛，衣冠人谓吏曰：“可更为此人称之，既是佛弟子，幸可度脱。”吏乃复上匮称之，称乃正平。既而将规至监官前辩之，监执笔观簿，迟疑久之；又有一人，朱衣玄冠，佩印绶，执玉板，来，曰：“算簿上未有此人名也。”监官愕然，命左右收录去，须臾，见反缚向五人来，监官曰：“杀鬼，何以滥将人来？乃鞭之。少顷有使者称：“天帝唤道人来。”既至帝宫，经见践历略，皆金宝精光，晃昱不得凝视。

    Explanation

    93

    A man appeared, dressed entirely in red, and spoke to the monk Guī: "When you were born, what merits and faults did you have? Speak the truth, do not speak falsely." Guī was in great fear and unable to answer. The red-clothed person, acting like an official, said, "Can we open the ledger to check their merits and faults?" After a while, an official arrived at the long wooden stand, lifted a small chest of earth, and hung it on an iron beam to weigh it. As if sensing the imbalance, the official told Guī, "This is the scale for measuring merits and faults. Your merits are few and your faults many; you should be punished first." Soon, a man dressed in formal attire approached and said to Guī, "You are a monk, why don't you recite Buddha's name? I have heard that repentance can help cross the eight difficulties."

    Guī then sincerely recited Buddha's name. The formally dressed man told the official, "Can you weigh this person again? Since he is a disciple of Buddha, it is fortunate that he can be saved." The official then reweighed the chest, and the scale became perfectly balanced. They then took Guī to the supervisor's presence to debate the matter. The supervisor held a brush and looked at the ledger, hesitating for a long time. Another man, dressed in red with a black hat, wearing seals and holding a jade tablet, came and said, "There is no name of this person on the ledger." The supervisor was startled and ordered his attendants to take Guī away. Soon, five men appeared with their hands tied behind their backs. The supervisor said, "Kill the ghosts, why did you bring people indiscriminately? They were whipped." Shortly after, a messenger announced, "The Heavenly Emperor calls the Daoist priest." Upon arriving at the Heavenly Emperor's palace, Guī saw the journey and experiences, all adorned with golden treasures and brilliant light, dazzling to the point of not being able to look directly.

    94

    帝左右朱衣宝冠，饰以华珍，帝曰：“汝是沙门，何不勤业而为小鬼，横收捕也？”规稽首诸佛，祈恩请福，帝曰：“汝命未尽，今当还生；宜勤精进，勿屡游白衣家！杀鬼取人，亦多枉滥，如汝比也。”规曰：“横滥之厄，当以何方而济免之？”帝曰：“广设福业，最为善也；若不办，尔可作八关斋；生免横祸，死离地狱，亦其次也。”语毕，遣规去。行还未久，见一精舍，大有沙门，见武当寺主白法师，弟子慧进，皆在焉，居宇宏整，资待自然，规请欲居之，有一沙门曰：“此是福地，非君所得处也。”使者将规还至瑜家而去。珠林八十三

    Explanation

    94

    The emperor, adorned with red robes and a jeweled crown, surrounded by precious treasures, said to the monk, "You are a monk, why are you not diligently practicing your monastic duties but instead being captured as a demon?" The monk bowed to the Buddhas, praying for blessings. The emperor then said, "Your life is not yet over, and you will be reborn. You should diligently strive and not frequently visit the homes of laypeople! Killing demons and taking people is often unjust and excessive, like you." The monk asked, "What can I do to avoid such misfortune?" The emperor replied, "Widely establishing good deeds is the best; if you cannot, you can observe the eight-precept observance. This will help you avoid misfortune in life and be reborn in heaven after death, which is also good." After speaking, the emperor sent the monk away. Shortly after, the monk saw a monastery with many monks, including Master Bai, the head of the Wudang Temple, and his disciple Huixin. The monastery was grand and orderly, and the monk requested to stay there. One of the monks said, "This is a blessed place, not suitable for you to stay." The messenger then took the monk back to the house of Yu.

    何澹之，东海人，宋大司农，不信经法，多行残害。永初中，得病，见一鬼，形甚长壮，牛头人身，手执铁?，昼夜守之。忧布屏营，使道家作章符印录，备诸禳绝，而犹见如故。相识沙门慧义，闻其病往○；澹之为说所见，慧义曰：“此是牛头阿旁也，”罪福不昧，唯人所招；君能转心向法，则此鬼自消。”澹之迷很不革，顷之遂死。珠林八十三
    　　宋沙门竺慧炽，新野人，住在江陵四层寺，永初二年，卒，弟子为设七日会。其日将夕烧香竟，道贤沙门因往视炽弟子，至房前，忽暧暧若人形，详视，乃慧炽也，容貌衣服，不异生时。谓贤：“君旦食肉，美不？”贤曰：“美。”炽曰：“我坐食肉，今生饿狗地狱道。”贤惧詟未及得答，炽复言：“汝若不信，试看我背后。”乃回背示贤，见三黄狗，形半似驴，眼甚赤，光照户内，状欲啮炽而复止。贤骇怖闷绝，良久乃稣。具说其事。珠林九十四

    Explanation

    95

    He Danzhi, a man from Donghai, served as the Grand Agricultural Minister during the Song dynasty. He did not believe in religious teachings and often engaged in cruel and harmful acts. During the Yongchun era, he fell ill and saw a ghost. The ghost had a very tall and strong form, with a bull's head and a human body, holding an iron tool, and guarded him day and night. Feeling distressed and restless, he had Taoists create talismans and inscriptions to ward off evil, but still saw the ghost as before. A monk named Huiyi, whom he knew, heard of his illness and visited him. Danzhi told him about what he had seen. Huiyi said, "This is the 'Niu Tou A Pang' ghost." He explained that retribution for sins and blessings is not obscured, and it is only what one has brought upon oneself. "If you can change your heart and turn to the law (or religion), then this ghost will naturally disappear." Danzhi remained stubborn and unrepentant, and soon after, he died. This story is recorded in the "Zhu Lin" (Jewel Forest), entry 83.

    Monk Zhuhui Chi, a native of Xinye, lived in the Four-Tiered Temple in Jiangling. In the second year of the Yongchun era, he died. His disciples set up a seven-day memorial service. On that day, as evening approached and after burning incense, a monk named Daoxian went to visit Zhuhui Chi's disciples. Arriving at the front of the room, he suddenly saw a figure that appeared human. Looking closely, it was Zhuhui Chi. His appearance and clothing were no different from when he was alive. He said to Daoxian, "Did you enjoy the meat you ate this morning?" Daoxian replied, "Yes, it was enjoyable." Zhuhui Chi said, "I am suffering in the hell of hungry dogs because I ate meat." Daoxian was terrified and did not get a chance to answer. Zhuhui Chi spoke again, "If you don't believe me, look at my back." He turned his back to show Daoxian, who saw three yellow dogs, half the shape of donkeys, with very red eyes that illuminated the room. They seemed about to bite Zhuhui Chi but then stopped. Daoxian was terrified and fainted. After a long time, he regained consciousness and told the whole story. This account is recorded in the "Zhu Lin" (Jewel Forest), entry 94.

    96

    晋王练，字玄明，琅琊人也，宋侍中。父玟，字季琰，晋中书令；相识有一梵沙门，每瞻玟风釆，甚敬悦之辄语同学云：“若我后生得为此人作子，于近愿亦足矣。玟闻而戏之曰：“法师才行，正可为弟子子耳！”顷之，沙门病亡，亡后岁余，而练生焉。始能言，便解外国语及绝国之奇珍锒器珠贝；生所不见，未闻其名，即而名之，识其产出，又自然亲爱诸梵过于汉人。咸谓沙门审其先身，故玟字之曰阿练，遂为大名云云。珠林二十六　广记三百八十七　辩正论八陈子良注引冥祥记云琅琊王玟其妻无子常祈观音乞儿玟后行路逢一胡僧其意极甚悦之其胡僧曰我死当为君子少时道人果亡三月间玟妻有妊及生能语即解西域十六国音大聪明有器度即晋尚书王渊明身也故小名阿练前生时事有验

    Explanation

    96

    Jin Wang Lian, courtesy name Xuanming, was from Langya and served as a Shizhong in the Song dynasty. His father, Wen, courtesy name Jiyan, was a Zhongshu Ling in the Jin dynasty. Wen had an acquaintance, a Vajra monk, who greatly admired Wen's bearing and often told his fellow monks, "If I were to be reborn as a son of this person, it would be enough for my near wishes." Wen, upon hearing this, playfully responded, "The monk's virtue and talent, just suitable to be a disciple's child!" Soon after, the monk fell ill and passed away. A year or so after his death, Jin Wang Lian was born. From the moment he could speak, he could understand foreign languages and recognize exotic treasures, rare vessels, and precious jewels. He could name things he had never seen and knew their place of origin. He naturally loved all the monks more than Han people. Everyone believed that the monk knew his previous life, so Wen named him Alian, and thus it became a great name. Zhu Lin 26, Guang Ji 387, Bian Zheng Lun 8 Chen Ziliang annotation, citing the Míng Xiáng Jì (Record of Auspicious Signs): Wang Wen of Langya had no children and often prayed to Guanyin for a child. One day, while traveling, he met a Hu Seng, whom he greatly admired. The Hu Seng said, "After my death, I will be reborn as your son." Soon after, the monk died, and three months later, Wang Wen's wife became pregnant. When the child was born, he could speak and understood the languages of the sixteen kingdoms of the Western Regions. He was very intelligent and had a dignified bearing, which was later identified as that of Wang Yuanning, a Shangshu in the Jin dynasty. Therefore, he was given the nickname Alian, and the events of his previous life were verified.

    97

    宋珠林引作晋今依广记孙道德，益州人也，奉道祭酒，年过五十，未有子息。居近精舍，景平中，沙门谓德：“必愿有儿，当至心礼诵观世音经，此可冀也。”德遂罢不事道，单心投诚，归观世音；少日之中而有梦应，妇即有孕，遂以产男也。法苑珠林十七太平广记一百十
    　　宋齐僧钦者，江陵人也，家门奉法，年十许岁时，善相占云：“年不过三六。”父母兄弟甚为忧惧，僧钦亦增加勤敬斋戒精苦。至年十七，宋景平末，得病危笃，家斋祈弥励，亦淫祀求福，疾终不愈。时有一女巫云：“此郎福力猛盛，魔魍所不能亲，自有善神护之；然病久不差，运命或将有限。世有探命之术，少事天神，颇晓其数，当为君试效之。”于野中设酒脯之馈，烧钱经七日七夕，云：始有感见，见诸善神方为此郎祈祷，蒙益两算矣，病必得愈，无所忧也。僧钦于是遂差，弥加精至，其后二十四年而终，如巫所言，则一算十二年矣。珠林六十二

    Explanation

    97

    In the Zhu Lin of the Song dynasty, which cites the Jin (Treatise) and follows the Guang Ji (Broad Records), there is a story about Sun Daode, a man from Yizhou who served as a Taoist priest. He was over fifty years old and had no children. Living near a monastery, during the reign of Emperor Wen of Liu Song (424-427 AD), a Buddhist monk told him, "If you truly wish to have a son, you should devote yourself wholeheartedly to the worship and recitation of the Sutra of the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara. This is something you can hope for." Sun Daode then ceased his Taoist practices and devoted his heart in sincere faith to Avalokiteshvara. In a short period of time, he had a dream response, and his wife became pregnant, eventually giving birth to a son. This story is recorded in Fa Yuan Zhu Lin (Treasury of the Dharma Jewel) and Tai Ping Guang Ji (Broad Records of the Great Peace).

    Another story in Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest) concerns a monk named Qing from the Song and Qi dynasties, who was from Jiangling. His family adhered to the law, and when he was around ten years old, a fortune-teller predicted, "Your lifespan will not exceed thirty-six years." His parents, brothers, and he himself were greatly alarmed. Qing increased his diligence in reverence, fasting, and strict discipline. At the age of seventeen, towards the end of the reign of Emperor Wen of Liu Song, he fell gravely ill. His family intensified their prayers and offerings, and even engaged in superstitious practices to seek blessings, but his illness did not improve. At this time, a female witch said, "This young man has powerful good fortune and virtue, which even demons and evil spirits cannot approach; he has the protection of good spirits. However, his illness has lasted a long time, and his fate or destiny may be limited. There is a method to divining one's fate. I have served the heavenly deities and understand this technique. I will try it for you." She set up an offering of wine and meat in the wild, burned money, and performed rituals over seven days and seven nights during the seventh day of the seventh month. She said, "I have now seen a response. I saw various good spirits praying for this young man, and he has been granted two additional years of life. His illness will certainly be cured, so there is nothing to worry about." Qing then recovered, and his devotion became even more meticulous. He lived for twenty-four more years after this, as the witch had predicted, with each calculation representing twelve years. This story is recorded in Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest).

    98

    宋魏世子者，梁郡人也，奉法精进，儿子遵修，唯妇迷闭，不信释教。元嘉初，女年十四病死，七日而苏。云可安施高座，并无量寿经。世子即为具设经座，女先虽斋戒礼拜，而未尝看经，今广记引有今字即升座转读，声句清利，下启父言：“儿死便往无量寿国，见父兄及己三人，池中已有芙蓉大华，后当化生其中；唯母独无，不胜此苦，乃心，故归启报。”语绝，复绝，母于是乃敬信法教。信字教字据广记引补　珠林十五太平广记一百十四

    Explanation

    98

    The Crown Prince of Wei, a native of Liang Commandery, diligently followed the law, and his sons also adhered to it. However, his wife was confused and closed-minded, and she did not believe in the Buddhist teachings. In the early years of the Yüanjia era, their daughter, who was fourteen years old, died of illness. Seven days later, she revived and said that a high seat and the Infinite Life Sutra could be placed there. The Crown Prince immediately arranged for the sutra and the seat. Although the daughter had previously fasted, abstained, and prostrated, she had never read the sutra before. Now, with the addition of the characters "广记引" (from the Zhu Lin and Taiping Guangji), she ascended the seat and recited the sutra fluently. She then spoke to her father, saying, "When I died, I went to the Land of Infinite Life and saw my father, elder brother, and myself. There were already large lotus flowers in the pond, and I will be reborn there later. However, my mother was not there, and I could not bear this suffering. I was determined, so I returned to report." Her words ended, and she died again. Her mother then began to respect and believe in the teachings.

    99

    宋张兴者，新兴人也，颇信佛法，尝从沙门僧融昙翼时受八戒。兴常为劫所引，夫得走逃，妻坐系狱，掠笞积日。时县失火，出囚路侧，会融翼同行，经过囚边；妻惊呼：“阇梨何以赐救？”融曰：“贫道力弱，无救如何？唯宜勤念观世音，庶获免耳。”妻便昼夜祈念，经十许日于夜，梦一沙门，以脚蹈之广记引作以足蹑之曰：“咄咄可起！”妻即惊起，钳锁桎梏，忽然俱解。便走趣户，户时犹闭，警防殊严；既无由出，虑有觉者，乃复着械广记引作乃却自械寻复得眠，又梦向沙门曰：“户已开矣！”妻觉而驰出，守备者并已惛睡，妻安步而去。时夜甚闇，行可数里，卒值一人；妻惧躄地，已而相讯，乃其夫也。相扶悲喜，夜投僧翼，翼藏匿之，遂得免。时元嘉初也。珠林十七广记一百十

    Explanation

    99

    Cao Xing of the Song dynasty was a native of Xingning and had a strong belief in Buddhism. He once followed the monk Seng Rong (Tanyi) and received the Eight Precepts at that time. Cao Xing was often led by robbers, and his husband managed to escape, but his wife was imprisoned and beaten for several days. At one point, the county experienced a fire, and the prisoners were released to the side of the road. Coincidentally, Seng Rong happened to be walking with them and passed by the prisoners. The wife shouted in surprise, "Reverend, how can you save me?" Seng Rong replied, "I am weak in spirit and cannot help you. You should diligently recite the name of Guanyin, perhaps you may be spared." The wife then began to recite the name of Guanyin day and night. After about ten days, she had a dream in which a monk stepped on her feet and said, "Hurry up and get up!" The wife woke up in shock, and suddenly all her shackles and fetters were undone. She ran towards the door, but it was still closed, and the guards were very strict. There was no way to escape, and she worried that someone might wake up. So, she put the shackles back on and soon fell asleep again. In another dream, the same monk told her, "The door is open now!" The wife woke up and ran out, finding the guards all asleep. She walked calmly away. It was very dark at night, and she walked for several miles before suddenly encountering someone. The wife was afraid and fell to the ground, but when she looked up, it was her husband. They supported each other in joy and sorrow, and at night, they went to Seng Rong. Seng Rong hid them, and they thus escaped. This was at the beginning of the Yuanjia era. The story is recorded in Volume 17 of the "Book of Jewels" and Volume 110 of the "Comprehensive Records."

    100

    宋元嘉初，中有黄龙沙弥昙无竭者，诵观世音经，净修苦行。与诸徒属五十二人往寻佛国，备经荒险，贞志弥坚。既达天竺舍卫，路逢山象一群，竭赍经诵念，称名归命，有师子从林中出，象惊奔走。后有野牛一群，鸣吼而来，将欲加害，竭又如初归命，有大鹫飞来，牛便惊散。遂得克免。法苑珠林七十五

    Explanation

    100

    In the early years of the Yuanjia period of the Song dynasty, there was a novice monk named Tan Wujie, known as Huanglong, who chanted the Guanshiyin Sutra and engaged in pure cultivation and austere practices. Together with his disciples, fifty-two in number, he went to seek the land of the Buddha. They endured all kinds of dangers and hardships, yet his resolve became even stronger. After arriving at Shāwèi in Tianzhu (India), he encountered a group of wild elephants on the road. Monk Tan Wujie offered the sutra, chanted the name, and devoted himself to the Buddha. A lion emerged from the forest, and the elephants were frightened and fled. Later, a herd of wild cattle, roaring, came to attack. Monk Tan Wujie again recited the name and dedicated himself to the Buddha as before. A large vulture flew over, and the cattle were frightened and scattered. Thus, he was able to escape unharmed. (Chapter 75 of the Fa Yuan Zhu Lin)

    101

    宋唐文伯，东海戆榆人也，弟好蒲博，家资都尽；屯中有寺，经过人或以钱上佛，弟屡窃取。久后病癞，卜者云：“祟由盗佛钱。”父怒曰：“佛是何神，乃令我儿致此？吾当试更虏夺，若复能病，可也。”前县令何欣之妇上织成宝盖带四枚，乃盗取之，以为腰带。不盈百日，复得恶病，发疮之始，起腰带处。世时在元嘉年初尔。珠林七十九广记一百十六
    　　宋沙门释道冏，扶风好畤人也，本姓马氏，学业淳粹，弱龄有声。元嘉二年九月，在洛阳为人作普贤斋，道俗四十许人，已经七日，正就中食，忽有一人，裤褶乘马，入至堂前，下马礼佛；冏谓常人，不加礼异，此人登马挥鞭，忽失所在，便见赤光，赫然竟天，良久而灭。后三年十二月，在白衣家复作普贤斋，将竟之日，有二沙门，容服如凡，直来礼佛；泉中谓是庸僧，不甚尊仰，聊问何居？答曰：“住在前屯。

    Explanation

    101

    During the Tang dynasty, there was a man named Wen Bo from the region of Dangyu in the East Sea. His younger brother enjoyed gambling and eventually squandered all their family wealth. There was a temple within a military camp, and sometimes people passing by would offer money to the Buddha. The brother frequently stole these offerings. After a long time, he fell ill with leprosy. A diviner said, "The illness is caused by stealing the offerings to the Buddha." The father became angry and said, "What kind of god is the Buddha, causing my son to fall ill? I will try to steal the offerings myself. If I too fall ill, then the diviner's words are true." He stole four brocade belts that the wife of a former county magistrate named He Xin had offered as a canopy and used them as a belt. Within less than a hundred days, the father also fell ill, and the illness began at the place where the belt was worn. This event took place during the early years of the reign of Emperor Yuan of Liu Song. It is recorded in the Zhu Lin (Pearl Forest) and Guang Ji (Comprehensive Records).

    In the Liu Song dynasty, there was a Buddhist monk named Dao Jiong from the county of Haozhi in the region of Fufeng. Originally, he had the surname Ma and had pure and refined learning, being well-known for his scholarly achievements at a young age. In the ninth month of the second year of the reign of Emperor Yuan, he was in Luoyang, the capital city, conducting a ritual dedicated to the Bodhisattva Samantabhadra for someone. About forty people, including both monks and laypeople, had already been participating in the ritual for seven days. On the day of the midday meal, a person suddenly appeared, wearing trousers and a jacket and riding a horse, entering the hall and dismounting to pay respects to the Buddha. Dao Jiong considered the person to be an ordinary person and did not give him special attention. The person then mounted his horse, waved his whip, and suddenly disappeared. A bright red light spread across the sky, lasting for a long time before fading away. Three years later, in the twelfth month, Dao Jiong was again in a layperson's home, conducting a ritual dedicated to the Bodhisattva Samantabhadra. On the day the ritual was about to end, two monks appeared, dressed in ordinary clothing, and came directly to pay respects to the Buddha. Dao Jiong thought they were common monks and did not show much respect. He casually asked where they lived, and they replied, "We live in a previous garrison."

    ”时众白衣有张道，觉其有异，至心礼拜，沙门出门，行可数十步，忽有飞尘，直上冲天，追目此僧，不复知所。冏以七年与同学来游京师，时司空何尚之始构南涧精舍，冏寓居焉。夜中忽见四人乘一新车，从四人，传教来在屋内，呼与共载道，冏惊其夜至，疑而未言，因眼闭，不觉升车。俄而至郡后沈桥，见一贵人，着?被笺布单衣，坐床焘伞，形似华盖，卤簿从卫可数百人，悉服黄衣，见冏惊曰：“行般舟道人，精心远诣，○欲知其处耳！何故将来？”即遣人引送冏还。至精舍门外，失所送人，门闭如故，扣唤久之，寺内诸僧咸惊相报告，开门内之。视所住房户，犹故关之。珠林十七

    102

    At that time, among the common people, there was a man named Zhang Dao. He felt that the monk was unusual and worshiped him with utmost sincerity. The monk went out and walked about ten steps. Suddenly, flying dust shot straight up to the sky. Looking back at the monk, one could no longer see where he had gone. Jiong came to the capital with his fellow students after seven years. At that time, the Grand Works Commissioner He Shangzhi had just begun to construct the Nanjian Monastery, and Jiong stayed there. At night, he suddenly saw four people in a new carriage, accompanied by four attendants. They came into the house and called Jiong to ride with them. Jiong was surprised that they came at night and hesitated to speak. He closed his eyes and did not feel himself being lifted onto the carriage. Soon, they arrived at the Sheng Bridge behind the county. There, he saw a noble person wearing a robe made of fine cloth, sitting on a bed with an umbrella-like canopy, its shape resembling a canopy. There were hundreds of attendants and guards, all wearing yellow clothes. Seeing Jiong, the noble person was surprised and said, "The traveler on the Ban Zhou path, with sincere heart and far-reaching aspirations, wants to know the place. Why bring him here?" He immediately sent people to escort Jiong back. When they reached the monastery gate, the people who had escorted him were gone, and the gate was still closed. After knocking and calling for a long time, the monks inside the monastery were all startled and reported it. They opened the door and let him in. Looking at the room where he had stayed, it was still locked. Zhu Lin, Volume 17.

    宋李旦，字世则，广陵人也，以孝谨质素着称乡里。元嘉三年，正月十四日，暴病，心下不冷，七日而苏，含以饮粥，○○○○。○有一人，持信旛来至床头，称府君教唤，旦便随去。直北向行，道甚平净。既至，城阁高丽，似今宫阙，遣传教慰劳，问呼：“旦可前”至大厅事上，见有三十人，单衣青帻，列坐森然，一人东坐，披袍隐凡，左右侍卫，可有百余，视旦而语坐人云：“当示以诸狱，令世知也。

    103

    Lǐ Dàn, courtesy name Shìzé, was a man from Guangling, renowned in his village for his filial piety, diligence, and simplicity. In the third year of the Yuán Jiā era, on the fourteenth day of the first month, he suddenly fell ill, but his heart remained warm, and he revived after seven days, being fed porridge. One day, a person carrying a banner of faith came to his bedside, saying that the lord of the prefecture had called for him. Lǐ Dàn immediately followed the messenger. They traveled directly north, the road being very flat and clean. Upon arrival, they saw city gates and towers that were tall and beautiful, resembling the palaces of today. A messenger was sent to comfort and console him, and he was called to come forward to the main hall. There, he saw thirty people, all wearing plain clothes and blue headbands, sitting in an orderly and solemn manner. One person sat on the east side, wearing a robe and hiding in the mundane, with about a hundred attendants on either side. The person looked at Lǐ Dàn and spoke to the seated people, saying, "We will show you the various prisons, to make the world know."

    ”旦闻言已，举头四视，都失向处，乃是地狱中。见群罪人，受诸苦报，呻吟号呼，不可忍视。寻有传教，称：“府君信君，可还去，当更相迎。”因此而还。至六年正月复死，七日又活，述所见事，较略如先。或有罪因寄语报家，道生时犯罪，使为作福，称说姓字，亲识乡伍，旦依言寻求皆得之。又云：“甲申年当行疾疠，杀诸恶人，佛家弟子，作八关斋，心修善行，可得免也。”旦本作道家祭酒，即欲弃箓本法道民谏制故遂两事，而常劝化，作八关斋。法苑珠林六

    104

    Dawn heard the words and raised his head to look all around, completely losing the previous place, realizing he was in the underworld. He saw a crowd of sinners suffering various punishments, groaning and shouting, a sight that was unbearable to look at. Soon, a messenger appeared and said, "The Lord of the Mansion believes in you; you can return and go, and we will come to greet you again." Therefore, he returned. In the sixth year of January, he died again, but seven days later, he came back to life. He described what he saw, which was similar in detail to before. Some of the sins were reported by a messenger to the family, saying that when he was born, he committed a sin and was ordered to perform good deeds. The messenger called out names and surnames, and familiar faces and fellow villagers were found by Dawn following the words. He also said, "In the year Jia Shen, a plague will spread, killing all evil people. Buddhist disciples, by performing the Eight Precepts and practicing good deeds with the heart, can be exempted." Dawn originally practiced Daoism as a priest, but he wanted to abandon the Daoist scriptures due to the advice and control of Daoist followers, so he engaged in both practices and often preached, performing the Eight Precepts.     宋尚书仆射荥阳郑鲜之，元嘉四年，从大驾巡京至都，夕暴亡，乃灵语着人曰：“吾寿命久尽，早应过世，赖比岁来敬信佛法，放生布施，以此功德，延驰数年耳。夫幽显报应，有若影响，宜放落俗务，崇心大教。”于时胜贵多皆闻云。珠林六
    　　宋周宗者，广陵肥如人也，元嘉七年，随刘彦之北伐，王师失利，与同邑六人逃窜。闲行于彭城北，遇一空寺，无有僧徒，中有形像，以水精为相，因共窃取，出屯贸食。其一人羸病，等辈轻之，独不得分。既各还家，三四年中，宗等五人，相继病癞而死，不得分者，独获全免。珠林七十九广记一百十六

    Explanation

    105

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of the Liu Song dynasty, Zheng Xianzhi, a high-ranking official and servant to the emperor, traveled with the imperial procession to the capital city in the fourth year of the Yuanjia era. In the evening, he died suddenly. His spirit then spoke to someone, saying, "My life span has long ended, and I should have passed away long ago. However, due to the recent years of respecting and believing in Buddhism, releasing animals, and making charitable donations, by this merit, my life was extended by several years. Retribution in the visible and invisible worlds is as if it were an echo or shadow. One should abandon worldly affairs and uphold the great teaching." At that time, many noble and wealthy people heard of this. (Zhu Lin, Volume 6)

    Zhou Zong, a person from Feiru, Guangling, followed General Liu Yan to the northern campaign in the seventh year of the Yuanjia era. The imperial army suffered defeat, and Zhou Zong fled with six fellow townspeople. Wandering north of Pengcheng, they encountered an empty temple with no monks or disciples. Inside the temple, there were statues made of crystal. They collectively stole the statues and sold them at the military camp. One of them was weak and ill, and the others looked down on him, so he did not get a share. After each returned home, within three to four years, Zhou Zong and four others died one after another from leprosy, while the one who did not get a share remained unharmed. (Zhu Lin, Volume 79; Guangji, Volume 116)

    宋案当作晋广记引无顺阳郭诠，字仲衡，晋益州刺史，义熙初，以党附桓玄被诛。二句依广记引补亡后三十余载，元嘉八年，忽见形诣女婿南阳刘凝之家，车卫甚盛。谓凝之曰：“仆有谪事，可见为作四十僧会，当得免也。”言终不见。刘谓是魍魉，不以在意。复夕，诠又与女梦言：“吾有谪罚，已告汝婿，令为设会；何以至今四字广记引有不能见矜耶？”女晨起，见诠从户过，怒言：“竟不能相救？今便就罪。”女号踊留之，问当何处设斋？答云：“可归吾舍。”倏然复没。凝之即狼狈供办，会毕，有人称诠信与凝之相闻，言：“感君厚惠，事始获宥。”言已失去，于是而绝。珠林九十一广记三百二十四

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Shao of Liu Song, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    107

    宋司马文宣，河内人也，颇信佛法。元嘉九年，丁母难，弟丧，月望，旦忽见其弟身形于灵座上，不异平日，回遑叹嗟，讽求饮食。文乃试与言曰：“汝平生时修行十善，若如经言，应得生天，若在人道，何故乃生此鬼中耶？”沈吟俯仰，默然无对。文即夕梦见其弟云：“生所修善，蒙报生天；旦灵床之鬼，是魔魅耳，非其身也；恐兄疑怪，故诣以白兄。”文宣明旦请僧转首楞严经，令人扑系之，鬼乃逃入床下，又走户外，形稍丑恶。举家骇惧，叱詈遣之，鬼云：“饿乞食耳！”积日乃去。顷之，母灵床头有一鬼肤体赤色，身甚长壮，文宣长息孝祖与言，往反答对周悉；初虽恐惧，末稍安习之，鬼亦转相附狎，居处出入，殆同家人。于时京师传相报告，往来观者门巷叠迹，时南林寺有僧与灵味寺僧含沙门与鬼言论，亦甚款曲。

    107

    Wang Wenxuan, a person from the Song dynasty, was from Hebei and believed in Buddhism quite a lot. In the ninth year of the reign of Emperor Wu of Liu Song, his mother passed away, and his brother died. On the night of the full moon, in the morning, he suddenly saw his brother's body on the altar, which was no different from usual. He was lost and sighed, asking for food and drink. Wang Wenxuan then tried to speak to the ghost, saying, "If you did good deeds in life, according to the scriptures, you should have been reborn in heaven. If you were reborn in the human world, why did you become a ghost?" The ghost hesitated and looked around, remaining silent without answering. That night, Wang Wenxuan dreamed of his brother, who said, "The good deeds done in life have been rewarded with rebirth in heaven. The ghost on the altar in the morning is just a demon, not my body. I am afraid that you will doubt and be surprised, so I came to tell you." The next day, Wang Wenxuan invited a monk to recite the Shou Leng Yan Jing (Sutra of the Buddha's Protection) and had someone tie the ghost up. The ghost then fled under the bed and out the door, and its appearance became slightly ugly and evil. The whole family was terrified and scolded and drove it away. The ghost said, "I'm hungry and asking for food!" After several days, it left. Soon, there was a red-skinned, tall, and strong ghost at the mother's altar. Wang Wenxuan's eldest son, Xiao Zu, spoke with it, and they conversed back and forth thoroughly. At first, they were afraid, but later they became accustomed to it. The ghost also began to attach itself and become familiar, living and moving around as if it were part of the family. At that time, the capital city spread the news, and people came and went, and the streets were crowded. At the time, there were monks from Nanlin Temple and Lingwei Temple who spoke with the ghost, and they also spoke very kindly and politely.

    108

    鬼云：“昔世尝为尊贵，以犯众恶，受报未竟，果此鬼身。去寅年有四百部鬼，大行疾疠，所应钟灾者，不○道人耳；而犯横极众，多滥福善，故使我来监察之也。”僧以食与之，鬼曰：“我自有粮，不得进此食也。”含曰：“鬼多知我生何来，何因作道人？”答曰：“人中来出家，因缘本誓愿也。”问诸存亡生死所趣，略皆答对。具有灵验；条次繁多，故不曲载。含曰：“人鬼道殊，汝既不求食，何为久留？”鬼曰：“此间有一女子，应在收捕，而奉戒精勤，故难可得，比日稽留，用此故也。藉乱主人，有愧不少。”自此已后，不甚见形，后往视者，但闻语耳。时元嘉十年也。至三月二十八日，语文宣云：“暂来寄住，而汝倾家营福，见畏如此，那得久留。”孝祖云：“听汝寄住，何故据人先亡灵筵耶？”答曰：“汝家亡者，各有所属；此座空设，故权寄耳。”于是辞去。珠林六

    Explanation

    108

    The ghost said: "In a past life, I was once noble and dignified, but I committed many evil deeds, and the retribution has not been completed, resulting in this ghostly form. In the year of the Tiger, there were four hundred ghosts who spread great epidemics, causing disasters for those who deserved them, not the wicked or those who do not follow the path; I committed many violent acts, often bestowed excessive blessings, thus I came to oversee this." The monk offered food to the ghost, who said, "I have my own food and cannot accept this." The monk asked, "Do ghosts know where I came from and why I became a monk?" The ghost replied, "I came from among humans to become a monk, due to the karmic connection and original vow." The monk asked about the fate of the living and the dead, and the ghost answered in a general way. There were many miraculous occurrences; the details were numerous and detailed, thus not recorded in full. The monk said, "Humans and ghosts have different paths; since you do not seek food, why stay for a long time?" The ghost said, "There is a woman here who should be captured, but she follows the precepts diligently, thus difficult to capture. Recently, I have been delayed due to this reason. Causing trouble for the host, I feel considerable shame." From this point onward, the ghost was not often seen, and those who came to visit later only heard words. It was the tenth year of the Yuanjia era. On March 28th, the ghost said, "I am temporarily staying, and you have spent your entire family's resources to create merit, are so fearful, how can I stay for a long time?" The monk said, "Allow you to stay temporarily, why occupy the spirit table of the deceased?" The ghost replied, "Those who have passed away in your family, each has their own destination; this seat is empty, thus temporarily occupying it." Thus, the ghost departed. This is from the sixth chapter of the Zhu Lin.

    109

    宋沙门二字广记引作何昙远，庐江人也父万寿，御史中丞，远奉法精至，持菩萨戒，年十八，元嘉九年，丁父艰，哀毁致招疾，殆将灭性，号踊之外，便归心净土，庶祈感应。远时请僧，常有数人，师僧含亦在焉。远常向含悔忏宿业，恐有烦缘，终无感彻；僧含每奖厉，劝以莫怠。至十年二月十六日夜，转经竟，众僧已眠，四更中，忽自唱言歌诵，僧含惊而问之，远曰：“见佛身黄金色，形状大小，如今行像，金光周身，浮焰丈余，旛华翼从，充牣虚空，瑰妙丽极，事绝言称。”远时住西厢中，云：佛自西来，转身西向，当宁而立，呼其速去。昙远常日羸喘，示有气息，此夕壮厉，悦乐动容，便起净手。含布香手中，并取园华，遥以散佛。母谓远曰：“汝今若去，不念吾耶？”远无所言，俄而顿卧；家既宿信，闻此灵异，既皆欣肃，不甚悲惧。远至五更，忽然而终，中宅芬馨，数日乃歇。珠林十五广记一百十四

    Explanation

    109

    During the Song Dynasty, a monk named Tan Yuan, whose name is also recorded as He Tan Yuan in the Guang Ji (Volume 114), was from Lujiang. His father, Wan Shou, held the title of Yushi Zhongcheng (a high-ranking official). Tan Yuan observed the Dharma with great dedication and upheld the Bodhisattva precepts. At the age of eighteen, in the ninth year of the Yuanjia era, he experienced the death of his father, which led to deep grief and illness, nearly causing him to lose his life. Beyond crying and wailing, he dedicated himself to the Pure Land, hoping for a response or manifestation. Tan Yuan regularly invited several monks, including Seng Han, to his home. He frequently confessed his past sins to Seng Han, fearing that there might be obstacles, but eventually there was no response. Seng Han often encouraged him, urging him not to become complacent.

    On the sixteenth day of the second month of the tenth year, during the fourth watch of the night, after completing the recitation of scriptures, the other monks had already fallen asleep. Suddenly, Tan Yuan began to sing and chant on his own. Seng Han was startled and asked him what had happened. Tan Yuan replied, "I saw the Buddha's body, golden in color, with a shape and size like the image of a Buddha statue. His body was surrounded by golden light, with floating flames several feet high. Banners and flowers surrounded him, filling the void with their beauty and wonder, beyond description." At the time, Tan Yuan was in the western hall, where he said the Buddha came from the west, turned around to face the west, stood facing the central hall, and called for him to leave quickly.

    Tan Yuan, who was usually weak and breathless, showed signs of life that night, appearing vigorous and joyful. His face lit up with pleasure, and he immediately washed his hands. Seng Han placed incense in his hand and took flowers from the garden, scattering them towards the Buddha. His mother said to Tan Yuan, "If you are leaving now, do you not miss me?" Tan Yuan said nothing and soon after lay down suddenly. The family, who had long been believers, heard of this miraculous event and were all joyful and respectful, not overly sad or fearful. Tan Yuan passed away at the fifth watch of the night, and the house was filled with a fragrant aroma that lasted for several days. This event is recorded in Zhu Lin (Volume 15) and Guang Ji (Volume 114).

    110

    宋尼释智通，京师简静尼也，年貌姝少，信道不笃。元嘉九年，师死罢道嫁为魏郡梁群甫妻；生一男，年大七岁，家甚贫，无以为衣。通为尼时，有数卷素无量寿法华等经，悉练捣之，以衣其儿。居一年，而得病，恍忽惊悸，竟体剥烂，状若火疮，有细白虫，日去升余，燥痛烦毒，昼夜号叫。常闻空中语云：“坏经为衣，得此剧报。”旬余而死。珠林十八广记一百十六

    Explanation

    110

    Shi Zhitong, a nun from the Song dynasty, was a simple and tranquil nun from the capital city. She was young and beautiful, but not firmly committed to her faith. In the ninth year of the reign of Emperor Wu of Liu Song (432 AD), after the death of her teacher, she left the monastic life and married a man named Liang Qunfu from Wei Prefecture. They had a son who was seven years old. The family was very poor and lacked clothing. Shi Zhitong had several scrolls of the Amitabha Sutra and Lotus Sutra. She washed and pounded these scrolls to make clothes for her son. After a year, the child fell ill, experiencing confusion, fear, and a condition where his body peeled off like a burn, with small white worms emerging. He suffered from severe pain and fever, crying day and night. He often heard voices in the air saying, "Destroying the sutras to make clothes, you receive this severe retribution." The child died after ten days.

    Source: 珠林十八广记一百十六

    111

    宋仑氏二女，东官曾城人也，是时祖姊妹。元嘉九年。一引作元年姊年十岁，妹年九岁，里越愚蒙，未知经法。忽以二月八日并失所在，三日而归，粗说见佛。九月十五日又失，一旬还，作外国语，诵经及梵书见西域沙门，便相开解。明年正月十五日，忽复失之，田间作人云：见其从风径飘上天。父母号惧，祀神求福。一引作父母哀哭求祷神鬼既而经月乃返，剃头为尼，被服法衣，持发而归。自说；见佛及比丘尼，曰：“汝宿世因缘，应为我弟子。”举手摩头，发因堕落，与其法名；大曰法缘小曰法彩。临遣还，曰：“可作精舍，当与汝经法也。”女既归家，即毁除鬼座，缮立精庐，夜齐诵经，夕中每有五色光明，流泛峰岭，若灯烛。二女自此后容止华雅，音制诠正，上京风调，不能过也。刺史韦朗孔默等三字一引作就里并迎供养，闻其谈说，甚敬异焉。于是溪里皆知奉法。珠林五又二十二

    Explanation

    111

    Two daughters of the Song Lun family, residents of Dongguan Zengcheng, were cousins at the time. In the ninth year of the Yanchang era (432 AD), the elder sister was ten years old, and the younger sister was nine. Living in a remote village, they were ignorant of the scriptures and the Dharma. Suddenly, on the eighth day of the second month, both disappeared, and after three days, they returned, roughly describing having seen a Buddha. On the fifteenth day of the ninth month, they disappeared again, returning after ten days, speaking a foreign language, reciting scriptures and Sanskrit texts, and meeting monks from the Western Regions, immediately understanding each other. In the following year, on the fifteenth day of the first month, they suddenly disappeared again. Farmers in the fields reported seeing them being carried away by the wind and ascending into the sky. Their parents cried out in fear and worshipped gods to seek blessings. After a month, they returned, shaved their heads to become nuns, dressed in monastic robes, and carried their hair back. They said for themselves that they had seen a Buddha and nuns, and the Buddha said, "Your past-life karma has led you to be my disciples." He raised his hands and touched their heads, and their hair fell out. He gave them Buddhist names: the elder was named Fa Yuan, and the younger was named Fa Cai. When they were about to be sent back, he said, "You can build a temple, and I will give you the scriptures and teachings." After returning home, they immediately destroyed the altars for spirits, built a temple, and at night, they chanted the scriptures together. At dusk, there was often a five-colored light, flowing over the peaks and ridges, like lamps and candles. From then on, their demeanor became elegant and refined, their speech well-structured and correct, surpassing the style of the capital. Governor Wei Lang, Kong Mo, and others welcomed and supported them, hearing their discussions, greatly respecting and admiring them. Thus, everyone in the village came to respect the law. Julu 5, also 22.

    112

    宋玉球，字叔达，太原人也，为涪陵太守，以元嘉九年于郡失守，系在刑狱，着一重锁，钉鍱坚固。球先精进，既在囹圄，用心尤至。狱中百余人，并多饥饿，球每食，皆分施之。日自持斋至心念观世音。夜梦升高座，见一沙门，以一卷经与之，题云“光明安行品并诸菩萨名”球得而披读，忘第一菩萨名，第二观世音，第三大势至，又见一车轮沙门曰：“此五道轮也。”既觉，锁皆断脱球心知神力弥增专到，因自钉治其锁，经三日而被原宥。珠林二十三

    Explanation

    112

    Cao Yuqiu, courtesy name Shuda, was from Taiyuan. He served as the governor of Fuling and lost control of the city in the ninth year of the Yuanjia era (432 AD). As a result, he was imprisoned in a criminal court, where he was chained with a heavy lock that was firmly secured. Cao Yuqiu had always been diligent in his practice, and upon being imprisoned, he focused his efforts even more intently. There were over a hundred prisoners in the jail, many of whom were suffering from hunger. Whenever Cao Yuqiu ate, he would share his food with them. Each day, he would fast and meditate on the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara with great sincerity. One night, he dreamed of ascending to a high seat and encountering a monk who handed him a scroll of scripture, which was inscribed with the title "The Chapter of Enlightened Conduct and the Names of the Bodhisattvas." Cao Yuqiu read through it, but he could not remember the name of the first Bodhisattva, only recognizing the second as Avalokiteshvara and the third as Mahasthamaprapta. In the dream, he also saw another monk holding a wheel, who said, "This is the wheel of the Five Paths." Upon waking, he found that the lock on his chains had broken. Cao Yuqiu realized that his spiritual practice had increased his supernatural power, and he felt a deep sense of determination. He then proceeded to fix the lock himself, and after three days, he was pardoned. This account is recorded in the 23rd chapter of the Jewel Forest.

    113

    宋刘龄者，不知何许人也，居晋陵东路城屯，颇奉法，于宅中立精舍一闲，时设斋集。元嘉九年三月二十七日，父暴病亡。巫祝并云：家当更有三人丧亡。邻家有道士祭酒，姓魏名叵，常为章符，诳化屯里，语龄曰：“君家衰祸未已，由奉胡神故也。若事大道，必蒙福祐，不改意者，将来灭门。”龄遂揭延祭酒，罢不奉法。叵云：“宜焚去经像，灾乃当除耳。”遂闭精舍户，放火焚烧，炎炽移日，而所烧者，唯屋而已，经像旛○，俨然如故，像于中夜，又放火赫然。时诸祭酒有二十许人，亦有惧畏灵验，密委去者。叵等师徒，犹盛意不止；被发偊步，执持刀索，云斥佛还胡国，不得留中夏，为民害也。龄于其夕，如有人殴打之者，顿仆于地，家人扶起，示余气息，遂委挛躄不能行动，道士魏叵，其时体内发疽，日出二升，不过一月，受苦便死。自外同伴，并皆着癞。其邻人东安太守水丘和传于东阳无疑，时亦多有见者。珠林六十二

    Explanation

    113

    A Man Named Liu Ling from the Song Dynasty

    Liu Ling, a man from the Song Dynasty, was of unknown origin and resided in the Jinling Eastern Road City Garrison. He followed the law to some extent and built a small temple in his home, where he held periodic vegetarian feasts and gatherings. On the 27th day of the third month in the ninth year of the Yuanjia era, his father died suddenly. The shamans and diviners all said that his family would have three more deaths. A Taoist priest named Wei Po from a neighboring house, who often used talismans and deceived the people in the garrison, told Liu Ling, "Your family's misfortune has not ended because you worship foreign gods. If you serve the great Tao, you will surely receive blessings. If you do not change your mind, your entire family will be destroyed." Liu Ling then invited the Taoist priest and stopped following the law. Wei Po said, "You should burn the scriptures and statues, and the disaster will be eliminated." Liu Ling then closed the temple doors and set fire to them. The fire burned for a whole day, but what was burned was only the buildings. The scriptures, statues, and banners remained undamaged. In the middle of the night, the statue itself seemed to set fire again.

    At that time, there were about twenty Taoist priests. Some were also afraid of the miraculous events and secretly left. Wei Po and his disciples still persisted in their efforts. They went around with disheveled hair and weapons, claiming to drive the Buddha back to the foreign land, not allowing him to stay in China, where he would harm the people. That night, it seemed as if someone was beating Liu Ling. He fell to the ground, and his family helped him up, showing that he was still alive. He became paralyzed and could no longer move. The Taoist priest Wei Po developed a boil inside his body, producing two liters of pus daily, and he died within a month. His fellow practitioners also contracted leprosy. His neighbor, the governor of Dong'an, Shui Qiuhe, passed this story on to Dongyang Wuyi. Many people also saw these events. This story is recorded in "Jade Forest, Volume 62."

    114

    宋马虔伯，巴西阆中人也，少信佛法，尝作宣汉县宰。以元嘉十二年七月夜，于县得梦：见天际有三人，长二丈余，姿容严丽，临云下观，诸天妓乐盈仞，空中告曰：“汝厄在荆楚，戊寅之年，八月四日，若处山泽，其祸克消，人中斋戒亦可获免，若过此期，当悟道也。”时俯见相识杨暹等八人，并着锁械，又见道士胡辽，半身土中。天中天际神人皆记八人命尽年月，唯语辽曰：“若能修立功德，犹可延长也。”暹等皆如期终亡，辽益惧奉法，山居勤励弥至。

    Explanation

    114

    Ma Qianbo, from Langzhong, Bashu, was a devout follower of Buddhism. He once served as the magistrate of Xuanhan County. In the twelfth year of the Yuanjia era (435 AD), during the night of July, he had a dream: he saw three figures at the edge of the sky, each over two zhang tall, dignified and beautiful, descending from the clouds to observe. There were many heavenly musicians and dancers filling the space. From the air, they spoke to him: "Your calamity is in Jingchu. On the day of the Earth Tiger, August 4th, if you stay in the mountains and lakes, the calamity will be eliminated. If you observe fasting and purification, you can also be saved. If you miss this period, you will attain enlightenment." He saw eight familiar people, including Yang Xian, all bound with shackles. He also saw the Taoist priest Hu Liao, half of whose body was in the ground. The gods in the sky and at the edge of the sky all recorded the years and months when the eight people would die. They only spoke to Hu Liao: "If you can perform good deeds, you can extend your life." Yang Xian and the others all died as predicted. Hu Liao became even more fearful and devoted to the law, living in the mountains and working diligently.

    115

    虔伯后为梁州西曹掾广记引有掾字州将萧思话也，萧转南蛮，复命为行参军，虔伯耳荆楚之言，心甚惧然，求萧解职，将适衡山，萧苦不许。十五年即戊寅岁也，六月末，得病，至八月四日，危笃守命。其日黄昏后，忽朗然彻视，遥见西面有三人，形长可二丈，前一人衣?垂鬓，顶光圆明，后二人姿质金曜，仪相端备，列于空中，去地数仞。虔伯委悉详视，犹是前所梦者也。顷之不见，余芳移时方歇，同居小大，皆闻香气，因而流汗，病即小瘥。虔伯所居宇卑陋，于时自觉处在殿堂，廊壁环曜，皆是珍宝。于是所患悉以平复。珠林三十二广记一百十三

    Explanation

    115

    Qianbo later served as the Western Cao Assistant of Liangzhou, as cited in the Guangji with the term 'Cao', referring to the state governor Xiao Sihua. Xiao was reassigned as a traveling military advisor. Qianbo heard the words of Jingchu, and was greatly afraid, requesting Xiao to resign and planning to go to Mount Heng, but Xiao strongly refused. The year was the 15th year of the Wu Yin period. In late June, he fell ill, and by August 4th, his condition was critical, but he held on. That evening, he suddenly saw clearly, far to the west, three people, tall, about two zhang. The first person was dressed in fine clothes, with hanging hair, and a round, bright halo on top of his head. The next two had golden, radiant features and dignified, complete demeanor, standing in the air, several ren away from the ground. Qianbo carefully observed, and it was still what he had dreamed of before. Soon they disappeared, and the lingering fragrance took a long time to fade. Everyone living there, regardless of age, smelled the fragrance, as a result, he sweated, and his condition improved slightly. Qianbo's dwelling was humble and shabby, at that moment, he felt himself in a hall, with corridors and walls shining with light, all adorned with treasures. Thus, all his ailments were cured. Zhu Lin 32, Guang Ji 113.

    116

    宋沙门竺惠庆，广陵人也，经行修明。元嘉十二年，荆扬大水，川陵如一。惠庆将入庐山，船至小，而暴风忽起，同旅已得依浦，唯惠庆船未及得泊；飘扬中江，风疾浪涌，静待沦覆。庆正心端念，诵观世音经，洲际之人，望见其船迎飙截流，如有数十人牵挽之者，迳到上岸，一舫全济。珠林六十五
    　　宋葛济之，句容人，稚川后也。妻同郡纪氏体貌闲雅，甚有妇德。济之世事仙学，纪氏亦同，而心乐佛法，常存诚不替。元嘉十三年，方在机织，忽觉云日开朗，空中清明，因投释筐梭，仰望四表；见西方有如来真形，及宝盖旛幢，蔽映天汉。心独喜曰：“经说无量寿佛，即此者耶？”便头面作礼。济之敬其如此，仍起就之，纪授济手，指示佛所，济亦登见半身及诸旛盖，俄而隐没。于是云日鲜彩，五色烛耀，乡比亲族，颇亦睹见。两三食顷，方稍除歇。自是屯闾多归法者。珠林十五广记一百十四

    Explanation

    116

    A Buddhist Monk Named Zhi Huaiqing from the Song Dynasty, a native of Yangzhou, was devout and knowledgeable. In the twelfth year of the Yuanchi era (435 AD), there was a great flood in Jingzhou and Yangzhou, submerging the rivers and mountains as one. Zhi Huaiqing was about to enter Mount Lu, and his small boat was caught in a sudden storm while others had already found shelter. His boat was drifting in the middle of the river, facing strong winds and waves, and it seemed destined to sink. Zhi Huaiqing focused his mind and thoughts, reciting the Sutra of the Bodhisattva Avalokiteshvara. People on the shore saw his boat defying the wind and currents, as if pulled by dozens of people, and it eventually reached the shore safely, with all aboard unharmed. This story is recorded in Zhu Lin (Chapter 65).

    Ge Jizhi, a native of Jurong, was a descendant of Ge Hong, a famous alchemist and Taoist scholar. His wife, Ji, from the same province, was graceful and virtuous. Ge Jizhi followed Taoist practices, and Ji did the same, but she had a particular interest in Buddhism and remained sincere in her faith. In the thirteenth year of the Yuanchi era (436 AD), while weaving, Ji suddenly felt a sense of clarity and peace. She looked up and saw the Buddha of Infinite Life, along with canopies and banners, overshadowing the Milky Way. She was delighted and thought, "The sutras say the Buddha of Infinite Life, is this him?" She then bowed her head and face in reverence. Ge Jizhi, seeing her devotion, got up and went to her. Ji showed him the direction of the Buddha, and Ge Jizhi also saw the Buddha's half-body and the various canopies and banners, which soon disappeared. The sky and sun became colorful, and many people in the community saw the same phenomenon. After a couple of meals, the event gradually subsided. From then on, many people in the community turned to Buddhism. This story is recorded in Zhu Lin (Chapter 15, Guangji 114).

    117

    宋尼慧木者，姓傅氏，十一出家，受持小戒，居梁郡筑弋屯寺，始读大品，日诵两卷。师慧超，尝建经堂，木往礼拜，辄见屋内东北隅有一沙门，金色黑衣，足不履地。木又于夜中卧而诵习，梦到西方，见一浴池，有芙蓉华，诸化生人，列坐其中；有一大华，独空无人，木欲登华，攀牵用力，不觉诵经，音响高大，木母谓其魇惊，起唤之。木母笃老，口无复齿，木恒嚼哺饴母，为以过中，不得净漱，故年将立，不受大戒。母终亡后，木自除草开坛，请师受戒。

    Explanation

    117

    Nun Hui Mu of the Song dynasty, surnamed Fu, entered the monastic life at the age of eleven, received and upheld the lesser precepts, and dwelled in the Zui Tun Temple in Liang Prefecture. She began reading the Mahaprajnaparamita Sutra and recited two scrolls daily. Her teacher, Hui Chao, once built a scripture hall. When Hui Mu went to pay homage, she often saw a monk in the northeast corner of the room, golden in complexion and wearing black robes, whose feet did not touch the ground. At night, while lying down and reciting and studying, she dreamed of the Western Paradise, where she saw a bathing pool filled with lotus flowers and various beings born through transformation seated in rows. There was a large lotus flower, empty and without anyone. Hui Mu wanted to climb onto it, strained and pulled with effort, and unconsciously recited the sutra. The sound was loud and resonant. Her mother thought she was having a nightmare and got up to call to her. Hui Mu's mother was very old and had no teeth left. Hui Mu always chewed food and fed her mother, but because it was past noon, she could not perform a clean rinse, so she did not receive the full precepts as she approached adulthood. After her mother passed away, Hui Mu cleared the grass and prepared a platform, inviting a teacher to receive the precepts.

    118

    忽于坛所见天地晃然，悉黄金色，仰望西南，见一天人，着○衣，衣色赤黄，去木或近或远，寻没不见。凡见灵异，秘不语人。木兄出家，闻而欲知，乃诳诱之曰：“汝为道积年，竟无所招，比可养发，当访出门。”木闻甚惧，谓当实然，乃粗言所见。唯静称尼闻其道德，称往为狎，方便请问，乃为具说。木后与同等共礼无量寿佛，因伏地不起，咸谓得眠，蹴而问之，木竟不答，静称复独苦求问，木云：“当伏地之时，梦往安养国见佛，为说小品，已得四卷，因被蹴即觉，甚追恨之。”木元嘉十四年时已六十九。珠林十五

    Explanation

    118

    A Sudden Vision and Its Aftermath

    Suddenly, at the altar, he saw the heavens and earth shimmering, all in a golden hue. Looking up to the southwest, he saw a celestial being dressed in a robe of red and yellow, appearing sometimes near and sometimes far, eventually disappearing. All that he saw of the supernatural, he kept secret and did not speak of to others. Brother Mu, who had become a monk, heard of this and wanted to know more, so he deceived him, saying, "You have practiced the Way for many years, but have achieved nothing. Soon you will be able to grow your hair, and then you should leave the monastery." Mu was very afraid upon hearing this and thought it was true, so he roughly described what he had seen. Only the nun Jingcheng, who heard of his virtue, approached him with familiarity and skillfully asked, so he told her everything. Later, Mu and his peers worshipped the Buddha of Infinite Life, and because he fell to the ground and did not rise, they thought he had fallen asleep. They kicked him to ask, but Mu did not answer. Nun Jingcheng then persistently asked again, and Mu said, "When I was lying on the ground, I dreamed of going to the Pure Land and meeting the Buddha, who spoke to me a small sutra, which I have already received in four volumes. I was awakened by being kicked, and I deeply regret it." Mu was sixty-nine years old in the 14th year of the Yuanjia era. This account is from the 15th volume of the "Jewel Forest."

    119

    宋释僧瑜，吴兴余杭人，本姓周氏，弱冠出家，号为神理，精修苦业，始终不渝。元嘉十五年，游憩庐山，同侣有昙温慧光等，皆厉操贞洁，俱尚幽栖。乃共筑架其山之阳，今招隐精舍是也。瑜常以为：结溺三途，情形故也，情将尽矣，形亦宜损；药王之○，独何云远？于是屡发言誓，始契烧身，四十有四，孝建二年六月三日，将就本志，道俗赴观，车骑填接。瑜率众行道，训授典戒。尔日密云将雨，瑜乃慨然发誓曰：“若我所志克明，天当清朗；如期诚无感，便宜滂澍。使此四辈知神应之无昧也。”言已，顷之，云景明霁。及焚爓交至，合掌端一，有紫气腾空，别表烟外，移晷乃歇。后旬有四日，瑜所住房里，双桐生焉，根枝丰茂，巨细如一，贯榱直竦，遂成鸿树。理识者以为娑罗宝树，克炳泥洹，瑜之庶几，故见斯证。因号曰双桐沙门。吴郡张辩，时为平南长史，亲睹其事，具为传赞云。珠林六十三

    Explanation

    119

    A Monk Named Seng Yu of the Song Dynasty

    Seng Yu was a monk from Yuhang, Wu Prefecture, originally surnamed Zhou. At the age of twenty, he became a monk and was known for his mastery of spiritual principles. He diligently practiced ascetic practices and remained steadfast throughout his life. In the fifteenth year of the Yuanjia era (438 AD), he visited and stayed at Mount Lu, where he met fellow monks such as Tan Wen and Hui Guang, all of whom maintained pure and upright conduct and favored seclusion. Together, they built a dwelling on the sunny side of the mountain, which is now known as the Zhaoyin Monastery.

    Seng Yu often believed that being trapped in the cycle of rebirth was due to the nature of body and mind. When the mind is exhausted, the body should also be reduced. He thought that the practice of self-immolation, similar to the self-sacrifice of a medicine king, was not far-fetched. Therefore, he repeatedly made vows and began to agree to self-immolation. On the third day of the sixth month in the second year of the Xiaojian era (455 AD), he intended to fulfill his vow. Monks and laypeople came to witness the event, and carriages and horses filled the roads. Seng Yu led the congregation in chanting and taught the precepts. On that day, dark clouds were about to bring rain. Seng Yu made a solemn vow with great emotion: "If my wish is granted, the sky will be clear and bright; if my wish is not granted, it would be better for it to rain. So that these four groups of people know that the divine response is not hidden." After he spoke, soon after, the clouds cleared and the sky became bright. When the flames reached him, he had his hands joined and focused, and a purple aura rose into the air, separately visible outside the smoke, lasting for a while before disappearing.

    Fourteen days later, in the room where he lived, two cedars grew. The roots and branches were lush and uniform in size, straight and tall, piercing the rafters, thus becoming great trees. Those who understand the meaning believe they are the sacred sala trees, shining brightly in Nirvana, a sign of his near attainment. He was then called the Double Cedar Monk. Zhang Bian of Wu Prefecture, at the time the Chief Clerk of the Southern Pacification Department, witnessed the event personally and wrote a detailed account and praise.

    120

    宋阮稚宗者，河东人也，元嘉十六年，随钟离太守阮愔在郡。愔便与稚宗行至远屯，郡吏盖○边定随焉。行达民家，恍忽如眠，便不复寤；民以为死，举出门外，方营殡具，经夕能言。说：初有一百许人，缚稚宗去，行数十里，至一佛图，僧众供养，不异于世。有一僧曰：“汝好渔猎，今应受报。

    Explanation

    120

    In the sixteenth year of the Yuanjia era, a man named Ruan Zizong from Hedong followed the governor of Zhongli, Ruan Yin, to a remote military post. Gai Bianting, a local official, accompanied them. They reached a house where Ruan Zizong suddenly fell into a dazed state, as if he were asleep, and did not regain consciousness. The locals thought he was dead and carried him outside to prepare for burial. However, after a night, Ruan Zizong was able to speak again.

    He recounted that he had been taken by about a hundred people, who bound him and led him away for dozens of miles until they reached a Buddhist temple. The monks there were engaged in offerings and worship, just as they would in the world. One monk said to him, "You liked fishing and hunting in the past, and now you should receive your retribution."

    121

    ”便取稚宗皮，剥脔截具，如治诸牲兽之法，复纳于深水，钩口出之，剖破解切，若为脍状，又镬煮炉炙，初悉糜烂，随以还复，痛恼苦毒，至三乃止。问欲活不？稚宗便叩头请命。道人令其蹲地，以水灌之，云一灌除罪五百。稚宗苦求多灌，沙门曰：“唯三足矣。”见有蚁数头，道人指曰：“此虽微物，亦不可杀，无论复巨此者也。鱼肉自死，此可啖耳。斋会之日，悉着新衣，无新，可浣也。”稚宗因问：“我行旅有三，而独婴苦，何也？”道人曰：“彼二人自知罪福，知而故犯；唯尔愚蒙，不识缘报，故以相诫。”因尔便稣，数日能起。由是遂断渔○耳。珠林六十四

    Explanation

    121

    A monk took the skin of Zhi Zong, cut and prepared it as if treating various beasts, then placed it back into deep water, pulled it out with a hook, sliced and chopped it into pieces resembling sashimi, boiled it in a large pot and roasted it over a fire. Initially, everything was completely ruined, but then it was restored, causing intense physical and emotional suffering that lasted for three times before stopping. The monk asked if Zhi Zong wanted to live, and Zhi Zong knelt and begged for mercy. The monk made him squat and poured water over him, saying that each pour would remove 500 sins. Zhi Zong desperately requested more water to be poured, and the monk replied, "Only three times is enough." Seeing several ants, the monk pointed and said, "These are small creatures, but they should not be killed, let alone larger ones. Fish and meat should only be eaten if they die naturally. On days of religious gatherings, wear new clothes, or wash old clothes if new ones are not available." Zhi Zong then asked, "Among the three travelers, why was only I affected by this suffering?" The monk replied, "The other two knew their sins and rewards but deliberately committed them; you, being ignorant, did not understand the consequences, so I warned you." As a result, Zhi Zong recovered and was able to stand up after several days. From then on, he stopped fishing. This story is from Zhulin 64.

    122

    宋邢怀明，河间人，宋大将军参军，尝随南郡太守朱修之北伐，俱见陷没。于是伺○闲隙，俱得遁归，夜行昼伏，已经三日；犹惧追捕，乃遣人前觇虏○，即数日不还。一夕，将雨阴闇，所遣人将晓忽至。至乃惊曰：“向遥见火光甚明，故来投之，那得至而反闇？”修等怪愕。怀明先奉法，自征后，头上恒载观世音经，转读不废；尔夕亦暗诵，咸疑是经神力。于是常共祈心，遂以得免，居于京师。元嘉十七年，有沙门诣怀明云：“贫道见此巷中及君家，殊有血气，宜移避之。”语毕便去。怀明追而目之，出门便没，意甚恶之。经二旬，邻人张景秀伤父，及杀父妾，怀明以为血气之征，庶得无事。时与刘斌刘景文比门连接，同在一巷；其年，并以刘湛之党，同被诛夷云。珠林二十三

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    123

    宋程德度，武昌人，父道惠，广州刺史，度为卫军临川王行参军。时在寻阳，屋有?窠，夜见屋里忽然自明，有一小儿，从窠而出，长可尺余，洁净分明，至度床前曰：“君却后二年，当得长生之道。”儵然而灭。德度甚秘异之。元嘉十七年，随王镇广陵，遇禅师释道恭，因就学禅，甚有解分。到十九年春，其家武昌空斋，忽有殊香芬馥，达于衢路。阖境往观，三日乃歇。珠林二十八

    Explanation

    123

    Cheng Dedu of the Song Dynasty was from Wuchang. His father, Dao Hui, was the governor of Guangzhou, and Cheng Dedu served as an assistant military officer under the Prince of Linchuan. At the time, he was in Xunyang, where he had a nest in his house. One night, the inside of the house suddenly became illuminated. A small child emerged from the nest, about a foot tall, clean and distinct. The child walked up to Cheng Dedu's bed and said, "In two years, you will attain the way of immortality." The child then suddenly disappeared. Cheng Dedu found this event very mysterious and extraordinary. In the 17th year of the Yuanchang era (440 AD), he followed the Prince of Linchuan to Guangling, where he met the Zen master Shi Daogong. He began to study Zen Buddhism and gained significant understanding. By the spring of the 19th year (442 AD), in a vacant room in his family's home in Wuchang, a particularly fragrant aroma suddenly appeared and spread throughout the streets. People from the entire region came to see the phenomenon, and the fragrance lasted for three days before dissipating. This event is recorded in the 28th chapter of the Jade Forest.

    124

    宋刘琛之，沛郡人也，曾在广陵逢一沙门，谓琛之曰：“君有病气，然当不死，可作一二百钱食，饭饴众僧，则免斯患。”琛之素不信法，心起忿慢，沙门曰：“当加祗信，勿用为怒。”相去二十步，忽不复见。琛之经七日，便病时气，危顿殆死；至九日方昼。如梦非梦，见有五层佛图在其心上，有二十许僧绕塔作礼，因此而寤，即得大利，病乃稍愈。后在京师住，忽有沙门，先不相识，直来入户，曰：“君有法，缘何不精进？”琛之因说先所逢遇，答曰“此宾头卢也。”语已，便去，不知所向。琛之以元嘉十七年夏，于广陵遥见惠汪精舍前，旛盖甚众而无形像；驰往观之，比及到门，奄然都灭。珠林三十六

    Explanation

    124

    Liu Chenzhi, a native of Pei Commandery in the Song Dynasty, once encountered a monk in Guangling. The monk told Chenzhi, "You have an illness, but you will not die. You can prepare a meal worth one or two hundred coins to feed the monks, and then you will be free from this illness." Chenzhi always disbelieved in the Dharma and had a rebellious heart. The monk said, "You should add faith, do not be angry." They were twenty steps apart, and suddenly the monk disappeared.

    Chenzhi suffered from a severe illness for seven days and was on the verge of death. On the ninth day, during the day, he saw a five-story pagoda in his heart, as if in a dream but not quite. There were about twenty monks circling the pagoda in reverence. Because of this, he woke up and gained great benefit, and his illness gradually improved.

    Later, while living in the capital, a monk suddenly appeared, whom he did not recognize, and entered directly. He said, "You have a karmic connection with the Dharma, why are you not diligent?" Chenzhi then recounted his previous encounter, and the monk replied, "This is Venerable Punahala." After speaking, the monk left, and his destination was unknown.

    In the summer of the 17th year of the Yuanjia era, Chenzhi saw from afar at the entrance of the Huaiwang Monastery in Guangling a large number of banners and canopies but no visible images. He rushed to see it, but by the time he reached the gate, everything had vanished. This story is recorded in the Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest), volume thirty-six.

    125

    宋伏万寿，平昌人也。元嘉十九年，在广陵为卫府行参军，假讫返舟，四更初过江。初济之时，长波安流，中江而风起如箭，时又极暗，莫知所向。万寿先奉法勤至，唯一心归命观世音，念无闲息。俄尔与船中数人同睹北岸有光，状如屯火，相与喜曰：“此必是欧阳火也。”回舳趣之，未旦而至。问彼人，皆云。昨夜无然火者。方悟神力，至设斋会。珠林二十七
    　　宋顾迈，吴郡人也，奉法甚谨，为卫府行参军。元嘉十九年，亦自都还广陵，发石头城，便逆湖，朔风至横决，风势未弭，而舟人务进，既至中江，波浪方壮，迈单船孤征，忧危无计，诵观世音经，得十许遍，风势渐歇，浪亦稍小。既而中流屡闻奇香芬馥不歇，迈心独嘉，故归诵不辍，遂以安济。珠林二十七

    Explanation

    125

    During the 19th year of the reign of Emperor Wu of Liu Song, Fu Wanshou, a man from Pingchang, was serving as an assistant military officer in the guard department in Guangling. After his leave of absence ended, he returned by boat, crossing the river at the beginning of the fourth watch of the night. At the start of the crossing, the river was calm and smooth, but a strong wind suddenly arose in the middle of the river, like an arrow. The night was extremely dark, and no one knew where to go. Fu Wanshou had been diligently observing the precepts and devoted his mind entirely to the Bodhisattva Guanyin, without a moment's interruption in his recitation. Soon, he and several people on the boat saw a light on the northern bank, which looked like a campfire. They were delighted and said, "This must be the fire of Ouyang!" They turned the boat towards it and arrived before dawn. When they asked the people there, they all said that no one had lit a fire the previous night. Only then did they realize the power of the divine, and they held a vegetarian feast. This story is recorded in the 27th chapter of the Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest).

    During the 19th year of the reign of Emperor Wu of Liu Song, Gu Mai, a man from Wu County, was also serving as an assistant military officer in the guard department. He returned from the capital to Guangling, departing from Shitoucheng and heading upstream along the lake. A northerly wind suddenly arose, causing the river to surge. The wind did not subside, and the boatmen were eager to proceed. When they reached the middle of the river, the waves were becoming increasingly strong. Gu Mai was traveling alone in a single boat, feeling worried and without a plan. He began to recite the Sutra of the Bodhisattva Guanyin, completing it about ten times. The wind gradually calmed, and the waves also became smaller. As they continued down the river, they frequently smelled a strange fragrance that did not dissipate. Gu Mai found this fragrance pleasing and continued to recite the sutra without stopping. Thus, he was able to cross the river safely. This story is also recorded in the 27th chapter of the Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest).

    126

    秦沙门释道冏，乡里氏族，已载前记，秦姚弘始十八年，师道懿遣至河南霍山采钟乳，与同学道朗等四人共行。持炬探穴，入且三里，遇一深流，横木而过。冏最先济，后辈坠木而死，时火又灭，冥然昏闇。冏生念已尽，恸哭而已。犹故一心呼观世音，誓愿若蒙出路，供百人会，表报威神。经一宿而见小光炯然，状若荧火，儵忽之间，穴中尽明。于是见路，得出岩下，由此信悟弥深，屡睹灵异。元嘉十九年，临川康王作镇广陵，请冏供养。其年九月，于西斋中作十日观世音斋，已得九日，夜四更尽，众僧皆眠，冏起礼拜还欲坐禅，忽见四壁有无数沙门，悉半身出见，一佛螺髻，分明了了；有一长人，着平上帻，笺布裤褶，手把长刀，貌极雄异，捻香授道冏，道冏时不肯受，壁中沙门语云：“冏公可为受香，以覆护主人。”俄而霍然无所复见。当尔之时，都不见众会诸僧，唯睹所置释迦文行像而已。珠林六十五

    Explanation

    126

    A Monk from the Qin Region Named Dao Jiong

    The hometown and clan of Monk Dao Jiong are already recorded in previous accounts. In the eighteenth year of Emperor Yao Xing's reign (396 CE), Master Dao Yi sent him to Mount Huo in Henan to collect cave-dwelling snails. He traveled with three fellow students, including Dao Lang. Holding a torch, they explored a cave for about three miles, where they encountered a deep stream and crossed it by placing a log across. Monk Dao Jiong was the first to cross, but his companions fell off the log and drowned. At that moment, the fire went out, plunging them into total darkness. Dao Jiong felt all hope was lost and wept bitterly. Still, he called out with all his heart to Avalokiteshvara, vowing that if he were granted a way out, he would offer a meal for a hundred people to express gratitude to the Bodhisattva's power. After one night, he saw a faint but clear light, shaped like a firefly. In an instant, the entire cave was illuminated. He then saw a path and emerged from the cave. From this experience, his faith and understanding deepened, and he frequently witnessed miraculous phenomena. In the nineteenth year of Emperor Wen's reign (442 CE), Prince of Linchuan, serving as governor of Guangling (modern Yangzhou), invited Dao Jiong to reside and provide for him. In the ninth month of that year, in the western study, a ten-day fasting observance dedicated to Avalokiteshvara was held. After nine days, at the fourth watch of the night, all the monks were asleep, but Dao Jiong got up to pay respects and was about to resume meditation. Suddenly, he saw countless monks on the walls, all appearing with their upper bodies visible. Among them was a Buddha with a coiled topknot, clearly visible. There was also a tall man, wearing a flat-topped hat, a robe, and trousers, holding a long sword, with an extremely fierce appearance. He offered incense to Dao Jiong, but the monk refused to accept it. The monks on the wall said, "Master Jiong, you should accept the incense to protect the host." Soon, the vision disappeared, and at that moment, Dao Jiong could not see any of the gathered monks, only the statue of Shakyamuni Buddha that was placed there. This account is found in the sixty-fifth volume of the "Jewel Forest" (珠林).

    127

    宋尼释昙辉，蜀郡成都人也，本姓青阳，名白玉，年七岁，便乐坐禅。每坐，辄得境界，意未自了，亦谓是梦耳。曾与姊共寝，夜中入定，姊于屏风角得之，身如木石，亦无气息；姊大惊怪，唤告家人，互共抱扶，至晓不觉。奔问巫觋，皆言鬼神所凭。至年十一，有外国禅师?良耶舍者来入蜀，辉请咨所见，耶舍者以辉禅既有分，欲劝化令出家。时辉将嫁，已有定日，法育未展，闻说，其家潜迎还寺，家既知，将逼嫁之；辉遂不肯行，深立言誓：“若我道心不果，遂被限逼者，便当投火饲虎，弃除秽形，愿十方诸佛证见至心。刺史甄法崇，信尚正法，闻辉志业，迎与相见。并召纲佐及有怀沙门互加难问，辉敷演无屈，坐者叹之。崇乃许离夫家，听其入道。元嘉十九年，临川康王延致广陵。珠林二十二

    Explanation

    127

    Buddhist Nun Tanhui from the Song Dynasty was from Chengdu, Sichuan, originally surnamed Qingyang and named Baiyu. At the age of seven, she enjoyed sitting in meditation. Whenever she meditated, she would attain a state of mind, but her thoughts were not fully clear, and she also considered it to be a dream. Once she slept with her sister, and at night she entered a deep meditative state. Her sister found her at the corner of the screen, and her body was like wood and stone, with no breath. Her sister was greatly surprised and alarmed, and called her family. They all held and supported her, until dawn when she came to. They ran to consult sorcerers, who all said it was due to spirits. By the age of eleven, a foreign monk named Yeshe came to Sichuan. Tanhui asked for his opinion on what she saw. Yeshe, seeing that she had a natural aptitude for meditation, wanted to persuade her to become a nun. At the time, Tanhui was about to marry, and the wedding date was already set. Her legal marriage was not yet arranged, and upon hearing this, her family secretly brought her back to the temple. When the family found out, they tried to force her into marriage. Tanhui refused to go and made a deep vow: "If my spiritual heart is not fulfilled and I am forced to marry, I will throw myself into the fire to feed tigers, discard my impure form, and wish that the Buddhas of the ten directions witness my sincere heart." Governor Zhen Fachong, who believed and upheld the true Dharma, heard of Tanhui's aspirations and welcomed and met with her. He also summoned his officials and monks who had aspirations to question her. Tanhui spoke eloquently and without being defeated, and those present were impressed. Zhen then allowed her to leave her fiancé's family and enter the path of the Dharma. In the 19th year of the Yuanjia era, King Kang of Linchuan invited her to Guangling.

    时宋淮南赵习，元嘉二十年为卫军府佐，疾病经时，忧必不济，恒至心归佛。夜梦一人，形貌秀异，若神人者，自屋梁上，以小裹物及剃刀授习，云：“服此药，用此刀，病必即愈。”习既惊觉，果得刀药焉，登即服药，疾除出家，名僧秀，年逾八十乃亡。珠林二十二
    　　宋沙门释慧全，凉州禅师也，开训教授，门徒五百。有一弟子，性颇粗暴，全常不齿。后忽自云：得三道果，全以其无行，永不信许。全后有疾，此弟子夜来问讯时，户犹闭如故，全颇惊异，欲复验之。乃语明夕更来。因密塞窗户。加以重关。弟子中宵而至，迳到床前，谓全曰：“阇黎可见信来。”因曰：“阇黎过世，当生婆罗门家。

    Explanation

    128

    During the reign of Emperor Wen of Song, in the year 423 AD, Zhao Xi, a native of Huainan, served as an assistant in the military office. He suffered from a prolonged illness, deeply concerned that it would not be cured. He always sincerely turned to Buddhism in his heart. One night, he dreamed of a person with an exceptionally beautiful and noble appearance, resembling a deity, who appeared from the ceiling and gave him a small wrapped object and a razor. The figure said, "Take this medicine and use this razor, and your illness will surely be cured immediately." Zhao Xi was startled awake and indeed found the razor and medicine. He immediately took the medicine, and his illness was cured. He then left home to become a monk, named Xiu, and lived past eighty years old before passing away. This story is recorded in the "Jewel Forest" chapter twenty-two.

    In the Song dynasty, there was a monk named Shihuiquan, a Zen master from Liangzhou, who taught and instructed five hundred disciples. One of his disciples had a rather rough and violent temperament, and Shihuiquan often disdained him. Later, the disciple suddenly claimed to have attained the three fruits of enlightenment. Shihuiquan, however, did not believe him due to his lack of virtuous conduct and never accepted his claim. When Shihuiquan later fell ill, the disciple came to visit him at night. The door was still closed as usual, and Shihuiquan was quite surprised and wanted to test him again. He told the disciple to come back the next evening. Shihuiquan then secretly sealed the windows and doors. That night, the disciple arrived in the middle of the night and went directly to the bed, saying to Shihuiquan, "Venerable one, you can believe me now." He then said, "After your passing, you will be reborn into a Brahmin family."
