    ”全曰：“我坐禅积业，岂方生彼？”弟子云：“阇黎信道不笃，兼外学未绝，虽有福业，不能超诣；若作一胜会，得饭一圣人，可成道果耳。”全于是设会。弟子又曰：“可以僧伽黎布施，若有须者，勿择长幼。”及会讫施衣，有一沙弥，就全求衣，全谓是其弟子，全云：“吾欲拟奉圣僧，那得与汝？”回忆前言不得择人，便以欢施。他日见此沙弥，问云：“先与汝衣着不大耶？”沙弥曰：“非徒不得衣，亦有缘事，愧不预会。”全方悟先沙弥者，圣所化也。弟子久乃过世，过世之时，无复余异，唯冢四边，时有白光。全元嘉二十年犹存，居在酒泉。珠林十九

    Explanation

    129

    Quan said, "I practice meditation and accumulate merit; how could I not be reborn in a higher realm?" The disciple replied, "Venerable one, your faith in the path is not firm, and you have not completely abandoned external studies. Even though you have merit, you cannot transcend to higher realms. If you hold a grand assembly and offer food to a sage, you can attain enlightenment." Quan then held the assembly. The disciple further advised, "You can offer the Sanghali robes as alms; if anyone needs one, do not choose based on age." After the assembly, when distributing the robes, a novice monk approached Quan and asked for one. Quan thought he was one of his disciples and said, "I intended to offer it to a holy monk; how could I give it to you?" Recalling his earlier words that he should not choose based on people, Quan happily gave the robe away. On another day, Quan saw this novice monk and asked, "Wasn't the robe you received not too big?" The novice monk replied, "Not only did I not receive a robe, but there were also some reasons, and I am ashamed that I was not invited to the gathering." Quan finally realized that the previous novice monk was a manifestation of a sage. The disciple passed away after a long time; at the time of his passing, there were no other unusual phenomena, only around the grave, there was sometimes a white light. Quan was still alive in the 20th year of the Yuanjia era, residing in Jiuquan. This is recorded in the 19th chapter of the Zhu Lin.

    宋王胡者，长安人也。叔死数载，元嘉二十三年，忽见形还家，责胡以修谨有阙，家事不理，罚胡五杖。傍人及邻里，并闻其语及杖声，又见杖瘢迹，而不睹其形；唯胡犹得亲接。叔谓胡曰：“吾不应死神道须吾算诸鬼录，今大从吏兵，恐惊损墟里，故不将进耳。”胡亦大见众鬼纷闹若屯外。俄然叔辞去，曰：“吾来年七月七日，当复暂还，欲将汝行，游历幽途，使知罪福之报也。不须费设，若意不已，止可茶来耳。”至期果还，语胡家人云：“吾今将胡游观，毕，当使还，不足忧也。”胡即顿卧床上，泯然如尽。叔于是将胡遍观群山，备睹鬼怪，末至嵩高山。诸鬼遇胡，并有馔设，余族味不异世中，唯姜甚脆美。

    Explanation

    130

    Hu of Song, a native of Chang'an, had a brother who died several years ago. In the 23rd year of the Yuanjia era (447 AD), the spirit of the deceased brother suddenly appeared in the form of a living person and returned home. He reproached Hu for lacking in carefulness and propriety, and for neglecting household affairs, and punished him with five strokes. People around and neighbors all heard his words and the sound of the strokes, and also saw the marks of the strokes, but they did not see his form; only Hu could still touch him. The spirit said to Hu, "I should not have died, but the divine way required me to calculate the records of the ghosts. Now I am accompanied by many officials and soldiers, fearing to frighten or harm the village, so I did not bring them in." Hu also saw many ghosts gathered outside, causing a commotion. Soon after, the spirit said goodbye and left, saying, "I will return again next year on the seventh day of the seventh month, and I want to take you along to tour the underworld, to make you understand the retribution of sin and virtue. No need to spend money on preparations; if you wish, just bring tea." On the appointed day, he indeed returned and told Hu's family, "I will now take Hu to see the sights, and when we are done, I will send him back; there is no need to worry." Hu immediately lay down on the bed, as if he had passed away. The spirit then took Hu to see all the mountains, and they saw all kinds of ghosts and monsters. Finally, they reached Mount Song. Various ghosts met Hu, and there were preparations for food. The rest of the flavors were not different from those in the world, but only the ginger was very crisp and delicious.

    胡欲怀将还，左右人笑胡云：“止可此食，不得将还也。”胡末见一处，屋宇华旷，帐筵精整，有二少僧居焉。胡造之，二僧为设杂果槟榔等。胡游历久之，备见罪福苦乐之报，乃辞归。叔谓胡曰：“汝既已知善之可修，何宜在家？白足阿练，戒行精高，可师事也。”长安道人足白，故时人谓为白足阿练也，甚为魏虏所敬，虏主主事为师。胡既奉此谏于是寺中，遂见嵩山上年少僧者游学众中。胡大惊，与叙乖阔，问何时来？二僧答云：“贫道本住此寺，往日不忆，与君相识。”胡复说嵩高之遇，此僧云：“君谬耳，岂有此耶？”至明日，二僧无何而去。胡乃具告诸沙门，叙说往日嵩山所见；众咸惊怪，即追求二僧，不知所在，乃悟其神人焉。元嘉末，有长安僧释昙爽来游江南，具说如此也。珠林六

    Explanation

    131

    Hu wished to return home with something in mind, but those around him laughed at him and said, "You can only eat here; you cannot take it with you." Hu then came upon a place where the house was grand and spacious, the furnishings were finely arranged, and two young monks lived there. Hu visited them, and the monks prepared a variety of fruits and betel nuts for him. After wandering for a long time, Hu fully witnessed the rewards and punishments of sin and virtue, as well as the sufferings and joys of life, and then he bade farewell and returned home. His uncle said to Hu, "Since you have now come to know that virtue can be cultivated, why should you remain at home? Whitefoot Alayan is strict in precepts and high in moral conduct; you can serve him as a teacher." The monk from Chang'an, whose feet were bare, was thus called Whitefoot Alayan, and he was highly respected by the Wei barbarians, who regarded him as a teacher. Hu then followed this advice and stayed in the temple, where he saw the young monk from Mount Song among the students. Hu was greatly surprised and talked about how long it had been since they last met, asking when he had arrived. The two monks replied, "I originally lived in this temple, but I don't remember meeting you in the past." Hu then recounted his encounter with the young monk from Mount Song, but this monk said, "You are mistaken; how could there be such a thing?" The next day, the two monks left without further ado. Hu then told all the monks about what he had seen at Mount Song in the past; they were all astonished and immediately searched for the two monks, but they could not be found. Hu then realized that they were divine beings. At the end of the Yuanjia era, a monk from Chang'an named Shitan came to tour the south and recounted the same story. This is recorded in the sixth chapter of the "Julei."

    宋居士二字广记引有卞悦之，济阴人也。作朝请，居在潮沟。行年五十，未有子息，妇为娶妾，复积载不孕。将祈求继嗣，千遍转观世音经；广记引作发愿诵观世音经千遍其数垂竟，妾便有娠，遂生一男。时广记引有时字元嘉二十八年原夺二字今补己丑岁也。云云珠林五十二广记一百十一
    　　宋沙门释昙典白衣时年三十，忽暴疾而亡，经七日方活。说：初亡时，见二人驱将去，使辇米。伴辇可有数千人，昼夜无休息。见二道人云：“我是汝五戒本师。”来慰问之。师将往诣官主，云是贫道弟子，且无大罪，历算未穷。即见放遣。二道人送典至家，住其屋上，具约示典。可作沙门，勤修道业。言讫下屋，道人推典着尸腋下，于是而稣。后出家，经二十年，以元嘉十四年亡。珠林九十

    132

    During the reign of the Song Dynasty, the Yingya Shenglan records a man named Bian Yuezhi from Jiyin. He held a court title and lived in Chao Gou. At the age of fifty, he had no children, so his wife arranged for him to take a concubine. After many years, the concubine remained barren. Intending to pray for descendants, he recited the Guanyin Sutra a thousand times. The Yingya Shenglan records that he made a vow to recite the Guanyin Sutra a thousand times, nearly completing the recitation. Soon after, the concubine became pregnant and gave birth to a son. At the time, the Yingya Shenglan records that it was the year of the Earth Ox in the 28th year of the reign of Emperor Wen of Song (451 CE).

    During the reign of the Song Dynasty, a Buddhist monk named Shi Tandian, who was a layperson at the age of thirty, suddenly died of a severe illness. After seven days, he came back to life. He recounted that at the moment of death, he saw two people leading him away, sent to carry rice. There were about several thousand people carrying rice, day and night without rest. He saw two monks who said, "We are your original teachers of the Five Precepts," and came to console him. The monks led him to the official, saying that he was their disciple, and that he had no great sin, and the calculation of fate had not run out. He was immediately released and sent away. The two monks escorted Tandian back home, stayed on the roof of the house, and explained everything to him. They advised him to become a monk and diligently practice the Dharma. After finishing speaking, the monks descended from the roof, pushed Tandian onto the body's armpit, and thus he revived. He later became a monk, practiced for twenty years, and died in the 14th year of the reign of Emperor Wen of Song (437 CE).

    宋王淮之字元曾，琅琊人也，世以儒专，不信佛法。常谓：身神俱灭，宁有三世？元嘉中，为丹阳令，十年，得病气绝，少时还复暂苏。时建康令贺道力省疾，下床会，淮之语力曰：“始知释教不虚，人死神存，信有征矣。”道力曰：“明府生平置论不尔，今何见而乃异之耶？”上二字及乃字并依广记引补淮之敛?答云：“神实不尽，佛教不得不信。”语卒而终。珠林七十九广记九十九
    　　宋沙门慧和者，京师众造寺僧也。宋义嘉难，和犹为白衣，隶刘胡部下。胡尝遣将士数十人值谍东下，和亦预行。行至雀渚而值台军西上，谍众离散，各逃草泽，和得窜下至新林外会。见野老衣服缕弊，和乃以完整裤褶易其衣，提篮负担，若类田人。时诸游军捕此散谍，视和形色，疑而问之；和答对谬略，因被笞掠，登将见斩。和自散走，但恒诵念观世音经，至将斩时，祈恳弥至。既而军人挥刃屡跌，三举三折，并惊而释之。和于是出家，遂成精业。珠林二十七

    Explanation

    133

    Wēi Huái zhī, whose courtesy name was Yuán Zēng, was from Lángyá. His family had long been devoted to Confucianism and did not believe in Buddhism. He often said, "The body and spirit both perish; how can there be three temporal realms?" During the reign of Emperor Wen of Song (Yùnjiā era), he served as the magistrate of Dānyáng. After ten years, he fell ill and appeared to die, but after a short while, he briefly revived. At that time, the magistrate of Jiàn Kāng, Hè Dàolì, came to visit him as he lay on his deathbed. Wēi Huái zhī spoke to Hè Dàolì, saying, "I now know that Buddhism is not empty or false; the spirit continues to exist after death, and there is indeed evidence of this." Hè Dàolì replied, "Your Excellency, you have always held different views in the past. What have you seen now that makes you change your mind?" Wēi Huái zhī, gathering his strength, answered, "The spirit is indeed not exhausted; one cannot help but believe in Buddhism." With these words, he passed away.

    The Zūlín (Volume 79), Guǎngjì (Volume 99).

    During the reign of Emperor Wen of Song, there was a monk named Huì Hé, a resident of the temple in the capital city. During the turmoil of the Yìjiā era, Huì Hé was still a layperson and served under the command of Lǐu Hú. Lǐu Hú once sent dozens of soldiers on a reconnaissance mission to the east, and Huì Hé was among them. They reached Qièzhǔ, but encountered the central government’s troops marching westward. The reconnaissance force was scattered, and everyone fled into the wilderness. Huì Hé managed to escape and reached the outskirts of Xīnlín. There, he saw an old farmer whose clothes were tattered. Huì Hé exchanged his complete trousers and jacket for the old man’s clothes, then carried a basket and a burden, appearing like a farmer. At that time, the patrol forces were searching for the scattered reconnaissance soldiers. Seeing Huì Hé’s appearance, they suspected him and questioned him. Huì Hé gave vague and inconsistent answers, and as a result, he was beaten and was about to be executed. As Huì Hé fled, he constantly recited the Guānshìyīn Sūtra. When the executioner was about to strike, Huì Hé’s prayers grew more fervent. The executioner’s sword slipped three times, and each time it fell short. Startled, the executioner released him. Huì Hé then left the military and entered monastic life, eventually achieving great spiritual attainments.

    The Zūlín (Volume 27).

    宋慧远沙门者，江陵长沙寺僧也，师慧印，善禅法，号曰禅师。远本印苍头，名黄迁，年二十时，印每入定，辄见迁先世乃是其师，故遂度为弟子。常寄江陵市西杨道产家，行般舟勤苦岁余，因尔遂颇有感变；或一日之中，赴十余处斋，虽复终日竟夜行道转经，而家家悉见黄迁在焉。众稍敬异之，以为得道。孝建二年一日，自言死期，谓道产曰：“明夕吾当于君家过世。”至日，道产设八关，然灯通夕。

    Explanation

    134

    Cui Huayan, a monk at the Changsha Temple in Jiangling, was a disciple of Huayan, who was skilled in Zen meditation and was known as a Zen master. Originally, Cui Huayan was Huayan's servant, named Huang Qian. When he was twenty years old, Huayan would often enter meditation and see in a vision that Huang Qian's previous life was his own teacher. Therefore, Huayan decided to ordain Huang Qian as a disciple. Cui Huayan often stayed at the home of Yang Daochan in the western part of Jiangling. He practiced the Banzhou method, involving continuous walking meditation, for over a year, and as a result, he experienced significant spiritual transformations. Sometimes, in a single day, he would attend more than ten religious ceremonies, continuing his spiritual practices throughout the day and night, and everyone who saw him would see Huang Qian. People began to respect and consider him enlightened. In the second year of the Xiaojian era, Cui Huayan announced his impending death, telling Yang Daochan, "Tomorrow night, I will pass away at your place." On that day, Yang Daochan prepared by setting up the Eight Precepts and lighting lamps all night.

    初夜中夜，迁犹豫众行道，休然不异；四更之后，乃称疲而卧，颜色稍变，有顷而尽。○境为设三七斋，起塔，塔今犹存。死后久之，现形多宝寺，谓昙珣道人云：“明年二月二十三日，当与诸天共相迎也。”言已而去。昙珣即于长沙禅房设斋九十日，舍身布施至其日，苦乏气，自知必终，大延道俗，盛设法会。三更中，呼问众僧：“有闻见不？”众自不觉异也，珣曰：“空中有奏乐声，馨烟甚异，黄迁之契，今其至矣。”众僧始还堂就席，而珣已尽。珠林九十七又十九
    　　宋路昭太后大明四年，造普贤菩萨乘宝轝白象，安于中兴禅房，因设讲于寺。其年十月八日，斋毕解座，会僧二百人。于时寺宇始构，帝甚留心，辇跸临幸，旬必数四，僧徒勤整，禁卫严肃。尔日僧名有定，就席久之，忽有一僧，预于座次，风貌秀举，阖堂惊瞩，斋主与语，往还百余言，忽不复见。列筵同睹识其神人矣。珠林十七

    135

    At the early and middle watches of the night, Huang Qian hesitated among the crowd on the road, resting peacefully without any difference; after the fourth watch, he claimed to be tired and went to sleep, his appearance gradually changing, and in a short while, it was over. The environment was set up for a three-seven斋 (a type of ritual or ceremony), a stupa was built, and it still exists today. After his death, for a long time, he appeared in the Many Treasures Temple, telling the monk Tanxun, "Next year on February 23rd, I will be welcomed by the heavenly beings together." After speaking, he left. Tanxun immediately set up a ninety-day斋 (ritual) in the Chan room of Changsha, offering his body as a sacrifice until that day, suffering from lack of energy, he knew he would die soon, greatly inviting both monks and laypeople, and held a grand Dharma assembly. In the third watch of the night, he called out to the monks, "Did you hear or see anything?" The monks did not feel any difference, but Tanxun said, "There was music playing in the air, and the incense smoke was very unusual, the covenant of Huang Qian has arrived." The monks just returned to the hall and took their seats, but Tanxun had already passed away. Zhu Lin 97, 19

    In the fourth year of Daming during the reign of Empress Dowager Lu of the Song Dynasty, a statue of the Bodhisattva Samantabhadra riding a white elephant in a precious carriage was placed in the Zongxing Chan room, and a lecture was held in the temple. On the eighth day of the tenth month of that year, after the斋 (ritual) was completed and the assembly was disbanded, there were two hundred monks present. At that time, the temple was just being constructed, the emperor paid great attention to it, visiting frequently, often several times a week, the monks were diligent and orderly, and the guards were strict. On that day, the names of the monks were determined, and they had been seated for a long time when suddenly one monk appeared among them, with a graceful and dignified appearance, causing the entire hall to be startled. The斋 (ritual) host spoke with him, exchanging over a hundred words, and then he suddenly disappeared. The guests at the banquet all recognized him as a divine being. Zhu Lin 17

    宋大明年中，有寺统法师名道温，居在棱陵县。既见皇太后睿鉴冲明。圣符幽洽，涤思净场研襟至境；固以声藻震中，事灵梵表，乃创思镕斲，抽写神华模造普贤彩仪盛像，宝倾宙珍，妙尽天饰。所设讲斋，迄今月八日，嚫会有限，名簿索定，引次就席，数无盈减。转经将半，景及昆吾，忽睹异僧，预于座内，容止端严，气貌秀发，举僧瞩目，莫有识者。斋主问曰：“上人何；名？”答曰：“名慧明。”问住何寺？答云：“来自天安。”言对之间，倏然不见。○堂惊魂，遍筵肃虑，以为明祥所贲，幽应攸阐，紫山可睹，华台不远。盖闻至诚所感还景移纬，澄心所殉，发石开泉；况帝德涵运，皇功懋洽，仁洞干遐，理畅冥外，故上王盛士，克表大明之朝，劝发妙身，躬见龙飞之室。意若曰：陛下慧烛海县，明华日月。故以慧明为人名，继天兴祚式垂无疆，故以天安为寺称。神基弥远，道政方凝，九服识泰，万寓齐悦。谨列言属县以诠天休。珠林十七

    Explanation

    136

    During the reign of Emperor Tai Ming of the Song Dynasty, there was a high-ranking Buddhist monk named Dao Wen, who resided in Lengling County. Having witnessed the Empress Dowager's wise insight and profound clarity, her divine signs and harmonious mysteries, and the purification of thoughts in a clean realm and delving into the highest realms of the heart, he naturally achieved reverberating eloquence in the center and engaged in affairs of the divine and the sacred. Thus, he innovatively thought and meticulously carved, extracting divine beauty to create the splendid statue of Samantabhadra, using treasures from the universe and exquisite adornments. The lecture and fasting sessions he organized continued until the eighth day of the month, with donations limited and names registered and determined, leading participants in order to the seats, with the number remaining constant. Halfway through the sutra recitation, when the sun reached the Kunwu Mountains, a strange monk suddenly appeared among the attendees, with a dignified and composed demeanor and a radiant and noble appearance, attracting the attention of all the monks. The host asked, "What is your name, revered one?" The monk replied, "My name is Hui Ming." The host then asked where he lived, and the monk answered, "I come from Tian'an Temple." As they spoke, the monk suddenly disappeared. The hall was filled with shock, and all the guests were solemn and thoughtful, thinking it was a sign of good fortune and mysterious responses and explanations. They imagined the purple mountain could be seen and the splendid platform was not far. It is said that sincere devotion can move the stars and change the constellations, and a clear heart can move mountains and open springs. Given the imperial virtue that encompasses the universe and the widespread and harmonious imperial achievements, benevolence reaches far, and principles extend beyond the visible world, thus, the great scholars of the court can represent the era of Great Ming, encouraging the manifestation of the wonderful body and seeing the dragon's flight room personally. As if saying, "Your Majesty's wisdom illuminates the sea and counties, bright as the sun and moon. Therefore, the name Hui Ming is given to a person, continuing the heavenly mandate and enduring forever. Therefore, the temple is named Tian'an." The divine foundation extends far, and the moral governance is solidifying, with all nine regions recognizing peace and all beings being joyful. Carefully listing words for the county to explain the heavenly blessings. Seventeenth Chapter of the Pearl Forest.

    宋蒋小德，江陵人也，为兵州刺史朱循时为听事监师，少而信向，勤谨过人，循大喜之，每有法事，辄令典知其务。大明末年，得病而死，夜三更，将殓便稣活。言：有使者，称王命召之，小德随去。既至，王曰：“君精勤小心，虔奉大法，帝敕精旨，以君专至，宜速生善地；而君算犹长，故令吾特相召也。君今日将受天中快乐欣然。”小德嘉诺。王曰：“君可且还家，所欲属寄及作功德，可速之，七日复来也。”小德受言而归。

    Jiang Xiaode, a man from Jiangling, served as a supervisor under the military governor Zhu Xunshi during the Song Dynasty. Young and trustworthy, he was diligent and meticulous beyond others, which greatly pleased Zhu Xunshi. Every time there was a legal matter, Zhu Xunshi would always instruct him to handle the affairs.

    In the late Ming Dynasty, Jiang Xiaode died of illness. In the third watch of the night, he was about to be buried when he suddenly revived. He said: "There was a messenger who claimed that he was summoned by the king." Jiang Xiaode followed him. After arriving, the king said, "You are diligent and careful, and you faithfully adhere to the great law. The emperor's decree and intent have specially appointed you, so you should quickly be reborn in a good place. But your life span is still long, so I have specially summoned you. You will now receive heavenly joy and happiness." Jiang Xiaode expressed gratitude and assent. The king said, "You may return home for now. Anything you wish to entrust or perform meritorious deeds, you should do it quickly, and return in seven days." Jiang Xiaode followed the instructions and returned home.

    There is a place called Route One, where there is a small house that is extremely shabby and dilapidated. The monk "Nan Gong" encountered the new temple in front of this house. Since we are already acquainted, we exchanged greetings. The monk said, "Since I became a monk, I have never drunk alcohol, and I went to see Lan Gong, who strongly urged and pressured me to drink about one sheng. Because of this, I was summoned by the king. If I had not stayed here, I would have attained heaven, but now I am staying in this dilapidated house, and I will finally ascend three years later." Indeed on that day, Monk Nan lay down to sleep at Lan Gong's place and died that evening.     宋吴兴沈僧覆，大明末，本土饥荒，逐食至山阳；昼入屯野乞食，夜还寄寓寺舍左右。时山阳诸寺小形铜像甚众，僧覆与其乡里数人，积渐窃取，遂囊箧数四悉满焉。因将还家，共铸为钱。事既发觉，执送出都，入船便云：见人以火烧之。昼夜叫呼，自称楚毒不可堪忍，未及刑坐而死；举体皆炘裂，状如火烧。吴郡朱亨亲识僧覆，具见其事。珠林七十九广记一百十六
    　　宋尼释慧玉，长安人也，行业勤修，经戒通备。尝于长安薛尚书寺见红白光十余日中，至四月八日，六重寺沙门来游此寺，于光处得弥勒金像，高一尺余。慧玉后南渡樊郢，住江陵灵收寺。元嘉十四年十月夜，见寺东树有紫光烂起，晖映一林，以告同学妙光等，而悉弗之见也。二十余日，玉常见焉。后寺主释法弘将于树下营筑禅基，仰首条闲得金坐像，亦高尺许也。珠林十六

    139

    During the reign of Emperor Gong, Shen Sengfu from Wu Prefecture, faced with famine in his hometown, went to Shan Yang in search of food. During the day, he would enter the fields to beg for food, and at night, he would stay near the temple. At that time, there were many small copper statues in the temples of Shan Yang. Shen Sengfu and several people from his hometown gradually stole these statues, eventually filling several bags and chests. They then took them back home and melted them down to make coins. When the theft was discovered, they were arrested and sent to the capital. On the boat, Shen Sengfu claimed to see someone burning him with fire. He screamed day and night, claiming that the pain was unbearable, and died before the official punishment could be carried out. His entire body burst open, as if burned. Zhu Hen from Wu Prefecture, who knew Shen Sengfu personally, witnessed the entire event. (From Zhu Lin 79 and Guang Ji 116)

    Nun Hui Yu, from Chang'an, was a diligent practitioner of the Dharma, well-versed in scriptures and precepts. One day, while at Xue Shangshu Temple in Chang'an, she saw red and white lights for over ten days. On the eighth day of the fourth month, a monk from Liu Chong Temple came to visit and found a golden statue of Maitreya, about a foot tall, where the light was. Hui Yu later moved south to Jiangling and stayed at Ling Shou Temple. In the fourteenth year of the Yuangang era, on a night in October, she saw a brilliant purple light rise from a tree in the temple grounds, illuminating the entire grove. She told her fellow monk Miao Guang about it, but he could not see it. Over the next twenty days, Hui Yu continued to see the light. Later, the temple master Fa Hong was building a meditation base under the tree when he found a golden seated statue, also about a foot tall. (From Zhu Lin 16)

    宋费崇先者，吴兴人也，少颇信法，至三十际，精勤弥至。泰始三年，受菩萨戒，寄斋于谢惠远家，二十四日，昼夜不懈。每听经，常以鹊尾香炉置膝前。初学记二十五引云费崇先少信佛常以鹊尾香炉置膝前初斋三夕，见一人容服不凡，迳来举炉将去；崇先视膝前炉犹在其处，更详视此人，见提去甚分明，崇先方悟是神异。自惟衣裳新濯，了无不净，唯坐侧有唾壶；既使去壶，即复见此人还炉坐前，未至席顷犹见两炉，既即合为一，然则此神人所提者，盖炉影乎。崇先又当闻人说：福远寺有僧钦尼精勤得道，欣然愿见，未及得往，属意甚至。尝斋于他家，夜三更中，忽见一尼，容仪端严着赭布袈娑，正立斋席之前，食顷而灭。及崇先后觐此尼，色貌被服，即窗前所睹者也。珠林二十四

    Explanation

    140

    A Man Named Fei Chongxian of Song

    Mr. Fei Chongxian of Song was from Wu County. In his youth, he had some faith in the Dharma, and by the age of thirty, his diligence and devotion became even more intense. In the third year of Tai Shi, he received the Bodhisattva precepts and stayed for meditation at the home of Xie Huaiyuan for twenty-four days, without rest day or night. Every time he listened to the scriptures, he would place a magpie-tail incense burner on his knees. According to the Initial Learning Record (卷二十五), it is recorded that Fei Chongxian, in his youth, believed in the Buddha and often placed a magpie-tail incense burner on his knees during his initial meditation retreat. On the third night of his retreat, he saw a person of extraordinary appearance and attire who came straight to take the incense burner away. Chongxian looked at the incense burner on his knees and found it still there. He looked more closely at the person and saw them take the incense burner away clearly. Chongxian then realized it was a supernatural phenomenon. He thought to himself that his clothes had just been washed and were completely clean, except for the spittoon near him. After he removed the spittoon, he saw the person return with the incense burner to sit in front of him. For a short while he still saw two incense burners, but then they merged into one. Thus, what the divine person took away was probably just a shadow of the incense burner.

    Chongxian also heard from others that there was a nun named Qinni at Fuyuan Temple who was diligent and had attained enlightenment. He was delighted to see her, but before he could go, he had already developed a strong attachment. Once, while staying for meditation at another's home, in the middle of the third watch of the night, he suddenly saw a nun with dignified appearance, wearing a dark red robe, standing upright in front of the meditation hall. She vanished after a meal's worth of time. When Chongxian later met this nun, her appearance and attire were exactly as he had seen from the window. This account is found in the Jewel Forest (卷二十四).

    东海何敬叔，少而奉佛，至泰始中，随湘州刺史刘韬珠林十四作刘韫监营浦县。敬叔时遇有旃檀，制以为像，像将就而未有光材；敬叔意愿甚勤，而营索无处，凭几微睡，见一沙门纳衣杖锡来，上五字依广记引补语敬叔云：“县后何家有一桐盾，甚堪像光，其人极惜之，苦求可得也。”敬叔寤，问县后，果有何家。因求买盾，何氏云：“实有此盾，甚爱惜之，明府何以得知？”敬叔具说所梦，何氏惊嘉，奉以制光。御览三百五十七广记二百七十六珠林十四云后为相府直省中夜梦像云鼠啮吾足清旦疾归视像果然矣

    141

    He Jingshu from the eastern sea region was devoted to Buddhism from a young age. During the reign of Emperor Wen (泰始 period), he followed the governor of Xiang Prefecture, Liu Yun (刘韫), in supervising Yingpu County. At the time, He Jingshu obtained some sandalwood and carved it into a statue. The statue was nearly complete, but it lacked the material for the halo. He Jingshu was very eager to complete the statue, but despite his efforts, he could not find the necessary material. While leaning against a table and dozing off, he saw a monk in a simple robe and holding a staff and alms bowl come to him. The monk said, "There is a paulownia shield in the house of the He family after the county, which is very suitable for the halo of the statue. The owner values it greatly, but it can be obtained with great effort." He Jingshu awoke and asked about the He family after the county, and indeed, there was such a family. He then requested to buy the shield. The He family said, "We do have this shield, and we value it greatly. How did you know about it, Your Excellency?" He Jingshu explained his dream, and the He family was amazed and impressed. They offered the shield to help complete the halo of the statue. Later, when He Jingshu served in the office of the prime minister, he had a dream in the middle of the night where the statue said, "A mouse is biting my foot." In the morning, he hurriedly returned to check on the statue, and indeed, a mouse was biting its foot.

    宋袁炳，字叔焕，陈郡人也。泰始末为临湘令。亡后积年，友人司马逊于将晓闲如梦见炳来，陈叙阔别，讯问安否，既而谓逊曰：“吾等平生立意置论，常言生为驰役，死为休息，今日始知，广记引有知字定不然矣。恒患在世有人，务驰求金币，共相赠遗，幽途此事，亦复如之。”逊问：罪福应报，定实如何？炳曰：“如我旧见，与经教所说，不尽符同，将是圣人抑引之谈耳！如今所见，善恶大科，略不异也。然杀生故最为重，禁慎不可犯也。

    142

    After many years following his death, Yuan Bing, a man from Chen County, served as the magistrate of Linxiang at the end of the Tai Shi era. His friend Sima Xun, in a dream-like state just before dawn, saw Yuan Bing appear to him. Yuan Bing recounted their long separation and inquired about his well-being. He then said, "Throughout our lives, we often discussed and held the view that life is a race, while death is rest. Now I know for the first time that the extensive records and quotations containing the word 'know' are certainly not correct. I was always troubled by people in the world who are busy chasing after money and gold, exchanging gifts with each other. In the afterlife, this situation is also the same."

    Sima Xun asked, "Are the rewards and punishments for sins and virtues truly determined?" Yuan Bing replied, "As I saw it before, it does not fully agree with what is said in the scriptures. This is probably the sage's way of guiding and restraining. The general categories of good and evil are not very different. However, killing living beings is the most serious, and it must be strictly forbidden and not violated."

    ”逊曰：卿此征相示，良不可言，当以语白尚书也。”炳曰：“甚善，亦请卿敬情尚书。”时司空简穆王公广记引作时司空王僧虔为吏部尚书，炳逊并其游宾，故及之。往返可数百语，辞去，逊曰：“阔别之久，恒思叙集，相值甚难，何不小住？”炳曰：“止暂来耳！不可得久留。且此辈语亦不容得委悉。”于是而去。初炳来闇夜，逊亦了不觉所以而明得睹见炳，既去，逊下床送之，始蹑屐而还闇，见炳脚间有光可尺许，示得照其两足，余地犹皆闇云。珠林二十一广记三百二十六

    "Xun said, 'Your sign that you have shown me is truly difficult to put into words; you should inform the Shangshu (Minister of Works).' At that time, the high-ranking official Jianmu Wang Gong (as recorded in Guangji), or Wang Sengqian as the Guangji states, was the Shangshu of the Ministry of Personnel, and Bing and Xun were among his honored guests, hence this conversation took place. Initially, when Bing arrived in the darkness, Xun did not know why but was able to see clearly.     宋沙门道志者，北多宝僧也，尝为众僧，为众二字依广记引补令知殿塔，自窃帐盖等宝饰，所取甚众。后遂偷像眉间珠相，既而开穿垣壁，若外盗者，故僧众不能觉也。积旬余而得病，便见异人以戈矛刺之，时来时去，来辄惊噭，应声流血。初犹日中一两如此，其后疾甚，刺者稍数，伤痍遍体，呻呼不能绝声。同寺僧众，颇疑其有罪，欲为忏谢，始问犹讳而不言，将尽二三日，乃具自陈列，泣涕请救，曰：“吾愚悖不通，谓无幽途，失意作罪，招此殃酷，生受楚拷，死萦刀镬，已糜之身，唯垂哀恕。

    Explanation

    144

    A monk named Daozhi from the Song dynasty, who was from the Northern Dabao temple, once served as a caretaker for the temple and pagoda. He secretly stole the canopy and other precious decorations, taking a great deal of them. Later, he stole the pearl from the Buddha statue's eyebrow. He then dug through the walls, as if it were an external thief, so the monks did not notice. After more than ten days, he fell ill and saw a strange person stabbing him with spears. The person came and went at times, and whenever they came, he would scream and blood would flow in response. At first, this happened once or twice a day, but later his illness worsened, and the number of stabbings increased, causing wounds all over his body. He moaned and could not stop. The monks of the same temple suspected he had committed a crime and wanted to perform a repentance ceremony. At first, he was still reluctant to speak, but as he was nearing death, two or three days later, he fully confessed and wept, begging for mercy. He said, "I am foolish and ignorant, believing there was no afterlife. Acting out of anger, I committed a sin, bringing this suffering upon myself. I suffer torture in life and am tormented in death. My ruined body, I only beg for pity and forgiveness."

    145

    今无复余物，唯衣被毡履，或足充一会，并烦请愿具为，忏悔。昔偷像相珠有二枚，一枚已属妪人，不可复得，一以质钱，在陈照家，今可赎取。”道志既死，诸僧合集赎得相珠，并设斋忏，初，工人复相珠时，展转迥趣，终不安合，众僧复为礼拜烧香，乃得着焉。年余而同学等于昏夜闲闻空中有语，详听即道志声也。自说云：自死以来，备萦痛毒，方累年劫，未有出期；赖蒙众僧，哀怜救护，赎像相珠，故于苦酷之中，时有闲息。感恩罔已，故暂来称谢，言此而已。闻其语时，腥腐臭气，苦痛难过，言终久久，臭乃稍歇。此事在泰始末年，其寺好事者，已具条记。珠林七十九广记一百十六

    Explanation

    145

    Now, using the research and context we gathered above, produce a final, polished translation of the source text.

    Your goal is to deliver a final English translation that is both faithful to the original Classical Chinese and reads naturally in English. Apply the insights from the pre-drafting research directly — handle idiomatic expressions, cultural allusions, syntactic ambiguities, and proper nouns as you planned.

    Here are 5 examples showing the expected translation quality and style:

    Example 1

    Source: 爰及農商工賈，廝役奴隸，釣魚屠肉，飯牛牧羊，皆有先達，可為師表，博學求之，無不利於事也。

    Translation: As for farmers, merchants, artisans, and traders, as well as servants, laborers, and slaves, those engaged in fishing and butchering, feeding oxen and herding sheep—all have predecessors who can serve as role models. By seeking knowledge broadly from them, nothing is unhelpful in one's endeavors.

    Example 2

    Source: 兩頭四臂女

    靈帝時，洛陽女子生時兩頭四臂。

    Translation: A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    Example 3

    Source: 凡為文章，猶乘騏驥，雖有逸氣，當以銜勒制之，勿使流亂軌躅，放意填坑岸也。

    Translation: In all writing, it is like riding a swift steed — though it may possess a wild and unrestrained spirit, one must control it with bit and bridle, and must not let it run wild, straying from the proper path or indulging in aimless wanderings.

    Example 4

    Source: 自古明王聖帝，猶須勤學，況凡庶乎！此事遍於經史，吾亦不能鄭重，聊舉近世切要，以啟寤汝耳。

    Translation: From ancient times, wise kings and sage emperors still required diligent study; how much more so, then, for common people! This matter is found throughout the classics and histories. I cannot elaborate further, but I will briefly mention a few essential points of recent times in order to enlighten you.

    Example 5

    Translation: As for writings, their origin lies in the Five Classics: edicts, memorials, and military proclamations arise from the Shujing (Book of Documents); expository and argumentative writings arise from the Yijing (Book of Changes); songs, odes, and praises arise from the Shijing (Book of Poetry); ritual sacrifices, mourning, and elegies arise from the Liji (Book of Rites); memorials, admonitions, and inscriptions arise from the Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn Annals). Court regulations, military oaths and decrees, the proclamation of benevolence and righteousness, the elucidation of virtue and merit, governing the people and establishing the state—all are indispensable. As for cultivating the mind and spirit, offering gentle admonition in a relaxed manner, and savoring the flavor of such writings, these too are pleasant pursuits. When one has spare energy, then one may study them.

    宋陈秀远者，颍川人也，尝为湘州西曹，客居临湘县。少信奉三宝，年过耳顺，笃业不衰。宋元徽二年，七月中，于昏夕闲，闲卧未寝，叹念万品死生，流转无定，自惟已身，将从何来，一心祈念，冀通感梦。时夕结阴，室无灯烛，有顷，见枕边如萤火者，冏然明照，流飞而去。俄而一室尽明，爰至空中，有如朝昼。秀远遽起坐，合掌端念。顷，见中宁四五丈上，有一桥阁焉，又阑槛朱彩，立于空中，秀远了不觉升动之时，而已自见平坐桥侧。见桥上士女，往返填衢，衣服妆束，不异世人。末有一妪，年可三十许，上着青袄，下服白布裳，行至秀远左边而立；有顷，复有一妇人，通体衣白布，为偏环髻，手持华香，当前而立。语秀远曰：“汝欲睹前身，即我是也，以此华供养佛故，故得转身作汝。”回指白妪曰：“此即复是我先身也。”言毕而去，去后桥亦渐隐。秀远忽然不觉还下之时，光亦寻灭也。珠林三十二广记一百十四

    Cen Xiu Yuan, a native of Yen-chuan, once served as the Western Censor of Xiangzhou and resided as a guest in Linxiang County. In his youth, he revered the Three Jewels of Buddhism, and even after reaching the age of sixty, he remained steadfast in his occupation. In the second year of the Yuexiu era of the Song Dynasty, during the seventh month, on an evening when he was lying down without sleeping, he reflected on the impermanence of life and death, pondering where he had come from. With a focused mind, he prayed, hoping for a dream that would convey a message. That evening was overcast, and the room was dark without any lighting. After a while, he saw a light like a firefly beside his pillow, shining brightly and then flying away. Soon, the entire room was illuminated, and the light reached the sky, as if it were daytime. Cen Xiu Yuan quickly sat up, folded his hands, and meditated. After a while, he saw a bridge and a pavilion about ten to fifteen feet above him, with red decorations standing in the sky. He did not realize how he was lifted, but he found himself sitting on the side of the bridge. He saw men and women on the bridge, coming and going, their clothing and appearance no different from ordinary people. An old woman, about thirty years old, appeared, wearing a green coat and a white cloth skirt, and stood to the left of Cen Xiu Yuan. After a while, another woman appeared, dressed entirely in white cloth, with a partial ring hairstyle, holding flowers and incense, and stood in front of him. She said to Cen Xiu Yuan, "If you want to see your previous life, I am it. Because I offered these flowers to the Buddha, I was reborn as you." She then pointed to the white-clad old woman and said, "This is also my previous life." After speaking, she left, and the bridge gradually disappeared. Cen Xiu Yuan suddenly realized he was back on the ground, and the light also disappeared. Jade Forest volume 32, Record of the Broadly Recorded volume 114.

    A Monk Named Zhi Da from the Song Dynasty

    Zhi Da was a monk from the Suo Temple in Yizhou (present-day Chengdu, Sichuan). His behavior was somewhat conventional, but he was skilled in reciting scriptures and chants. At the age of twenty-three, in the third month of the Yuangui era of the Song dynasty (475 AD), he fell ill and died. His body remained warm, delaying the burial. After two days, he began to show signs of recovery. On the third day morning, he could speak and see again. He recounted his experience: when he first became ill, he saw two people dressed in yellow cloth trousers and jackets. One stood outside the door, and the other came directly to the bedside. The person said, "Reverend, you should leave; get off the bed." Zhi Da replied, "I am weak and frail; I cannot travel." The person then said, "You can ride in a carriage." As soon as he spoke, the carriage arrived. Zhi Da got into it, and his consciousness became unclear. He no longer saw his family's house or the carriage. Looking around, he only saw a desolate wilderness with difficult paths. The path showed him to climb and walk without rest. He reached a red gate with very ornate walls and doors. Zhi Da entered the hall.

    In the hall, there was a noble person wearing a red cap and headband, sitting arrogantly on the bed with a severe and distant appearance, having a very dignified and imposing presence. About a hundred guards stood straight and orderly on either side, all holding red-handled swords. The noble person saw the monk and then adopted a serious expression, saying, "Why should a monk have many faults?" The monk replied, "Since gaining consciousness, I do not remember committing any sins." The noble person asked, "Have you neglected the recitation of the precepts?" The monk answered, "When I first received the full ordination, I indeed regularly recited them. In recent times, I have been attending sermons and reciting scriptures, thus there have been occasional lapses in reciting the precepts." The noble person said, "You may recite the scriptures instead." The monk then recited the Lotus Sutra three times and stopped. The noble person instructed those in charge, "You may send him to a bad place, but do not make it too harsh." Two people led the monk away, traveling for dozens of miles, and gradually heard a loud and chaotic noise, while the road ahead became darker.

    Translation
    Next, he reached a gate, towering several dozen feet high, very dark and black, indicating it was made of iron. The wall was also similar in appearance. Da thought to himself: "The scriptures speak of hell, this must be it." He became greatly terrified. He regretted not cultivating virtue and good deeds in his lifetime. As he entered the gate, the noise grew louder. After a while, upon quiet listening, he realized it was the sound of people calling out. Inside the gate, it grew darker, and he could no longer see anything. The firelight flickered on and off. He saw several people bound and being led forward, behind them were several people holding something, and blood flowed like a spring. One of them was Da's aunt. They saw each other and wanted to speak, but someone dragged him away so quickly that he had no time to speak. After entering the gate for about two hundred steps, he saw an object shaped like a grain silo, about ten feet tall. Two people grabbed Da and threw him onto the silo. Inside the silo was fire, which burned Da's body. Half of his body was burned to a crisp, and the pain was unbearable. He fell from the silo to the ground and fainted for a long time. Two people took Da away again.

    They saw more than ten iron cauldrons, all boiling criminals within them. The victims, submerged in the boiling liquid, rose and sank with the waves of the heat.     151

    In the Song Dynasty, there was a man named Yuan Kuo, whose courtesy name was Sishu, and he was from Chen Prefecture. During the reign of Emperor Yuan of Song (472-477), he served as the magistrate of Wu Prefecture. He fell ill for a short time and appeared to be dead, but his breath was not completely gone. All the funeral preparations were ready, and they waited until the preparations were complete before embalming him. After three days, he was able to move and blink. He recounted that a messenger came and called him, and Kuo followed him. Upon arrival, they saw a large city with high and orderly towers and battlements, and grand and beautiful stairs and gates. Once he was invited to enter, the host sat facing south, with a solemn and majestic appearance adorned with a crown. A person with a knife pointed at Kuo to sit, and once seated, warm and cool dishes were served, including wine, roasted meat, fruits, zongzi (sticky rice dumplings), pickled vegetables, and other dishes. Kuo tried all the food, which had various types and flavors, no different from what is found in the world. After several rounds of wine, the host said to Kuo, "My position is humble and unfortunate, lacking in duties. Because of your sharp talent, I wish to invite you. Can you consider it?" Kuo understood that this was a reference to the afterlife and firmly declined, saying, "My humble position is not suitable. My family is poor and has few members, and my brothers are scattered in both public and private life. I beg for your mercy and release." The host replied, "You are declining because the afterlife is different from the world. Here, there are many honors and resources, and my body and clothing are well cared for, which will be better than your hard work in the world. I very much desire to work together, and I hope you will lower your expectations to meet my expectations." Kuo again firmly declined, saying, "My children are still young, and if I accept this role, there will be no one to care for them. The affection between father and son is something that can be pitied." Kuo then wept and bowed. The host said, "Your refusal is so sincere, how can I force you? If I cannot persuade you, I deeply regret it."

    ”就案上取一卷文书拘黵之。既而廓谢恩辞归，主人曰：“君不欲定省先亡乎？”乃遣人将廓行，经历寺署甚众，末得一垣，城门楣并，盖囹圄也。将廓入中，斜趣一隅，有诸屋宇，骈填衔接，而甚陋弊。次有一屋，见其所生母羊氏在此屋中，容服不佳，甚异平生，见廓惊喜。户边有一人，身面伤痍，形类甚异，呼廓语，廓惊问其谁？羊氏谓廓曰：“此王夫人，汝不识耶？”王夫人曰：“吾在世时，不信报应，虽复无甚余罪，正坐鞭挞婢仆过苦，故受此罚。亡来楚毒，殆无暂休，今特少时宽隙耳。前唤汝姊来，望以自代，竟无所益，徒为忧聚。”言毕涕泗，王夫人即廓嫡母也。廓姊时亦在其侧。有顷，使人复将廓去，经涉巷陌，闾里整顿，似是民居。末有一宅竹篱茅屋，见父披被着巾，?案而坐。廓入门，父扬手遣廓曰：“汝即蒙罢，可速归去，不须来也。廓跪辞而归，使人送廓至家而去。廓今太子洗马是也。”珠林五十二

    From the table, a document was taken and used to detain someone. Afterward, Kuò expressed gratitude and declined to return. They finally reached a wall, with the city gate and lintel aligned, which was a prison. Kuò was led inside and moved to a corner, where there were several buildings closely packed and connected, but in poor condition. In one of these buildings, Kuò saw his biological mother, Yang Shi, who was dressed poorly and looked very different from her usual self. She was surprised and delighted to see Kuò. Near the door, there was a person with visible injuries and a strange appearance who called out to Kuò. Kuò was startled and asked who she was. Yang Shi said to Kuò, "This is Wang's wife, do you not recognize her?" Wang's wife said, "When I was alive, I did not believe in retribution. Although I had no major sins, I was punished for excessively whipping my servants and maids. Since my death, I have suffered greatly, almost without a moment's rest. Now, I am only experiencing a brief respite. I previously called your sister to come, hoping she would take my place, but it was of no benefit and only caused more worry." She finished speaking and wept. Wang's wife was Kuò's stepmother. At that time, Kuò's sister was also present. After a while, the person who had led Kuò away brought him back, passing through streets and alleys that seemed to be residential areas. The person who had led him was sent back home. Kuò is now a high-ranking official in the imperial court, known as the Imperial Horse Washer. This is recorded in the "Jade Forest, Chapter Fifty-Two."

    宋韩徽者，未详何许人也，居于支江，其叔幼宗，宋末为湘州府中兵。升明元年，荆州刺史沈攸之举兵东下，湘府长史庾佩玉阻甲自守，未知所赴；以幼宗猜贰，杀之，戮及妻孥，徽以兄子系于郡狱，铁木竟体，钳梏甚严，须考毕情党，将悉诛灭。徽惶迫无计，待斯而已。徽本尝事佛，颇讽读观世音经，于是昼夜诵经至数百遍。方昼，而锁忽自鸣，若烧炮石瓦爆吒之声，已而视其锁，鏙然自解。徽惧狱司谓其解截，遽呼告之，吏虽惊异，而犹更钉鍱。徽如常讽诵，又经一日，锁复鸣解，状如初时。吏乃具告佩玉，玉取锁详视，服其通感，即免释之。徽今尚在，勤业殊至。珠林二十七

    Explanation

    153

    Han Hui of the Song Dynasty, whose origins are unknown, lived in Zhijiang. His uncle, Youzong, served as a military officer in the government of Xiang Prefecture at the end of the Southern Song Dynasty. In the first year of the Shengming era, Governor Shen Youzhi of Jing Prefecture led an army eastward. Yu Peiyu, the chief secretary of Xiang Prefecture, defended himself with armor but did not know whom to follow. Suspecting disloyalty from Youzong, he had him executed along with his wife and children. Han Hui, being Youzong's nephew, was imprisoned in the prefectural jail, where he was bound with iron and wood, his shackles being very tight and severe. They intended to interrogate his associates and kill all of them. Han Hui was in a state of panic and had no plan; there was nothing else to do but wait. Han Hui had previously been a Buddhist and often recited the Guanshiyin Jing. He recited the scripture day and night, hundreds of times. One day, the lock on his cell suddenly made a noise, like the sound of exploding stones or tiles when they are burned. When he looked at the lock, it opened by itself. Han Hui was afraid that the jailer would think he had tampered with the lock, so he quickly called out to explain. The official was surprised but still re-fastened the shackles. Han Hui continued to recite the scripture as usual, and after another day, the lock again made a noise and opened by itself, just as it had before. The official then reported everything to Yu Peiyu. Yu Peiyu took the lock and examined it carefully, convinced by the supernatural phenomenon, and immediately released Han Hui. Han Hui is still alive today, diligently pursuing his career. This story is recorded in the Zhu Lin, volume 27.

    宋释慧严京师东安寺僧也，理思该畅，见器道俗。尝嫌大涅槃经文字繁多，遂加刊削，就成数卷，写两三通，以示同好。因寝寤之际，忽见一人，身长二丈余，形气伟壮，谓之曰：“涅槃尊经，众藏之宗，何得以君璅思，轻加斟酌？”严怅然不释，犹以发意，苟觅多知明夕将卧，复见昨人，甚有怒色，谓曰：“过而知改，是谓非过；昨故相告，犹不己乎？此经既无行理，且君祸亦将及。”严惊觉失措，未及申旦，便驰信求还，悉烧除之。尘外精舍释道俨具所谙闻也。珠林十八

    Explanation

    154

    Master Huaiyan, a monk at Dong'an Temple in the capital city, was known for his comprehensive and smooth reasoning, esteemed by both monastics and laypeople. He once found the Mahāparinirvāṇa Sūtra to be verbose and decided to edit it, producing several volumes and copying them two or three times to show to like-minded people. One night, while sleeping, he suddenly saw a figure over two zhang tall (approximately 6.6 meters), who appeared physically imposing and strong. The figure told him, "The Mahāparinirvāṇa Sūtra is the revered scripture and the root of all collections. How can you lightly edit it with your trivial thoughts?" Master Huaiyan felt disappointed but still held onto his intention to edit the text, hoping to seek more knowledge. The next night, as he was about to sleep, he saw the same figure again, who appeared with an angry expression and said, "To recognize and correct mistakes is not a mistake; I warned you yesterday, but you still haven't stopped? This scripture has no reason to be practiced, and your misfortune will also come to you." Startled awake and at a loss, before dawn, he sent a message to return the edited text and burned it all. The monk from the hermitage outside the world, Master Daoyan, has heard of this incident. Jade Forest, Chapter Eighteen.

    155

    宋罗玙妻费氏者，宁蜀人，父悦宋宁州刺史。费少而敬信，诵法华经，数年勤至不倦，后忽得病，苦心痛守命，阖门遑惧，属纩待时。费氏心念：我诵经勤苦，宜有善佑，庶不于此，遂致死也。既而睡卧，食顷，如寤如梦见佛于窗中，授手以摩其心，应时都愈。一堂男女婢仆，悉睹金光，亦闻香气。玙从妹即琰外族曾祖尚书中兵郎费愔之夫人也，于时省疾床前，亦具闻见。于是大兴信悟，虔戒至终，每以此瑞进化子侄焉。珠林九十五广记一百九

    Explanation

    155

    A Woman Named Fei, the Wife of Luo Yu of Song

    Fei was a native of Ningzhou in the region of Shu, and her father was the governor of Ningzhou during the Song dynasty. From a young age, Fei was respectful and devout, reciting the Lotus Sutra with diligence and without tiring for many years. Later, she suddenly fell ill, suffering from heart pain and clinging to life. Her entire family was in great fear, waiting anxiously for her to pass away. Fei thought to herself, "I have recited the scriptures diligently; I should be protected by good fortune. Perhaps not here, leading to death." Afterward, she fell asleep, after a meal, as if waking up or dreaming. She saw a Buddha at the window, who placed his hand on her heart, and she was immediately cured. All the men, women, maids, and servants in the house saw golden light and smelled a fragrant aroma.

    Yu's cousin, who was the wife of Fei Yin, a former military official and great-grandson of Yu's uncle, visited Fei at her bedside at that time and also witnessed everything. Thus, she greatly strengthened her faith and enlightenment, remained devout until the end, and often used this miracle to inspire her nephews and nieces. This story is recorded in the Zhu Lin (Jade Forest) volume 95 and Guangji (Record of Miracles) volume 19.

    156

    宋彭子乔者，益阳县人也，任本郡主簿，事太守沈文龙。建元元年，以罪被系，子乔，少年，尝经出家，末虽还俗，犹常诵习观世音经。时文龙盛怒，防械稍急，必欲杀之。子乔忧惧，无复余计，唯至诚诵经至百余遍。疲而昼寝，时同系者有十许人，亦俱睡卧。有湘西县吏杜道策亦系在狱，乍寐乍寤，不甚得熟。忽有双白鹤集子乔屏风上，有顷，一鹤下至子乔边，时复觉如美丽人形而已。道策起，见子乔双械脱在脚外，而械雍犹在焉。道策惊视始毕，子乔亦寤，共视械咨嗟。问子乔：有所梦不？乔曰：“不梦，”道策如向所见说之。子乔虽知必已，尚虑狱家疑其欲叛，乃解脱械雍更着。经四五日而蒙释放。琰族兄琏，亲识子乔及道策，闻二人说皆同如此。珠林二十七

    Explanation

    156

    Cao Ziqiao, a native of Yiyang County, served as the chief clerk in his own prefecture under Prefect Shen Wenlong. In the first year of the Jianyuan era, he was imprisoned due to a crime. Cao Ziqiao was a young man who had once been a monk. Although he eventually returned to lay life, he still regularly recited the Guanyin Sutra. At the time, Prefect Shen Wenlong was extremely angry, and the guards and restraints were becoming increasingly harsh, determined to kill him. Cao Ziqiao was filled with fear and had no other options, so he sincerely recited the sutra more than a hundred times. He became tired and took a nap during the day. At the same time, there were about ten other prisoners who were also sleeping.

    Suddenly, two white cranes gathered on Cao Ziqiao's screen. After a while, one of the cranes flew down to Cao Ziqiao's side. Sometimes he felt as if it was a beautiful human form. Du Daoce, a fellow prisoner, got up and saw that Cao Ziqiao's restraints were off his feet, but the restraints on his wrists were still there. Du Daoce was amazed and watched in disbelief. Cao Ziqiao also woke up, and they both looked at the restraints in amazement. Someone asked Cao Ziqiao if he had dreamed anything. Cao Ziqiao said, "I didn't dream." Du Daoce then told him about what he had seen.

    Cao Ziqiao knew that the restraints would be removed, but he still worried that the guards might suspect him of trying to escape. So, he took off the wrist restraints and put them back on. After four or five days, he was released. Yan's elder brother Lian, who knew both Cao Ziqiao and Du Daoce, heard their stories and found them to be the same. This account is recorded in the 27th chapter of the Jiu Ling (Nine Records).

    宋董青建者，不知何许人，父字贤明，建元初为越骑校尉。初，建母宗氏孕建时，梦有人语云：“尔必生男，体上当有青志，可名为青建。”及生如言，即名焉。有容止，美言笑，性理宽和，家人未尝睹其愠色，见者咸异之。至年十四，而州迎主簿。建元初，皇储镇樊汉，为水曹参军。二年七月十六日，寝疾，自云：必不振济。至十八日临尽，起坐谓母曰：“罪尽福至，缘累永绝；愿母自割，不须忧念。”因七声大哭，声尽而绝。

    Explanation

    157

    Dong Qingjian of the Song Dynasty, whose origins are unknown, had a father named Xianming. In the first year of Jianyuan, he served as the Inspector General of Cavalry. Initially, when Jian's mother, Lady Zong, was pregnant with him, she had a dream in which someone told her, "You will give birth to a boy, and there will be a blue mark on his body. He can be named Qingjian." Upon his birth, just as foretold, he was named Qingjian. He had a dignified appearance and demeanor, with graceful speech and laughter. His nature was broad and harmonious, and family members never saw him angry. Those who met him were all surprised by him. By the age of fourteen, he was appointed as a county clerk by the state. In the first year of Jianyuan, the crown prince governed Fan and Han, and Qingjian served as a water administration officer. On the sixteenth day of the seventh month in the second year, he fell ill and, on his own, said that he would not recover. On the eighteenth day, as he was nearing death, he stood up and said to his mother, "All sins are exhausted, and blessings have arrived; all karmic ties are forever severed. May Mother cut herself off, do not worry or think about it." He then cried seven times in loud sobs, and cried until he was exhausted and died.

    将殡丧斋前，其夜灵语云：“生死道乖，勿安斋前，自当有造像道人来迎丧者。”明日，果有道人来，名昙顺，即依灵语，向昙顺说之。昙顺曰：“贫道住在南林寺，造丈八像垂成，贤子乃有此感应。寺西有少空地，可得安葬也。”遂葬寺边。三日，其母将亲表十许人，墓所致祭，于墓东见建如生，云：“愿母割哀还去，建今还在寺住，”母即止哭而还，举家菜食长斋。至闰月十一日。贤明梦见建云：“愿父暂出东斋。”贤明便香汤自浴斋，出东斋。至十四夜，于眠中闻建唤声，惊起，建在斋前，如生时。父问：“汝住在何处？”建云：“从亡来住在练神宫中，满百日当得生忉利天。

    The coffin was carried to the front of the斋, and that night, a spirit's message was heard: "The ways of life and death are different; do not place the coffin in front of the斋.     建不忍见父母兄弟哭泣伤恸，三七日礼诸佛菩萨请四天王，故得暂还。愿父母从今以后，勿复啼哭祭祀。阿母已发愿求见建，母不久当命终，即共建同生一处。父寿可得七十三，命终之后，当三年受罪报，勤苦行道，可得免脱。”问曰：汝从夜中来，那得有光明？”建曰：“今与菩萨诸天共下，此其身光耳！”又问云：“汝天上识谁？”建曰：“见王车骑张吴兴外祖宗西河。”建曰：“非但此一门中生，从四十七年以来，至今七死也生，已得四道果。先发七愿，愿生人闲，故历生死，从今永毕，得离七苦。建临尽时，见七处生死，所以大哭者，与七家分别也。

    Explanation

    159

    Jian could not bear to see his parents and siblings crying and grieving deeply. After observing the traditional mourning period of 21 days and offering rites to the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas and inviting the Four Heavenly Kings, he was able to return briefly. He wished that his parents would stop crying and performing rituals from now on. Jian's mother had made a vow to see him, and she would soon pass away. Then, Jian and his mother would be reborn together in the same place. Jian's father could live to be seventy-three years old. After his death, he would suffer for three years, but by diligently practicing the path, he could be freed. Jian was asked, "How can there be light when you come from the night?" Jian replied, "I come down with the Bodhisattvas and heavenly beings, and this is just their body's light!" He was then asked, "Do you recognize anyone in heaven?" Jian said, "I saw my maternal grandfather, Zhang Wuxing from Xihé, who held the title of Wang Cheqi." Jian explained, "Not only in this family, but since forty-seven years ago, until now, I have been reborn seven times, and I have already attained the four fruits of the path. I first made seven vows, wishing to be born among humans, and therefore, I have experienced rebirth. From now on, it is finished, and I can be freed from the seven sufferings. When Jian faced his end, he saw seven places of rebirth and death, which is why he cried so bitterly, as he was saying goodbye to seven different families."

    ”问云：“汝昔生谁家？”建曰：“生江吏部，羊广州，张吴兴，王车骑，萧吴兴，梁给事，董越骑等家。唯此间生十七年，余处止五三年耳。目今以后，毒疠岁多，宜勤修功德。建见世人死，多堕三涂，生天者少；勤精进，可得免度，发愿生天，亦得相见，行脱差异，无相值期。”又问云：“汝母忧忆汝，垂死，可令见汝不？”建曰：不须相见，益怀煎苦耳！耶但依向言说之。诸天已去，不容久住。”惨有悲色，忽然不见。去后竹林左右，犹有香气，家人亦并闻余香焉。建云所生七家；江湛羊希张永王玄谟萧惠明梁季父也。贤明遂以出家，名法藏也。珠林五十二

    160

    The question was asked: "Who were your families in the past?" Jian replied: "I was born into the families of Jiang (the Ministry of Personnel), Yang (of Guangzhou), Zhang (of Wu Xing), Wang (the Chariot Commander), Xiao (of Wu Xing), Liang (the Counselor to the Emperor), and Dong (the Elite Cavalry Commander). I lived in this place for seventeen years, and in the others for only five or three years each. From now on, there will be many diseases and epidemics, so it is advisable to diligently cultivate virtue and merit. Jian has seen that when people die, most fall into the three evil realms, and few are reborn in heaven; by diligently practicing and making vows to be reborn in heaven, one can also meet again, but due to the differences in our paths, we cannot meet at the same time." The question was then asked: "Your mother is dying of grief and longing for you. Can she see you?" Jian said: "It is not necessary to see her, as it would only cause her more distress! She should follow my previous advice. The gods have already departed, and I cannot stay long." With a sad expression, Jian suddenly disappeared. After he left, the bamboo grove still had a lingering fragrance, and the family members also smelled the remaining scent. Jian mentioned seven families: Jiang Zhan, Yang Xi, Zhang Yong, Wang Xuanmo, Xiao Huiming, Liang Jifu, and Dong Yueqi. Xianming eventually became a monk and was named Faxiang. This is recorded in the Zhu Lin (Jewel Forest), Volume Fifty-Two.

    齐王氏，名四娘，永明三年病死，下尸在地，为庄饰者，觉其心暖，故未殡殓。经二宿，肌体稍温。气息渐还，俄而能言。自说：有二人录其将去，至一大门有一沙门，踞胡床坐。见之甚惊，问：何故来？乃骂此二人云：“汝误录人来，各鞭四十余，此四娘女郎可去。答曰：“向来恍恍，不知道路，请人示津。”沙门即命一人力送之行，少地，见其先死奴子倚高楼上，惊问：“四娘那忽至此？欲见新妇不？”答：“不知处。

    161

    The Lady of the Qi family, named Si Niang, died in the third year of the Yongming era. Her body was found lying on the ground, and the person preparing it for burial noticed that her heart was warm, so she had not yet been buried. After two nights, her body began to warm up, and her breath gradually returned. Soon, she was able to speak. She began to speak for herself, saying that two people had taken her away. They arrived at a large gate where a monk was sitting on a trapeze-like seat. The monk was very surprised to see her and asked why she was there. The monk then scolded the two people, saying, "You have made a mistake by taking her. Each of you shall be whipped more than forty times. This girl can go." The two people responded that they were confused and did not know the way, asking for guidance. The monk then ordered one person to escort her. After a short distance, she saw a servant who had died before her, leaning against a high building. She was surprised and asked why she was there, and whether she wanted to see her new wife.

    ”唤奴自送，奴云：“不得奉送，四娘但去，前路应相值也。”投一马鞭与之，曰：“谨执此鞭，自知行路。”可行数里，便见新妇，即四娘之?也，正被苦?，四体碜缚，如○鹅鸭法，县于路侧，相见悲号。新妇自说：生时作罪，今贻此楚毒，欲屈手搏颊，求乞哀助，而手被挛格，不得至颊。又闻左右受苦之声，而不睹形。四娘问：“此为何声？”答曰：“此是无行众僧，破斋犯戒，获此苦报，呼叫声也。”于是?路而归，须臾至家。见其尸骸，意甚憎恶，不复愿还；不觉有人排其踣着，乃得就身而稍稣活。其人今休然尚存。珠林九十一

    A servant was called to accompany, but the servant said, "I cannot accompany you, Lady Four, just go, you will meet on the way ahead." After walking several miles, she saw a young wife, who was Four Lady's daughter-in-law, suffering greatly, her four limbs tightly bound, hung by the roadside, and they met with sorrowful cries. The young wife said, "In life, I committed sins, now I am receiving this suffering, I want to hit my cheek with my hand, begging for mercy and help, but my hands are restrained, I cannot reach my cheek." She also heard sounds of suffering around her, but could not see the forms. Four Lady asked, "What is this sound?"     前齐永明中，扬都高座寺释慧进者，少雄勇游侠，年四十，忽悟非常，因出家。蔬食布衣，誓诵法华，用心劳苦，执卷便病。乃发愿造百部，以悔先障。始聚得一千六百文，贼来索物，进示经钱，贼惭而退。尔后遂成百部，故病亦愈。诵经既度，情愿又满，回此诵业，愿生安养。闻空中告曰：“汝愿已足，必得往生。”无病而卒，八十余矣。珠林九十五

    Explanation

    163

    During the Yongming period of the Southern Qi Dynasty, in Yangzhou, at the Gaozuo Temple, there was a monk named Shihuijin. When he was young, he was brave and adventurous. At the age of forty, he suddenly had a profound realization and decided to become a monk. He lived a simple and ascetic life, eating vegetables and wearing coarse clothing, and vowed to recite the Lotus Sutra. His efforts were arduous, and he often fell ill while reading or reciting the scriptures. He then made a vow to create a hundred copies of the text to atone for past obstacles. Initially, he collected one thousand six hundred coins. Bandits came to demand things, and the monk showed them the money he had collected for the scriptures. The bandits were ashamed and left. After this, he completed the hundred copies, and his illness was cured. After finishing the recitation of the scriptures, his wishes were fulfilled. He redirected his recitation efforts to wish for rebirth in the Pure Land. He heard a voice from the air saying, "Your wishes are fulfilled, and you will definitely be reborn." He died without illness, over eighty years old. This story is recorded in the "Jade Forest" (珠林) volume 95.

    沙门安法开者，北人也，尝见吴公，长三尺，自屋堕地，旋回而去。御览九百四十六
    　　元嘉八年蒲阪城中大灾火，里中小屋虽焚，而于煨烬下得金经，纸素如故。苏易简文房四谱四
    　　晋世有竺长舒者，本天竺人，专心诵观世音经为业，后居吴中。于时邑内遭火，屋宇连栋，甍檐相接，火至皆焚，无能为救。长舒家正在下风，分意烧毁，一心唤观世音。欲至舒家，风回火灭，竟家获免。合县惊异，叹其有神。时有凶恶少年，怪其老胡，有何灵应，火烧不然？到后夜风急，少年以火投屋，四投皆灭，年少嗟感，至明，乃叩头首过。舒云：“我无神力，常以观世音为业，每有事恒得免脱也。”辩正论八注

    Explanation

    164

    A Buddhist monk named An Fakai, from the north, once saw a figure known as Wu Gong, who was three feet tall. The figure fell from a house to the ground and then turned around and left. This account is found in Taiping Guangji, volume 946.

    In the eighth year of the Yuanjia era (431 AD), there was a great fire in Puzhou city. Although the small houses in the village were burned, a golden sutra was found beneath the ashes, and the paper remained as before. This is recorded in the fourth chapter of Wenfang Sishu by Su Yijian.

    During the Jin dynasty, there was a man named Zhu Changshu, originally from India, who devoted himself to reciting the Guanyin Sutra as his profession. He later settled in Wu. At that time, the town suffered a fire, and the houses, connected in rows with their roofs touching, were all burned, with no one able to stop it. Zhu Changshu's family was located downwind, and he thought they would be burned. He called out to Guanyin with all his heart. Just as the fire was about to reach his house, the wind changed, the fire was extinguished, and his entire family was saved. The whole county was amazed and admired his divine power. At that time, there was a wicked young man who wondered about the old foreigner, thinking he had some miraculous response, as the fire did not burn him. On the following night, when the wind was strong, the young man threw fire at Zhu Changshu's house, but all four attempts failed. The young man was moved and, until dawn, knelt and apologized. Zhu Changshu said, "I have no divine power. I always recite the Guanyin Sutra as my profession, and whenever there is trouble, I always escape." This is recorded in the eighth chapter of Bianzheng Lun (辨正论).

    晋世沙门僧洪住京师瓦官寺，当义熙十二年时，官禁镕铸，洪既发心铸丈六金像：“像若圆满，我死无恨。”便即偷铸，铸竟，像犹有模，所司收洪，禁在相府，锁械甚严。心念观世音，日诵百遍，便梦所铸金像往狱，手摩头曰：无虑。”其像胸前一尺许铜色燋沸。当洪禁日，感得国家牛马，不肯人栏，时以为怪。旬日敕至彭城洪因放免像即破模自现。同上
    　　史俊有学识，奉道而慢佛，常语人云：“佛是小神，不足事耳。”每见尊像，恒轻诮之，后因病脚挛，种种祈福，都无效验，其友人赵文谓曰：“经道福中，佛福第一，可试造观音像。”俊以病急，如言灌像，像成梦观音，遂差。辩正论八注云出宣验冥祥等记
    　　陈玄范妻张氏，精心奉佛，恒愿自作一金像，终身供养，有愿皆从。专心日久，忽有观音金像，连光五尺，见高座上。辩正论八注云出宣验冥祥等记

    Explanation

    165

    During the Jin Dynasty, the Buddhist monk Hong resided at the Wuguan Temple in the capital. In the twelfth year of the Yixi era, the government had banned metal casting. Hong, having resolved to cast a golden image of the Buddha measuring sixteen chi, vowed, "If the image is completed, I will have no regrets even if I die." He secretly began the casting, but when it was finished, the image still had a mold. The authorities apprehended him, and he was imprisoned in the Chancellor's office with strict shackles. In his heart, he meditated on Guanyin and recited his name a hundred times daily. One night, he dreamed that the golden image he had cast came to him in prison, placing his hand on his head and saying, "Do not worry." The image's chest bore a patch of copper that appeared to be boiling. During Hong's imprisonment, it was said that national cattle and horses refused to enter their pens, which was considered a strange omen. After ten days, an imperial decree arrived in Pengcheng, leading to Hong's release. At that moment, the image broke free from its mold and appeared on its own.

    Shi Jun, a man of learning who respected Daoism but was indifferent to Buddhism, often told others, "Buddha is a minor deity, not worth serving." Whenever he saw revered Buddha images, he would mock them. Later, due to a leg ailment, he prayed for blessings in various ways, but none worked. His friend Zhao Wen advised him, "Among all forms of blessings, the blessings of Buddhism are the greatest. You might try making an image of Guanyin." Urged by his illness, Shi Jun cast the image as advised. When the image was completed, he dreamed of Guanyin, and his condition improved. This account is cited in the Dian Zheng Lun (Eight Annotations) from Xuan Yan Ming Xiang (Records of Manifestations and Auspicious Signs).

    Chen Xuanfan's wife, Zhang, devotedly served Buddhism. She always wished to make a golden image herself, to be worshipped for life. All her wishes were fulfilled. After long and dedicated practice, she suddenly saw a golden image of Guanyin, five feet tall with radiating light, appearing on a high seat. This account is also cited in the Dian Zheng Lun (Eight Annotations) from Xuan Yan Ming Xiang (Records of Manifestations and Auspicious Signs).
